Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Ruling on Using a Sutra in Prayer
Hashiya commentary on the sutra ruling with proofs and inter-madhhab comparison.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sutra, distinguish between makruh tanzih and wajib, and cite the dalil for the recommended practice.

Core Idea
The sutra is sunnah mu'akkadah; omitting it when passing is expected is makruh tanzih — not sinful but best to use.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi refines the ruling on the sutra (screen) in prayer. While the Prophetic command appears imperative, the Hanafi school interprets it as recommendation. The hashya clarifies the degree of dislike and the conditions under which omitting the sutra is acceptable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of omitting to place a sutra when one expects people to pass in front. The ruling is makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful).
This ruling applies only when passing is expected; otherwise omission is permissible.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutra and not let anyone pass in front of him.' This is a command from the Prophet.
The hadith is from authentic sources like Muslim and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The Hanafi school holds that the imperative form (li-yusalli ila sutra) indicates recommendation (nadb) here, not obligation, because the command is for the benefit of focus and to prevent sin for the passerby. The context and other evidences (like permissibility when no one passes) show it is not wajib.
This interpretation is based on the principle that a command can be turned from wujub to nadb if there is a qarina (indication).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal considers the sutra obligatory due to the apparent imperative. He also cites reports from Umar and Ibn Mas'ud emphasizing its importance.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both positions are within the valid scope of ijtihad.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position (makruh tanzih for omission when passing expected) is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi). It is based on the principle that absent a clear qarina of obligation, the command is for recommendation. The practical difference is that the prayer remains valid even without a sutra, though it is better to use one.
The tarjih is supported by later Hanafi authorities like al-Tahtawi and al-Haskafi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(و) يكره (ترك اتخاذ سترة في محل يظن المرور فيه بين يدي المصلي) لقوله : إذا صلى أحدكم فليصل إلى سترة ولا يدع أحداً يمر بين يديه، وسواء كان في الصحراء أو غيرها احترازاً عن وقوع المار في الإثم ولذا عقبناه ببيانها فقلنا . في اتخاذ السترة ودفع المار بين يدي المصلي إذا ظن أي مريد الصلاة (مروره) أي المار (يستحب له أي مريد الصلاة (أن يغرز سترة) لما روينا لقوله ليستتر أحدكم ولو بسهم وأن تكون طول ذراع فصاعداً) لأنه سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن سترة المصلي فقال مثل مؤخرة الرجل بضم الميم، وهمزة ساكنة وكسر الخاء المعجمة والعود الذي في آخر الرحل يحاذي رأس الراكب على البعير، وتشديد الخاء قوله: ( ويكره ترك اتخاذ سترة) أي تنزيهاً كما أفاده في البدائع. قوله: (في محل يظن المرور فيه قال في التنوير وشرحه ولو عدم المرور جاز تركها، وفعلها أولى اهـ . قوله : (ولذا عقبناه) أي لما ذكر من الحديث الآمر بها ومن كراهة تركها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. فصل في اتخاذ السترة بالضم هي قوله : (إذا ظن الخ) الأولى فعلها مطلقاً لأن فيها كف بصره عما وراءها، وجمع خاطره بربط الخيال بها كي لا ينتشر وقدمناه قوله : (يستحب له أن يغرز سترة وأوجبه الإمام أحمد لظاهر الأمر، ولما ورد عن عمر : لو علم المصلي ما ينقص من صلاته ما صلى إلا إلى شيء يستره من الناس، وعن ابن مسعود أنه ليقطع نصف صلاة المرء المرور بين يديه، وتصبح بالسترة المغصوبة عندنا قوله : (لما أحمد تبطل صلاته ومثله لصلاة في الثوب المغصوب عنده . وعند روينا) من الحديث المذكور قبيل الفصل. قوله : (طول) ذراع) في الاعتداد بالأقل خلاف، ولا خلاف في الأكثر ، وشمل كل ما انتصب كإنسان قائم أو قاعد أو دابة كما في القهستاني والحلبي وجوز في القنية بظهر الرجل، ومنع بوجهه، وتردد في جنبه، ومنع بالمرأة غير المحرم، واختلف في المحارم، ولا يستتر بنائم ومجنون ومأبون في دبره وكافر كما في في الأصل ما يستتر به مطلقاً ثم غلب على ما ينصب قدام المصلى قهستاني.
(And) it is disliked (to omit taking a sutra in a place where one expects a passerby to pass in front of the praying person) because of his saying: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutra and not let anyone pass between him.' And it is the same whether in the desert or elsewhere, as a precaution against the passerby falling into sin. And therefore we have followed it with its explanation and said: Regarding taking a sutra and repelling the passerby in front of the praying person: when he expects – i.e., the one intending prayer (his passing) i.e., the passerby, (it is recommended for him, i.e., the one intending prayer, to plant a sutra) because of what we have narrated from his saying: 'Let one of you take a screen even if with an arrow.' And that its length should be a cubit or more because the Messenger of Allah ﷺ was asked about the sutra of the praying person and he said: 'Like the back of the saddle' – with dammah on the meem, a silent hamzah, and kasrah on the kha' – and the stick at the back of the saddle aligning with the head of the rider on the camel, and with tashdeed on the kha'. His saying: (And it is disliked to omit taking a sutra) i.e., as a tanzih dislike as expounded in al-Bada'i'. His saying: (in a place where he expects passing) He said in al-Tanwir and its commentary: And if there is no passing, it is permissible to omit it, but doing it is better. End. His saying: (and therefore we followed it) i.e., because of what was mentioned of the hadith commanding it and the dislike of omitting it. And Allah Most High knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent. Chapter on taking a sutra – with dammah on the seen, it is: His saying: (when he expects, etc.) – It is better to do it absolutely because it contains restraining the gaze from what is beyond it and concentrating the mind by tying the imagination to it so that it does not wander, as we have mentioned previously. His saying: (it is recommended for him to plant a sutra) – Imam Ahmad made it obligatory due to the apparent command, and because of what was reported from Umar: 'If the praying person knew what is lost from his prayer, he would not pray except towards something that screens him from people.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'The passing of a person in front of a praying person cuts half of his prayer.' And it is valid with a usurped sutra according to us. His saying: (for the hadith we narrated) from the hadith mentioned just before this chapter. His saying: (length of a cubit) – there is difference regarding considering less, and no difference regarding more. And it includes everything that stands erect, like a standing person, a sitting person, or an animal, as in al-Qahistani and al-Halabi. And it is permitted in al-Qunyah with the back of a man, and prohibited with his face, and there is hesitation regarding his side. And it is prohibited with a non-mahram woman, and there is difference regarding mahrams. And one is not screened by a sleeping person, a mad person, a passive homosexual in his rear, or a disbeliever, as in al-Asl. 'What is used as a screen' absolutely, then it became predominant for what is erected in front of the praying person – Qahistani.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage is a hashya on the matn of Maraqi al-Falah regarding the sutra (screen) in prayer. The matn states that it is disliked (makruh) to omit taking a sutra when one expects people to pass in front. The hashya clarifies that this dislike is tanzihi (not sinful) and that the Prophetic command is for recommendation, not obligation. The evidence is the hadith: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutra and not let anyone pass in front.' The hashya also discusses the dimensions: the sutra should be at least a cubit in height, and can be any upright object. The hashya addresses various issues: using a usurped sutra is valid (though sinful), what counts as a sutra (e.g., a standing person, animal, but not a sleeping person or mad person), and the difference between mahram and non-mahram women as screens. It also mentions that Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal considered the sutra obligatory, but the Hanafi position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah (recommended), and omitting it when passing is expected is makruh tanzih. The passage also emphasizes the wisdom behind the sutra: it helps focus the mind and prevents sin for the passerby.

Key Terms
سترة (sutra): An object placed in front of a praying person to prevent people from passing directly in front, serving as a screen.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyyah): Disliked but not sinful; omitting a sunnah without punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hashiya, what is the ruling on using a sutra that is stolen (مغصوبة)?
A) The prayer is invalid because the object is unlawful
B) The prayer is valid but the use is sinful
C) The prayer is invalid only if the owner objects
D) It is not permissible to use any sutra

Key Takeaway
The sutra is sunnah; omitting it when passing is expected is makruh tanzih, and it is valid even if the sutra is usurped.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Sutra in Prayer: Rulings and the Line Dispute
Expounds rulings and etiquettes of the sutra in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on taking a sutra in prayer and apply the Hanafi position on drawing a line as a sutra.

Core Idea
Taking a sutra is sunnah; drawing a line is permitted by later Hanafis despite early opposition.

The sutra is a screen placed in front of the worshipper to aid concentration and prevent passers-by from cutting the prayer. This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the ruling, the recommended size, and the disputed rule about drawing a line when no object is available. Understanding these details helps you practice the recommended etiquettes of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the hukm level for taking a sutra: it is sunnah (mustahabb). Leaving it is makruh tanzihi when passing is expected.
The command in the hadith is interpreted as recommendation, not obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutra and not let anyone pass in front of him.'
This is a hadith ahad, so it gives zanni thubut and dalala.
3
Analyse the intra-school difference
Early Hanafis (e.g., author of al-Hidayah) forbade drawing a line; later scholars (e.g., al-Kamal) permitted it. Understand the reasoning and why the later view is mufta bihi.
The later view relies on authenticated hadith and the purpose of concentration.
4
Determine practical application
What qualifies as a sutra? Minimum size: a cubit height and finger thickness (some say no minimum). Placement: on one side, not directly in front. What cannot be used? Sleeper, madman, non-mahram woman, large rivers, etc.
The sutra should be upright and stable.
5
Apply to everyday scenarios
In a mosque corridor, place a bag or chair. In an open field, draw a line if nothing else is available. If no one passes, it is permissible to omit, but doing it is better.
The purpose is to collect the mind and prevent distraction.

Source Text

(و) يكره (ترك اتخاذ سترة في محل يظن المرور فيه بين يدي المصلي) لقوله : إذا صلى أحدكم فليصل إلى سترة ولا يدع أحداً . يمر بين يديه، وسواء كان في الصحراء أو غيرها احترازاً عن وقوع المار في الإثم ولذا عقبناه ببيانها فقلنا . في اتخاذ السترة ودفع المار بين يدي المصلي إذا ظن أي مريد الصلاة (مروره) أي المار (يستحب له أي مريد الصلاة (أن يغرز سترة) لما روينا لقوله ليستتر أحدكم ولو بسهم وأن تكون طول ذراع فصاعداً) لأنه سئل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم عن سترة المصلي فقال مثل مؤخرة الرجل بضم الميم، وهمزة ساكنة وكسر الخاء المعجمة والعود الذي في آخر الرحل يحاذي رأس الراكب على البعير، وتشديد الخاء قوله: ( ويكره ترك اتخاذ سترة) أي تنزيهاً كما أفاده في البدائع. قوله: (في محل يظن المرور فيه قال في التنوير وشرحه ولو عدم المرور جاز تركها، وفعلها أولى اهـ . قوله : (ولذا عقبناه) أي لما ذكر من الحديث الآمر بها ومن كراهة تركها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم. ، فصل في اتخاذ السترة بالضم هي قوله : (إذا ظن الخ) الأولى فعلها مطلقاً لأن فيها كف . بصره عما وراءها، وجمع خاطره بربط الخيال بها كي لا ينتشر وقدمناه قوله : (يستحب له أن يغرز سترة وأوجبه الإمام أحمد لظاهر الأمر، ولما ورد عن عمر : لو علم المصلي ما ينقص من صلاته ما صلى إلا إلى شيء يستره من الناس، وعن ابن مسعود أنه ليقطع نصف صلاة المرء المرور بين يديه، وتصبح بالسترة المغصوبة عندنا قوله : (لما أحمد تبطل صلاته ومثله لصلاة في الثوب المغصوب عنده . وعند روينا) من الحديث المذكور قبيل الفصل. قوله : (طول) ذراع) في الاعتداد بالأقل خلاف، ولا خلاف في الأكثر ، وشمل كل ما انتصب كإنسان قائم أو قاعد أو دابة كما في القهستاني والحلبي وجوز في القنية بظهر الرجل، ومنع بوجهه، وتردد في جنبه، ومنع بالمرأة غير المحرم، واختلف في المحارم، ولا يستتر بنائم ومجنون ومأبون في دبره وكافر كما في في الأصل ما يستتر به مطلقاً ثم غلب على ما ينصب قدام المصلى قهستاني. خطأ، وفسرت بأنها ذراع فما فوقه ( في غلظ الأصبع ) وذلك أدناه لأن ما دونه ربما لا يظهر للناظر فلا يحصل المقصود منها والسنة أن يقرب منها لقول النبي : إذا صلى أحدكم إلى سترة فليدن منها لا يقطع الشيطان عليه صلاته ويجعلها على) جهة (أحد حاجبيه ولا يصمد إليها صمداً) لما المقداد روي عن الله عنه أنه قال: ما رأيت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي إلى عمود ولا شجرة إلا جعله على حاجبه الأيمن أو الأيسر لا . يصمد صمداً ا أي لا يقابله مستوياً مستقيماً، بل كان يميل عنه (وإن لم يجد ما ينصبه) منع جماعة من المتقدمين الخط، وأجازه المتأخرون لأن السنة أولى بالاتباع لما روي في السنن عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال : إن لم يكن . معه عصا (فليخط خطا) فيظهر في الجملة إذ المقصود جمع الخاطر بربط الخيال كي لا ينتشر ويجعله إما طولاً بمنزلة الخشبة المغروزة أمامه، وإما كما قالوا أيضاً يجعله (بالعرض مثل الهلال وإذا كانت الأرض صلبة يلقي ما معه طولاً كأنه غرز ثم سقط من العيني على البخاري قوله وفسرت بأنها ذراع روى أصحاب السنن عن عطاء قال : آخرة الرحل ذراع فما فوقه كذا في غاية البيان. قوله : ( في غلظ الأصبع خلاف المذهب، فلا حد لما روى الحاكم عن أبي هريرة مرفوعاً يجزىء من السترة قدر مؤخرة الرحل، ولو بدقة شعرة كذا في البحر عن البدائع، وفي القهستاني والبئر والنهر والحوض الصغيرات ليست بسترة في الأصح، والكبيرات منها كالطريق أهـ أي، وهي لا تكون سترة لأنها مظنة المرور، وفي العيني على البخاري وفي غريب الروايات النهر الكبير ليس بسترة كالطريق وكذا الحوض الكبير اهـ . قوله : (وذلك أدناه أي أدنى ما يغرز قوله: (والسنة أن يقرب منها قال ابن أمير حاج، والنسة في ذلك أن لا يزيد ما بينها وبينه على ثلاثة أذرع اهـ والظاهر اعتبار هذا القدر قدمه . قوله : (لا يقطع) مجزوم في جواب شرط مقدر تقديره فإن يدن منها لا يقطع الشيطان عليه الصلاة، ووجه القطع أنه إذا بعد منها يظن المار أنه لا سترة له فيمر داخلها فيدفعه، وربما كان الدفع بعمل كثير فتفسد الصلاة قوله : ( ويجعلها على جهة أحد حاجبيه) والأيمن أفضل قهستاني قوله: (منع جماعة من المتقدمين الخط منهم صاحب الهداية قوله: (وأجازه المتأخرون) ورجحه الكمال لورود الأثر، والحديث وإن جعله في البدائع . شاذاً، وضعفه النووي فقد تعقب بتصحيح الإمام أحمد وابن حبان، وغيرهما له ولو سلم أنه غير مفيد، فلا ضرر فيه مع ما فيه من العمل الكثير بالحديث الذي يجوز العمل به في مثله كما في الشرح قوله : (لما روى) الأولى أن يقول وهي ما روي الخ. قوله : (فيظهر الخ الأولى أن يقول فيفيد في الجملة قوله : ( بربط (الخيال) أي خيال المصلي أي قوته المخيلة أي فيقل فكره بخلاف ما إذا عدمت فيتبع البصر فيكثر الفكر قوله : (بمنزلة الخشبة المغروزة) فيصير شبه ظل السترة . قوله: (مثل الهلال) وقيل مدور شبه المحراب كما في القهستاني وفي شرح المشكاة للمنلا على وقاس الأئمة على الخط المصلى كسجادة مفروشة، وهو قياس أولى لأن المصلي أبلغ في دفع
And it is disliked to omit taking a sutra in a place where passing in front of the worshipper is expected, due to his (peace be upon him) saying: 'When one of you prays, let him pray towards a sutra and not let anyone pass in front of him.' Whether in the desert or elsewhere, to avoid the passer falling into sin. Therefore we followed it with its explanation, saying: Regarding taking a sutra and repelling the passer in front of the worshipper, when he (the intending worshipper) expects passing (of the passer), it is recommended for him (the intending worshipper) to plant a sutra, because of what we narrated from his saying: 'Let one of you screen himself even with an arrow.' And that it be a cubit or more, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked about the sutra of the worshipper and he said: 'Like the back of the saddle' (with damm of the meem, sukoon of the hamza, and kasr of the khaa), which is the wood at the back of the saddle facing the rider's head on the camel. The commentator said: 'And it is disliked to omit taking a sutra' i.e., as a tanzihi dislike, as indicated in al-Bada'i. He said: 'In a place where passing is expected.' In al-Tanwir and its commentary: 'Even if there is no passer, it is permissible to omit it, but doing it is better.' He said: 'Therefore we followed it' i.e., because of the hadith commanding it and the dislike of omitting it. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness. Then a section on taking the sutra (with damm): it is said: 'When he expects' etc. The preferable is to do it absolutely, because it restrains his sight from what is beyond it and collects his mind by tying his imagination to it so that it does not wander. We have preceded it. He said: 'It is recommended for him to plant a sutra, and Imam Ahmad made it obligatory due to the apparent command, and because of what was reported from Umar: 'If the worshipper knew what diminishes from his prayer, he would not pray except towards something that screens him from people.' And from Ibn Mas'ud: 'Passing in front of a person cuts half of his prayer.' And the prayer is valid with a usurped sutra according to us. He said: 'Ahmad would invalidate it, similar to prayer in a usurped garment according to him.' And 'according to us' from the hadith mentioned before the section. He said: 'Length of a cubit' there is disagreement regarding the minimum, no disagreement about the maximum. And it includes everything that stands upright, like a standing or sitting person or an animal, as in al-Qahistani and al-Halabi. In al-Qunyah, he permitted the back of a man, prohibited his face, and hesitated about his side. He also prohibited a non-mahram woman, and there is disagreement about mahrams. One cannot take as sutra a sleeper, a madman, a hermaphrodite from behind, or a disbeliever, as in al-Qahistani. The original meaning is anything used as a screen, then it became predominant for what is placed in front of the worshipper. It is an error, and it was interpreted as a cubit or more (in thickness of a finger), and that is the minimum because less than that may not be visible to the observer, so the purpose is not achieved. And the sunnah is to be near it, due to the Prophet's (peace be upon him) saying: 'When one of you prays towards a sutra, let him come close to it, lest the devil cut off his prayer.' And he should place it on the side of one of his eyebrows and not directly face it, because al-Miqdad narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that he never prayed towards a pillar or tree except he placed it on his right or left eyebrow, not directly facing it. That is, he did not oppose it straight on, but leaned away from it. And if he does not find anything to set up, a group of early scholars forbade drawing a line, but later scholars permitted it, because the sunnah is more worthy of being followed, due to what is reported in the Sunan from the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'If he does not have a stick, let him draw a line.' So it suffices somewhat, since the purpose is to collect the mind by tying the imagination so that it does not wander. He should make it either lengthwise like a planted piece of wood in front of him, or as they also said, make it widthwise like a crescent. And if the ground is hard, he should throw what he has lengthwise as if it was planted then fell. From al-Ayni on al-Bukhari: he said 'interpreted as a cubit or more' - the authors of the Sunan narrated from Ata: 'The back of the saddle is a cubit or more.' Similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan. He said: 'In thickness of a finger' is against the madhhab; there is no limit, because al-Hakim narrated from Abu Hurayra marfu': 'A sutra suffices the size of the back of the saddle, even if as fine as a hair.' Similarly in al-Bahr from al-Bada'i. In al-Qahistani: wells, rivers, and small ponds are not sutras according to the most correct view, and large ones are like a road. That is, they do not count as sutras because they are places where passing is expected. In al-Ayni on al-Bukhari and in Ghariq al-Riwayat: a large river is not a sutra, like a road, and similarly a large pond. He said: 'And that is the minimum' i.e., the minimum to plant. He said: 'And the sunnah is to be near it' - Ibn Amir Haj said: 'The sunnah in that is that the distance between it and him should not exceed three cubits.' And apparently this measure is considered. He said: 'It does not cut' is jussive as the answer to an implied conditional, i.e., if he draws near, the devil does not cut off his prayer. The reason for cutting is that if he is far, the passer thinks he has no sutra, so he passes within it, thus he pushes him, and perhaps the pushing involves much action, invalidating the prayer. He said: 'And he should place it on the side of one of his eyebrows' - the right is better. He said: 'A group of early scholars forbade the line, among them the author of al-Hidaya. He said: 'And later scholars permitted it, and al-Kamal preferred it due to the report. Even though al-Bada'i considered the hadith anomalous and al-Nawawi weakened it, it is refuted by the authentication of Imam Ahmad and Ibn Hibban and others. Even if it is not beneficial, there is no harm in it, especially with the much practice of acting on the hadith, which is permissible in such matters as in the sharh. He said: 'It is preferable to say 'and what is reported' etc. He said: 'It becomes apparent' etc. It is preferable to say 'it benefits somewhat.' He said: 'By tying the imagination' i.e., the worshipper's imagination, i.e., his imaginative faculty, i.e., his thought is reduced, unlike when it is absent, then his sight follows and his thought increases. He said: 'Like a planted piece of wood' so it becomes like the shadow of the sutra. He said: 'Like a crescent' and it was said: rounded like a mihrab, as in al-Qahistani. In Sharh al-Mishkat for al-Mulla Ali, the imams analogized the line to a prayer mat spread out, and it is a more appropriate analogy because the worshipper is more effective in repelling.
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah deals with the rulings and etiquettes of the sutra (an object placed in front of the worshipper) during prayer. The author begins by stating that it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) to omit taking a sutra in a place where one expects someone to pass in front of him, based on the hadith commanding the sutra. Even if no one passes, it is better to have one. Then, the section (fasl) on the sutra details that it is mustahabb (recommended) to plant a sutra, and the minimum recommended size is a cubit (about 45 cm) and the thickness of a finger, though some scholars say no minimum. The sutra should be placed on the right or left eyebrow, not directly in front, following the Prophet's practice. If no object is available, the later Hanafi scholars permit drawing a line on the ground, unlike early scholars like the author of al-Hidayah, who forbade it. This permissibility is based on authentic hadith. Additionally, the text discusses what can serve as a sutra: a standing person (back only), an animal, etc., and what cannot: a sleeper, a mad person, a non-mahram woman in front, and large rivers or ponds that are places of passing. The essential point is that the sutra helps concentrate the mind and prevents the devil from cutting the prayer. The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that drawing a line is allowed when no sutra is found.

Key Terms
سترة (sutra): An object placed in front of the worshipper to screen him from passers-by and aid concentration.
خط (khatt): A line drawn on the ground to serve as a sutra when no object is available.
مؤخرة الرجل (mu'akhkharat al-rajul): The back of the saddle, used as a measure for the minimum size of a sutra (approximately a cubit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on drawing a line as a sutra when no object is available?
A) It is prohibited by all Hanafi scholars.
B) It is permissible according to later Hanafi scholars.
C) It is wajib according to the Hanafi school.
D) It is only allowed if the line is a cubit long.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling on the sutra: it is sunnah to have one, and if none is available, drawing a line is permissible per the later preferred view.

Ruling on Driving Away a Passerby During Prayer
Ruling on repelling a passerby with gesture or tasbeeh

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended and permissible methods of repelling a passerby during prayer and identify the Hanafi ruling on combining gestures and tasbeeh.

Core Idea
The default is tranquility; repelling is a license, not a duty.

This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi explains the balance between maintaining the tranquility of prayer and addressing an interruption. You will learn when and how a worshipper may gesture, recite, or use tasbeeh to repel a passerby, and why the recommended action is to refrain.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Determine what the text recommends as the ideal course of action when a passerby approaches during prayer. The passage states that the recommended (mustahabb) is to refrain from driving away the passerby because prayer is built on stillness and tranquility.
The default is not to repel; the license is an exception.
2
Recognize the license (rukhsa)
Understand that the command to repel in the hadith is interpreted as a license (rukhsah), not an obligation (wajib). The text compares it to the command to kill a snake or scorpion during prayer, which is also a license for necessity.
The command 'فليسبح' is permissive, not imperative.
3
List the permitted methods
Identify the specific ways a worshipper may repel a passerby: gesture (head, eye, hand), saying tasbeeh (Subhanallah) aloud, and for men, raising the voice in recitation. For women, gesture or clapping (striking back of right fingers on left palm) is permitted, but not raising the voice.
The Prophet gestured to the children of Umm Salama, setting a precedent.
4
Understand the disliked combination
Note that combining both gesture and tasbeeh is makruh (disliked) because one method is sufficient. The principle is to minimize extra movements and utterances that disturb the prayer's tranquility.
The ruling applies only when one method effectively achieves the purpose.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا اتخذها أو لم يتخذ كان المستحب ترك دفع المار لأن مبنى الصلاة على السكون والأمر بالدرء في الحديث لبيان الرخصة كالأمر بقتل الأسودين في الصلاة (و) لذا (رخص دفعه) أي المار (بالإشارة) بالرأس أو العين أو غيرهما كما فعل النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بولدي أم سلمة (أو) دفعه (بالتسبيح) لقوله : إذا نابت أحدكم نائبة في الصلاة فليسبح» (وكره الجمع بينهما) أي بين الإشارة، والتسبيح لأن بأحدهما كفاية (ويدفعه) الرجل (برفع الصو بالقراءة) ولو بزيادة على جهره الأصلي وتدفعه بالإشارة أو التصفيق بظهر أصابع يدها اليمنى على صفحة كف اليسرى لأن لهن التصفيق ولا ترفع صوتها بالقراءة والتسبيح (لأنه فتنة) فلا يطلب
And whether he takes a sutrah or not, the recommended thing is to refrain from driving away the passerby, because prayer is based on tranquility, and the command to repel in the hadith is to indicate a license (rukhsah), like the command to kill the two black things (snake and scorpion) during prayer. Therefore, it is permitted to repel him (the passerby) by gesture, with the head, eye, or other, as the Prophet did with the two children of Umm Salama, or by tasbeeh (saying Subhanallah), due to his saying: 'If something happens to one of you during prayer, let him say Subhanallah.' And it is disliked to combine both (gesture and tasbeeh) because one is sufficient. A man may repel him by raising his voice in recitation, even if increasing over his original loudness. And a woman repels him by gesture or by clapping with the back of the fingers of her right hand on the palm of her left, because for them clapping is prescribed, and she does not raise her voice in recitation or tasbeeh because it is a fitna (temptation).
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya addresses the ruling on driving away a passerby who walks in front of a person during prayer. The commentator begins by stating that the recommended (mustahabb) course is not to drive away the passerby at all, because prayer is built on stillness and tranquility. However, there is a license (rukhsah) to repel, indicated by a hadith where the Prophet allowed repelling during prayer, similar to the command to kill a snake or scorpion (which would otherwise harm the worshipper). The license is not an obligation but a concession. The permitted methods include: (1) gesture with the head, eye, or hand, as the Prophet gestured to the children of Umm Salama to stop; (2) saying tasbeeh (Subhanallah) aloud, based on the hadith: 'If something happens to one of you during prayer, let him say Subhanallah.' It is disliked (makruh) to combine both gesture and tasbeeh, since one is sufficient for the purpose. For a man, he may also repel by raising his voice in recitation, even if that means increasing loudness beyond his normal jahr in audible prayers. For a woman, she repels by gesture or by clapping: striking the back of her right fingers on the palm of her left hand, because women are instructed to clap instead of speaking in prayer. She should not raise her voice in recitation or tasbeeh because her voice may be a source of fitna (temptation). The commentator emphasizes that these are licenses, not requirements, and the original recommendation is to avoid driving away the passerby.

Key Terms
الدفع (al-daf'): Repelling a passerby who crosses in front of the worshipper during prayer.
التسبيح (al-tasbeeh): Saying 'Subhanallah' aloud to alert others during prayer.
التصفيق (al-tasfiq): Clapping by a woman during prayer to alert the imam or indicate something, done by striking the back of the right fingers on the palm of the left.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) By raising her voice in recitation
B) By saying 'Subhanallah' loudly
C) By clapping with the back of her right fingers on her left palm
D) By stepping back

Key Takeaway
Repelling a passerby is a permitted license, but the ideal in prayer is stillness and tranquility.

Ruling on the Person Praying Preventing the Passer-by
Critical refinement of the hadith on repelling the passer-by

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repelling a passer-by during prayer and explain why the permission to fight is abrogated.

Core Idea
The worshiper may push gently but must not fight; the hadith's permission to fight is abrogated.

This lesson addresses a common issue faced during prayer: someone passing in front of you. A well-known hadith commands the worshiper to fight the passer-by, but this ruling is not applied literally. The Hanafi school teaches that the command is abrogated, and only gentle repulsion is allowed. We will examine the evidence, the abrogation, and the practical consequences including liability if harm occurs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the hadith and its apparent meaning
Read the hadith cited in the passage: 'When one of you prays, do not let anyone pass in front of him; ward him off as much as possible; if he refuses, fight him, for he is a devil.' Note the imperative 'fight'.
This hadith is sahih but its ruling is abrogated.
2
Understand the interpretation (ta'wil) and abrogation
The commentator explains that fighting was permissible in early Islam when actions contrary to prayer were allowed, but this was abrogated by the later hadith 'Verily, in prayer there is occupation (with Allah).' So the permission to fight is no longer valid.
Abrogation (naskh) is accepted when clear evidence comes later.
3
State the current Hanafi ruling
The worshiper may signal, say tasbih, or push the passer-by gently once. If he does not stop, the worshiper must leave him and not fight. Walking from his place to repel is not allowed.
The mufta bihi is gentle push only; fighting invalidates the prayer.
4
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Imam Muhammad allowed forceful repulsion (al-mudafa'a bi 'unf), but the relied-upon position is the soft approach. The commentator sides with the majority.
This is a rare difference; the fatwa follows the prohibition of fighting.
5
Analyze the dispute on liability
If the passer-by dies from a permissible push, Hanafis say the blood-money is due from the worshiper's own wealth, while Shafi'is say it is unavenged. The Hanafi position is based on general liability for causing death.
Permissibility does not remove civil liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منهن الدرء به ولا يقاتل المصلي (المار) بين يديه وما ورد (به من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : «إذا كان أحداً أحدكم يصلي فلا يدع يمر بين يديه وليدرا ما استطاع فإن أبي فليقاتله إنما هو شيطان لأنه (مؤول بأنه كان جواز مقاتلته في ابتداء الإسلام (والعمل المنافي للصلاة (مباح) فيها إذ ذاك (وقد نسخ) بما قدمناه . فصل من الأفعال لا يكره له شد (الوسط) لما فيه من صون العورة والتشمير للعبادة حتى لو سبح فقط ، فهما بمعنى واحد، ولو سبحت وصفق لا تفسد وقد تركل السنة .در قوله : (والتسبيح) الواو بمعنى أو وهو كذلك في نسخ. قوله: (لأنه فتنة) قد أن الفتنة إنما تكون بما فيه تمطيط، وتبيين لا مطلق الصوت. قوله : ولا يقاتل المصلي الخ الحاصل إنه إذا قصد المرور بين يديه إن كان قريباً منه يمكنه مدافعته بدون مشي أشار إليه، أو لا ليرجع يسبح فإن لم يرجع دفعه مرة بلطف فإن لم يرجع ،تركه، ولا يقاتله وإن كان بعيداً عنه إن شاء أشار إليه وإن شاء وإذا مر بين يديه ما لا تؤثر فيه الإشارة كهرة دفعه برجله، أو الصقه إلى السترة كذا في العيني على البخاري وعزاه للمالكية وقواعدنا لا تأباه وفيه أيضاً، ولا يجوز له المشي من موضعه ليرد، وإنما يدافعه، ويرده من موضعه لأن مفسدة المشي أعظم من مروره بين يديه، وإنما أبيح له قدر ما يناله من موقفه، ولا ينتهي بذلك إلى ما يفسد صلاته فإنّ دفعه بما يجوز له فمات فلا إثم عليه بإتفاق العلماء، وهل تجب ديته، أو يكون هدراً فيه مذهبان للعلماء، والدية عليه في ماله كاملة، وقيل هي على العاقلة اهـ، وفي الدر عن الباقاني أنه يجب الضمان على مقتضى كتبنا، وهدر عند الشافعي .اهـ. قوله إنما هو (شيطان قال الخطابي : معناه أن الشيطان هو الذي حمله على ذلك، ويجوز أن يراد بالشيطان نفس المار لأن الشيطان هو المارد الخبيث من الأنس، ومن الجن. قوله : (مؤول بأنه الخ) وأوله الإمام محمد بالمدافعة بعنف، وأما حملها على ظاهر فغير ما عليه العامة قوله : (بما قدمناه من قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن في الصلاة لشغلا، والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
Among them is that he may ward off (the passer-by) and the person praying should not fight the (passer-by) who passes in front of him, and what is narrated of his statement, peace be upon him: 'When one of you prays, do not let anyone pass in front of him, and let him ward him off as much as he can. If he refuses, let him fight him, for he is a devil.' This is interpreted that fighting was permissible in early Islam, and actions that contravene prayer were permissible at that time, and this has been abrogated by what we have mentioned earlier. Section: Of actions, it is not disliked for him to tie his waist cloth because it protects his private parts and prepares for worship, even if he recites tasbih only, and they are synonymous, and if he recites tasbih and claps, the prayer is not invalidated, though he may leave the sunna. In the commentary on his statement 'and tasbih': the waw is in the sense of 'or', and so it is in some copies. Regarding his statement 'because it is a trial': the trial only occurs with that which involves stretching and making clear, not absolute sound. His statement: 'and the person praying should not fight etc.' The summary is: if someone intends to pass in front of him, if he is near and can repel him without walking, he signals to him. If not, he says tasbih so that he returns. If he does not return, he pushes him once gently. If he does not return, he leaves him and does not fight him. If he is far from him, he may signal to him if he wishes, or not. If something passes in front of him for which signals are ineffective, like a cat, he pushes it with his foot or sticks it to the sutra. This is from al-Ayni on al-Bukhari, and he attributed it to the Malikis, and our principles do not reject it. It also includes: it is not permissible for him to walk from his place to repel him; rather, he defends and repels him from his place because the harm of walking is greater than the harm of his passing before him. He is permitted only to the extent that he can reach from his standing place, and he should not go to the extent of invalidating his prayer. If he pushes him in a permissible manner and he dies, there is no sin on him by agreement of the scholars. Whether his blood-money is obligatory or goes unavenged: there are two opinions among the scholars. The blood-money is on his own wealth in full, and it is said it is on the 'aqlah. In al-Durr from al-Bazdawi, liability is required according to our books, and it goes unavenged according to al-Shafi'i. His statement 'he is a devil': al-Khattabi said: meaning the devil prompted him to that. It is also possible that by 'devil' is meant the passer himself, because the devil is the recalcitrant evil one from mankind and jinn. His statement: 'interpreted that etc.': Imam Muhammad interpreted it as repelling forcefully. But taking it literally is not what the common people do. His statement: 'with what we have presented from his statement, peace be upon him: Verily in prayer there is occupation.' And Allah, the Exalted and Glorious, knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Magnificent.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the ruling of the person praying preventing someone from passing in front of him. The author begins by citing the hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that commands the worshipper to ward off a passer-by and even fight him if necessary. He then clarifies that this ruling is interpreted to have been abrogated: fighting was permissible in early Islam but later prohibited. The current Hanafi position is that the worshipper may push gently but not fight; if the passer-by dies from a permissible push, no sin is incurred, but the blood-money is still due from the worshipper's own wealth according to the Hanafi school, though there is a difference with the Shafi'is. The passage also addresses practical details: if the passer-by is near, the worshipper signals or says tasbih; if that fails, he pushes once gently; if still not, he leaves him. He may not walk to repel, as walking is more harmful. For animals like cats, he may push them with his foot. The mention of 'devil' is interpreted as either the satanic impulse or the evil nature of the passer himself. Imam Muhammad interprets the hadith as allowing forceful repulsion, but the general community does not take it literally. The passage ends with a reference to the hadith that prayer occupies one from worldly matters.

Key Terms
الدرء (al-dar'): Warding off or repelling the passer-by
المار (al-marr): The person passing in front of the one praying
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of the earlier ruling permitting fighting

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Stop praying

Key Takeaway
The permission to fight in the hadith is abrogated; the worshiper may only push gently, and if the passer-by dies, blood-money is due from his wealth.

Actions Not Disliked During Prayer: A Critical Refinement
List of permissible actions with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions are not disliked during prayer according to the Hanafi school and identify the conditions that make them disliked.

Core Idea
Prayer tolerates many actions unless they cause distraction or resemble worship of other than Allah.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiyah refines earlier rulings on actions permissible during prayer. While many acts are allowed, each carries a condition—distraction, resemblance to non-Islamic practices, or exposure of 'awrah—that can render it disliked. Understanding these nuances prevents unnecessary hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Read the Arabic text and list each action mentioned: wearing a qaba', wearing a sword, not inserting hands into sleeves, facing a mus'haf, sword, back of a person, candle/lamp, prostrating on a carpet with images, killing a snake.
The act of facing the back of a seated person is permitted only if the person is speaking quietly.
2
Determine the default ruling
For each act, the default is 'la yukrah' (not disliked) unless a specific condition is present. State the default ruling.
e.g., wearing a sword is not disliked unless it distracts the worshiper.
3
Identify the condition that triggers dislike
Each act has a condition that, if present, makes it disliked. Find these conditions in the text.
For qaba': the condition is 'non-tied waist exposing 'awrah'. For sword: 'distraction in non-battle'. For carpet: 'prostrating directly on the images'.
4
Note the refinement
Al-Tahtawi refines earlier rulings, e.g., the dislike for carpet images was absolute in al-Asl but restricted to prostrating on the images. Recognize which view is mufta bihi.
The chosen view is from al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Bada'i', and Taj al-Shari'ah.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Given a scenario, determine if an action is disliked based on the conditions.
Practice with: praying while facing a lit candle in a mosque.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أنفسهم وناقض العهد خائن فيخشى منه أو ممن هو تحته. قوله: (وفي غير القباء قيل بكراهته أشار بقيل إلى ضعفه لما فيه من الحرج. قوله: (ولا يكره عدم إدخال يديه في (فرجيه هو ما في الخلاصة، وقد تقدم ما فيه . قائم قوله : (يتحدث) أي سرا بحيث لا يخاف منه الغلط، وقيد بالظهر لأنها إلى الوجه مكروهة، والكراهة على المتعدي وقيد بالتحدث ليفيد عدم الكراهة حال عدمه بالأولى . قوله : (أو شمع قال ابن قتيبة في باب ما جاء فيه :لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما الشمع بالسكون والأوجه فتح الميم اهـ من الشرح قوله: (لأنه لا يشبه عبادة المجوس) لأن المجوس يعبدون الجمر لا النار الموقدة قاله السيد قوله : (ولا) يكره السجود على بساط الخ) هذا ما في الجامع الصغير وصححه في البدائع، وتاج الشريعة، وأطلق الكراهة في الأصل قال في النهر : ولو حمل المطلق على المقيد لارتفع الخلاف، ولم يلح ما المانع من ذلك اهـ وتكره الكتابة على الأبسطة، ونحوها ولو بالحروف المفرقة ولو حرفاً واحداً أفاده السيد. قوله : (وأما بالنظر لخشية الجان الخ) قال صدر الإسلام الصحيح من الجواب أن يحتاط في قتل الحيات حتى لا يقتل جنياً فإنهم يؤذونه أذى كثيراً بل إذا رأى حية، وشك أنه جني يقول خل طريق المسلمين، ومر فإن تركه فإن واحداً من إخوتي وهو أكبر سناً مني قتل حية كبيرة بسيف في دارنا فضر به الجن حتى جعلوه زمناً لا تتحرك رجلاه قريباً من الشهر، ثم عالجناه وداويناه بإرضاء الجن حتى تركوه فزال ما به، وهذا مما عاينته بعيني اهـ وفي القهستاني عن شرح التأويلات أنهم أضعف من الأنس حتى لا يقدرون على إتلاف أحد من الإنس، وعلى سلب أموالهم، وإفساد طعامهم، وشرابهم اهـ وفيه تأمل قوله : (أو ممن هو مثله) أي في الخانية كبني آدم الذين اتصفوا بذلك، وهذا يغني عنه قوله وناقض العهد لأنها في مقام الكلية، وقوله من أهله يعني
His statement: 'Of actions' meaning also sayings, such as repeating a surah in the two rak'ahs of supererogatory prayer. His statement: 'in a qaba' not tied at the waist' – the qaba' is any garment open at the front like a qaftan. The first to wear it was Prophet Solomon (peace be upon him). The meaning is that he gathered its two ends without tying; otherwise the 'awrah would be exposed if he wore nothing else. If he prays in a qaba' not tied at the waist, he is doing a reprehensible act. In garments other than the qaba', it is said to be disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. And it is not disliked for the person praying to wear (a sword or the like) if he is not distracted by its movement. If it distracts him, it is disliked outside a state of fighting. And it is not disliked for him not to insert his hands into his sleeves and split them (i.e., of the garment) according to the chosen view, because it does not occupy the mind. And it is not disliked to face a mus'haf or a hanging sword because they are not worshipped. Allah said: 'And let them take their precaution and their weapons.' Or the back of a seated person who is speaking quietly according to the chosen view, because it does not resemble the worship of images. Ibn 'Umar prayed facing the back of Nafi'. Or a candle or lamp according to the correct view, because it does not resemble the worship of the Magians. And it is not disliked to prostrate on a carpet containing images of living beings if he does not prostrate on them, because he insults them by stepping on them. And it is not disliked to kill a snake of all kinds for the purpose of prayer. As for fear of the jinn, he should refrain from killing the white snake that walks straight because it broke the covenant that the Prophet made with the jinn not to enter the houses of his ummah and not to show themselves. The covenant-breaker is treacherous, so one fears from it or from one like it. His statement: 'In other than the qaba', it is said to be disliked' – he indicated by 'said' its weakness due to hardship. His statement: 'And it is not disliked to not insert his hands into his two sleeves (firjayh)' – this is as in al-Khulasa, and what was mentioned earlier applies. His statement: 'And his shiq' (split) meaning the split of the two sleeves like the Hejazi cloak. His statement: 'hanging' is an accidental restriction. His statement: 'And let them take' meaning that if the sword is in front of him, it is easier to take when needed, so it does not cause dislike. His statement: 'Or the back of a seated person' – meaning or standing. His statement: 'speaking quietly' meaning secretly so that no error is feared. He restricted it to the back because facing the face is disliked, and the dislike is for the one who transgresses. He restricted it to speaking to indicate that in its absence, there is no dislike, by priority. His statement: 'or a candle' – Ibn Qutaybah said in the chapter on what is said about it: there are two pronunciations; the people use the weaker one 'sham' with sukun, but the correct is with fatha on the mim. From the commentary. His statement: 'Because it does not resemble the worship of the Magians' because the Magians worship embers, not the ignited fire, as said by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'And it is not disliked to prostrate on a carpet' etc. This is in al-Jami' al-Saghir and was declared correct in al-Bada'i' and Taj al-Shari'ah. In al-Asl, dislike was declared absolute. In al-Nahr, it was said: If the absolute is restricted to the qualified, the disagreement is resolved, and there is no obstacle to that. And writing on carpets and similar is disliked, even with disconnected letters, even a single letter, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'As for fear of the jinn etc.' – Sadr al-Islam said: The correct answer is that one should be cautious in killing snakes so as not to kill a jinn, for they cause great harm. Rather, if he sees a snake and doubts it is a jinn, he should say: 'Clear the way of the Muslims and pass.' If it leaves him (good). One of my brothers, older than me, killed a large snake with a sword in our house, and the jinn harmed him until they made him crippled, his legs immobile for nearly a month. Then we treated him and appeased the jinn until they left him and he recovered. This is something I witnessed with my own eyes. In al-Qahistani from Sharh al-Ta'wilat, they (jinn) are weaker than humans, unable to kill anyone or steal their wealth or spoil their food and drink – but this is questionable. His statement: 'or one like him' meaning in al-Khaniyya, like the sons of Adam who are characterized by that. This suffices for his statement 'covenant-breaker' because it is in a general context, and his statement 'from his family' means.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on a series of rulings about actions that are not disliked (makruh) during prayer. The commentator, al-Tahtawi, refines the statements from Maraqi al-Falah. The rulings cover: (1) wearing a qaba' (open-front garment) not tied at the waist – this is disliked if it exposes the 'awrah; (2) wearing a sword or similar weapon – not disliked if not distracted, but disliked if distracted except in battle; (3) not inserting hands into sleeves – not disliked because it does not preoccupy the mind; (4) facing a mus'haf or hanging sword – not disliked because they are not objects of worship; proof is the Quranic command to take weapons; (5) facing the back of a seated person who is speaking quietly – not disliked because it does not resemble worshipping images; (6) facing a candle or lamp – not disliked because it does not resemble Magian fire-worship; (7) prostrating on a carpet with images of living beings – not disliked if not prostrating directly on the images, as stepping on them insults them; (8) killing snakes during prayer – not disliked for prayer's sake, but caution is advised regarding white snakes that walk straight, as they may be jinn with a covenant; killing such snakes may provoke harm. The commentator also explains that the dislike for not tying a qaba' is weak due to hardship, and that the ruling on the carpet's images is correct in al-Jami' al-Saghir and al-Bada'i', but some expressed absolute dislike. Finally, there is a long anecdote about jinn to illustrate the danger of killing a jinn accidentally.

Key Terms
القباء (al-qaba'): A garment open at the front like a qaftan
التقلد (al-taqallud): Wearing a sword or similar weapon by slinging it over the shoulder or hanging it
فرجيه (firjayh): The sleeves of the garment (dual form)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it disliked to pray facing a hanging sword?
A) Yes, because it resembles idolatry
B) No, because swords are not worshipped and the Quran commands taking weapons
C) Only if the sword is ornamental
D) Yes, because it distracts from prayer

Key Takeaway
Many actions during prayer are permissible unless they cause distraction or resemble worship of other than Allah, and later Hanafi authorities refined earlier rulings to reduce hardship.

Actions Not Disliked in Prayer: Attire, Weapons, and Facing Objects
Critical refinement on actions in prayer that are not disliked

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which actions regarding attire, weapon-carrying, and facing objects are not disliked in Hanafi prayer and identify the evidence for each ruling.

Core Idea
Prayer is not invalidated by permissible attire, carrying a sword, or facing a hanging mushaf—these are not disliked unless they distract.

This lesson clarifies several actions that some may consider problematic during prayer. The Hanafi school, as detailed in Maraqi al-Falah and its commentary by al-Tahtawi, explicitly states that certain actions are not disliked (makruh). Understanding these rulings removes unnecessary scrupulosity and aligns practice with sound evidence from the Quran and sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify each action
List the specific actions mentioned: wearing an untightened izaar, wearing other garments like qaba, carrying a sword, not inserting hands into garment openings, facing a hanging mushaf or sword, facing the back of a seated person, facing a candle or lamp.
2
Determine the ruling for each
For each action, state whether it is disliked, not disliked, or if there is a difference of opinion. Note that the untightened izaar is 'doing wrong' (disliked), others are not disliked on the preferred view.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ala al-mukhtar' (preferred view).
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa 4:71) used to justify carrying a sword. Understand how it provides rationale for not disliking the action. Also note the reliance on the practice of Ibn Umar and the concept that these objects are not worshipped.
The verse is cited to show that taking weapons is a precaution, not a distraction.
4
Evaluate the ikhtilaf
Recognize that some opinions (like disliking the qaba) are weak due to hardship. The commentator al-Tahtawi strengthens the permissive view. Understand that intra-Hanafi differences exist (e.g., on inserting hands) but the mufta bihi is the non-dislike.
The term 'qila' indicates weakness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كان يصلي في قباء غير مشدود الوسط فهو مسيء، وفي غير القباء قيل بكراهته لأنه صنيع أهل الكتاب (ولا) يكره (تقلد) المصلي بسيف ونحوه إذا لم يشتغل بحركته) وإن شغله كره في غير حالة قتال (ولا) يكره (عدم إدخال يديه في فرجيه وشقه على المختار) لعدم شغل البال (ولا) يكره التوجه لمصحف أو سيف (معلق لأنهما لا يعبدان، وقال تعالى: وليأخذوا حذرهم وأسلحتهم أو ظهر قاعد يتحدث في المختار لعدم التشبه بعبادة الصور وصلى ابن عمر إلى ظهر نافع أو شمع أو سراج على الصحيح) لأنه لا يشبه عبادة المجوس. قوله: (وفي غير القباء قيل بكراهته أشار بقيل إلى ضعفه لما فيه من الحرج. قوله: (ولا يكره عدم إدخال يديه في (فرجيه هو ما في الخلاصة، وقد تقدم ما فيه. قوله: (وشقه) أي شق الفرجي كالعباء الحجازي قوله: (معلق) قيد اتفاقي. قوله: ( وليأخذ والخ) أي، وإذا كان السيف بين يديه كان أمكن لأخذه إذا احتاج إليه فلا يوجب الكراهة. قوله: (أو ظهر قاعد) أي أو قائم قوله: (يتحدث) أي سرا بحيث لا يخاف منه الغلط، وقيد بالظهر لأنها إلى الوجه مكروهة، والكراهة على المتعدي وقيد بالتحدث ليفيد عدم الكراهة حال عدمه بالأولى. قوله: (أو شمع قال ابن قتيبة في باب ما جاء فيه: لغتان استعمل الناس أضعفهما الشمع بالسكون والأوجه فتح الميم اهـ من الشرح قوله: (لأنه لا يشبه عبادة المجوس) لأن المجوس يعبدون الجمر لا النار الموقدة قاله السيد
If he prays in an izaar (loincloth) that is not tightened in the middle, he is doing wrong. And in other than an izaar, it is said to be disliked because it is the practice of the People of the Book. And it is not disliked for the worshipper to carry a sword or the like if he is not occupied by its movement. And if it occupies him, it is disliked in a non-battle state. And it is not disliked not to insert his hands into the openings of his garment (farj) and its slit, according to the preferred view, because there is no preoccupation of mind. And it is not disliked to face a mushaf or a sword that is hung because they are not worshipped. And Allah says: 'Let them take their precautions and their weapons.' Or facing the back of a seated person who is speaking quietly, according to the preferred view, because of non-resemblance to image worship. And Ibn Umar prayed facing the back of Nafi' or a candle or a lamp, according to the sound opinion, because it does not resemble the worship of the Magians. His statement: 'And in other than an izaar, it is said to be disliked' he indicated by 'it is said' its weakness due to hardship. His statement: 'not to insert his hands into his farj' is what is in al-Khulasa, and its discussion has preceded. His statement: 'and its slit' meaning the slit of the farj like the Hijazi aba. His statement: 'hung' is an incidental condition. His statement: 'Walyakhudhu wa al-kha' meaning that if the sword is in front of him, it is more possible for him to take it when needed, so it does not necessitate dislike. His statement: 'or the back of a seated person' meaning or standing. His statement: 'talking' meaning quietly so that no mistake is feared. He restricted it to 'back' because facing the face is disliked, and the dislike is for the one who does it excessively. He restricted it to 'talking' to indicate no dislike in its absence a fortiori. His statement: 'or a candle' said Ibn Qutayba: there are two pronunciations; people use the weaker one: 'sham' with sukun, and the more proper is with fatha on the mim. End from the sharh. His statement: 'because it does not resemble the worship of the Magians' because the Magians worship embers, not the kindled fire, as said by al-Sayyid.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) on rulings from Maraqi al-Falah concerning actions in prayer that are not disliked (makruh). The commentator, al-Tahtawi, clarifies and corrects the base text. First, he addresses wearing an izaar (waist-wrapper) that is not tightened: the base text says one who prays thus is 'doing wrong' (musi'), meaning his prayer is valid but he commits a disliked act. For other garments like a shirt (qaba), it is said to be disliked because it resembles the dress of Jews and Christians. However, the commentator notes that this 'qila' (it is said) indicates weakness, as there is hardship in avoiding it. Second, carrying a sword in prayer is not disliked unless one becomes occupied with its movement (except in battle). Third, not inserting hands into the garment openings (farj and shaqq) is not disliked on the preferred view, contrary to some opinions that considered it makruh. Fourth, facing a hanging mushaf (Quran) or sword is not disliked because they are not objects of worship; a Quranic verse (Surah al-Nisa, 8:71) is cited to show that carrying weapons in prayer is permitted. Fifth, praying facing the back of a seated person who is talking quietly is not disliked, as it does not resemble the worship of images; Ibn Umar is reported to have prayed facing the back of his servant Nafi. Sixth, praying towards a candle or lamp is permissible (not disliked) because it does not resemble Magian worship of fire. The commentator notes linguistic variants for 'sham' (candle). The overall thrust is to ease concerns about these actions.

Key Terms
قباء (qaba'): A type of garment, like a shirt or tunic, that is tailored and has sleeves, as opposed to an izaar (waist-wrapper).
فرجيه (farjaih): The two openings or slits in a garment, such as the opening for the head or arms, or the sides of an aba.
تقلد (taqallud): To carry or wear something by suspending it from the shoulder or neck, e.g., a sword.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on praying while facing a hanging mushaf (Quran) according to the preferred Hanafi view?
A) It is disliked (makruh).
B) It is forbidden (haram).
C) It is not disliked.
D) It invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Most actions regarding attire, weapon-carrying, and facing objects are not disliked in Hanafi prayer unless they distract or involve excessive resemblance to non-Muslim worship.

Prostration on Images and Killing Creatures in Prayer
Clarifies rules on prostrating on images and killing harmful creatures in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on prostrating on a mat with images and killing harmful creatures during prayer, including the exception for the white snake, and apply the intra-Hanafi differences regarding lice.

Core Idea
Prostration on images is permitted when not directly on them; killing harmful creatures is allowed in prayer, but the white snake is spared as a jinni.

This lesson from Hashiya al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah addresses two practical issues in prayer: the permissibility of prostrating on a mat with pictures and the rulings on killing snakes, scorpions, and other creatures during salat. The Hanafi school provides detailed guidance based on the principle of necessity and respect for images, along with a prophetic tradition distinguishing between harmful snakes and jinn snakes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues
The passage covers (1) prostration on a mat with images and (2) killing snakes and scorpions during prayer. Recognize that these are separate but both relate to actions permissible in prayer.
2
Analyze the ruling on prostration
The text states it is not disliked to prostrate on a mat with images as long as one does not prostrate directly on them. The underlying reason is insulting the image by stepping on it.
This resolves the apparent conflict with texts that unconditionally dislike it.
3
Examine the ruling on killing snakes
Generally, killing a snake for the sake of prayer is not disliked. However, the text introduces a caution: refrain from killing the white snake that walks straight, as it may be a jinni with a covenant.
The hadith 'Kill the two abnormal ones... beware of the white snake' is cited.
4
Understand the conditions for killing
Killing a snake or scorpion is only not disliked if the worshipper fears harm. If safe, much action is disliked. The text permits multiple strikes and turning from qibla in the apparent view.
The list of seven creatures from Abu al-Layth expands the ruling to other harmful pests.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on lice
Imam Abu Hanifa prefers burying lice over killing, while Muhammad permits killing and Abu Yusuf dislikes both. The cross-madhhab issue: Shafi'is consider louse blood impure.
The Hanafi view is more lenient in killing lice if needed.

And it is not disliked to prostrate on a mat that has images of living beings if he does not prostrate on them, because of insulting them by stepping on them. And it is not disliked to kill a snake of any kind for the sake of the prayer itself. But with regard to fear of jinn, he should refrain from killing the white snake that walks straight, because it has broken the covenant of the Prophet (ﷺ) with the jinn that they would not enter the houses of his community nor show themselves. The covenant-breaker is treacherous, so he fears harm from it or from those under it. His statement: 'because it does not resemble the worship of the Magians' because the Magians worship embers, not the kindled fire, as said by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'And it is not disliked to prostrate on a mat' is what is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, and it was declared sound in al-Bada'i' and Taj al-Shari'ah. He declared dislike unconditionally in the original. In al-Nahr: If the absolute were carried on the restricted, the disagreement would be removed, and no obstacle to that is apparent. End. And writing on mats and the like is disliked, even with separate letters, even one letter, as related by al-Sayyid. His statement: 'And with regard to fear of jinn' said Sadr al-Islam: The correct answer is that one should be cautious in killing snakes so as not to kill a jinni, for they harm him greatly. Rather, if he sees a snake and doubts it is a jinni, he says: 'Clear the way of Muslims and pass.' If it leaves (then fine). A certain person, one of my brethren, older than me, killed a large snake with a sword in our house, and the jinn struck him until they made him paralyzed, his legs would not move for nearly a month. Then we treated him and pacified the jinn until they left him and his affliction went away. This is what I witnessed. End. In al-Qahistani from Sharh al-Ta'wilat: They (jinn) are weaker than humans, so they cannot destroy any human, steal their wealth, or corrupt their food and drink. End. But there is reflection on this. His statement: 'or from someone like him' means in al-Khaniyah, like humans who are described as such. This suffices for his statement 'and the covenant-breaker' because it is general, and his statement 'from his people' means 'like him from his people.' Harm is feared from killing or striking it. And he said: 'Kill, then, the two abnormal ones and the stunted (snake) and beware of the white snake, for it is of the jinn.' And it is not disliked to kill a snake and scorpion if the worshipper fears their harm. And if he kills them with two strikes and deviation from the qibla, it is the apparent view (al-azhar). It is said with fear of harm, because if there is safety, much action is disliked. And in the Sab'iniyat of Abu al-Layth, there are seven creatures which, if the worshipper sees, there is no harm in killing them: the snake, scorpion, gecko, hornet, tick, flea, and louse; and also add the bedbug, mosquito, and ant that bite harmfully. But avoiding hitting the blood of the louse is better so as not to carry impurity that prevents (prayer) according to Imam al-Shafi'i. We have already mentioned the dislike of taking a louse and killing it in prayer according to Imam (Abu Hanifa). He said burying it is more beloved than killing it. Muhammad said the opposite. Abu Yusuf said both are disliked.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage covers two main issues: prostration on a mat with images and killing snakes/scorpions in prayer. First, prostrating on a mat with pictures of living beings is not disliked according to the sound view, as long as one does not prostrate directly on the image. Stepping on the image is considered an insult, thus permissible. However, writing on such mats is disliked. This ruling is from al-Jami' al-Saghir. Second, killing a snake during prayer for the sake of the prayer itself (e.g., out of fear of harm) is not disliked. However, the commentator introduces a caveat: one should refrain from killing the 'white snake' that walks straight because it is believed to be a jinni that has a covenant with the Prophet (ﷺ). Killing it could bring harm from the jinn. The commentator narrates a story about a man who killed such a snake and was afflicted. Then he cites a hadith: 'Kill the two abnormal ones (snakes with two stripes) and the stunted one, and beware of the white snake, for it is of the jinn.' This indicates a distinction. Third, if the worshipper fears harm from a snake or scorpion, it is not disliked to kill them, even with multiple actions (two strikes, turning from qibla), according to the apparent view. During safety, much unnecessary action would be disliked. The commentator lists seven creatures that can be killed in prayer according to Abu al-Layth: snake, scorpion, gecko, hornet, tick, flea, louse, plus bedbug, mosquito, and harmful ant. He notes a difference among the Hanafi imams about killing a louse: Imam Abu Hanifa preferred burying it, Muhammad allowed killing it, and Abu Yusuf disliked both taking and killing. The text emphasizes avoiding blood stains from lice because they are impure according to Imam al-Shafi'i, but Hanafis consider it merely disliked.

Key Terms
السجود على بساط فيه تصاوير (al-sujud 'ala bisat fihi tasawir): Prostration on a mat or carpet that contains pictures of living creatures.
الحية البيضاء (al-hayyat al-bayda'): A white snake believed to be a jinn that has a covenant with the Prophet (ﷺ); it walks straight.
الطفيتين والأبتر (al-tufayatayn wa al-abtar): Two types of snakes: the 'tufaya' (with two stripes on its back) and the 'abtar' (tailless, stub-tailed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the Hanafi ruling say about killing a white snake that walks straight during prayer?
A) It is obligatory to kill it.
B) It is recommended to kill it.
C) One should refrain from killing it due to fear of harming a jinni.
D) It invalidates the prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prostration on images is permissible with care; killing harmful creatures in prayer is allowed except for the white snake, and lice may be killed but burying is preferable.

Permissible Minor Actions in Prayer: Dusting, Wiping, and Glancing
Details actions that are permissible in prayer: shaking off dust, wiping face, and glancing without turning the head.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on shaking clothes, wiping the forehead, and glancing with peripheral vision in prayer, distinguishing permissible from disliked.

Core Idea
Minor purposeful movements in prayer are permissible if they aid devotion, but avoid unnecessary distractions.

This passage from Maraqi al-Falah clarifies that not all movements invalidate prayer. Shaking dust from clothes, wiping sweat or dirt from the forehead, and glancing with the corner of the eyes are all permissible under specific conditions. Understanding these rulings helps maintain khushu' (devotion) without falling into extremism or negligence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Action
Read the source text and list the three actions mentioned: shaking clothes (nafd thawb), wiping the forehead (masah jabha), and glancing with the eyes (al-nazar bi-mawq al-'aynayn).
The text uses 'la ba'sa' (no harm) for each, indicating permissibility.
2
Determine the Hukm Level
Each action is ruled as permissible (mubah) in Hanafi fiqh. However, the text also states that it is better to avoid glancing unnecessarily. Assess the hukm for each: is it allowed, recommended, or disliked?
The phrase 'al-awla tarkuhu' (it is better to leave it) indicates that the action is not completely free of dislike (makruh tanzih) when done without need.
3
Check Conditions and Limitations
Note the conditions mentioned: actions must be minimal (qalil), not excessive. For wiping, it is allowed only if sweat or dirt disturbs concentration. For glancing, it is allowed without turning the head. Identify the conditions that make the action valid.
The principle is that the action should not compromise khushu' or become a distraction.
4
Explore the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf on Invalidation
The text mentions a difference of opinion on whether killing a harmful snake with much action invalidates prayer. Al-Halabi says it does, others say it does not. Identify the mufta bihi opinion as per al-Bahr and al-Kamal.
This shows that the definition of 'much action' is not fixed, and later Hanafi authorities lean toward non-invalidation but dislike.
5
Apply to Modern Scenarios
Consider modern equivalents: adjusting a prayer mat, brushing off a fly, or wiping glasses. Apply the same principles of minimal action and necessity to determine permissibility.
The rulings are based on the same illa (cause): preserving khushu' and avoiding unnecessary movement.

Commentary
This passage discusses minor actions permissible in prayer, focusing on convenience and maintaining concentration. Firstly, shaking one's clothes with a minimal action to prevent them from clinging to the body during ruku' is allowed, as it avoids revealing the shape of limbs. Similarly, protecting clothes from dust is fine. Wiping dust or grass from the forehead after prayer is permissible as a cleaning practice. Wiping before completion is also allowed if sweat or dirt disturbs concentration. Glancing left or right with the eyes (without turning the head) is not prohibited, but better avoided unless necessary due to etiquette. The commentator then returns to the earlier discussion on killing snakes, emphasizing that if one is safe, much action is disliked but a little action like stepping on a scorpion with a sandal is fine. He notes a difference in whether killing with much action invalidates prayer: some say it does, others not. The relied-upon view (from al-Bahr) is that it does not invalidate but is still disliked. Killing harmful ants is only permissible if they bite; non-harmful ones cannot be killed. Regarding the louse, the earlier dislike applies only to non-harmful ones. Finally, wiping the forehead is discussed: there is a hadith that angels seek forgiveness for the worshipper as long as dust remains, so leaving it is better, but the commentator notes that cleaning off dirt is also preferable to avoid looking disheveled. The text ends abruptly but the gist is that these minor actions are permissible to enhance devotion.

مسح جبهة (masah jabha): Wiping the forehead to remove traces of dust or sweat after or during prayer.

Killing Harmful Creatures in Prayer: Permissibility and Conditions
Fiqh ruling on killing harmful creatures during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when killing a harmful creature during prayer is permissible and identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding lice.

Core Idea
Fear of harm permits actions that would otherwise be disliked.

Prayer requires stillness, but what if a snake or scorpion threatens you? This lesson examines the Hanafi position on killing harmful creatures during salah, balancing the sanctity of prayer against necessity. We will explore the proof from hadith, the scope of permissible actions, and the nuanced disagreement among the Hanafi imams regarding lice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its general ruling
The act is killing a harmful creature (snake, scorpion, etc.) during prayer. The ruling: it is not disliked (mubah) if the worshipper fears harm.
The default ruling for killing in prayer is disliked due to excessive action; fear of harm overrides this.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites a hadith: 'Kill the two-palmed snake and the tailless snake, and beware of the white snake for it is from the jinn.' This is a command (amr) indicating permissibility.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted by the Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'اقتلوا' (kill) in context of harmful creatures gives permissibility, not obligation. The condition is fear of harm. The hadith is applied via the principle that preventing harm outweighs the prohibition of excessive action in prayer.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless there is a qarina (context) indicating permissibility. Here, fear of harm is the qarina.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on lice
For lice, Abu Hanifa disliked killing and preferred burying; Muhammad allowed it; Abu Yusuf disliked both. The difference stems from whether lice are considered harmful enough to warrant action in prayer.
Practical consequence: a Hanafi may choose to bury a louse rather than kill it, while Muhammad's view permits killing.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The passage does not specify the operative view, but later Hanafi practice often follows Muhammad's view for lice due to ease and the general principle of necessity.
This reflects the later Hanafi tendency to adopt the lighter position in matters of necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And it is not disliked (to kill a snake and scorpion if the worshipper fears (their harm)) i.e., the snake and scorpion, (even if) he kills them (with two strikes and deviation from the qibla in (the most apparent) view. But caution against touching louse blood is preferable, lest it carry impurity that prevents (prayer) according to Imam al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on him). Commentary
This passage addresses the permissibility of killing harmful creatures during prayer. It begins by citing a hadith commanding the killing of certain types of snakes (the 'two-palmed' and 'tailless' snakes, and the white snake from the jinn). The ruling then states that it is not disliked to kill a snake or scorpion if the worshipper fears harm from them, even if it requires multiple actions like two strikes or turning away from the qibla. This is based on the principle that fear of harm permits actions that would otherwise be disliked if done without need. The text then lists seven creatures that can be killed without blame according to Abu al-Layth: snake, scorpion, gecko, hornet, tick, flea, and louse. Later scholars added bedbugs, mosquitoes, and biting ants. For lice, there is a specific intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa considered taking and killing lice in prayer disliked (makruh), and preferred burying the louse over killing it. Muhammad al-Shaybani disagreed, allowing the killing without dislike. Abu Yusuf disliked both actions (taking and killing). The passage also notes that one should avoid touching louse blood because it is considered impure by Imam al-Shafi'i, though the Hanafi school has a different view on blood impurity. This passage shows the Hanafi approach of balancing necessity with the prohibition of excessive action in prayer.

Key Terms
العمل الكثير (al-‘amal al-kathir): A large amount of physical action that invalidates prayer if done without necessity.
الطغيتين (al-tughyatayn): A type of snake with two marks like palm-leaves on its back; considered harmful.
الأبتر (al-abtar): A tailless snake; considered harmful and commanded to be killed.

Key Takeaway
Fear of harm permits killing otherwise prohibited creatures during prayer; the Hanafi school provides a detailed case-by-case ruling balancing necessity and prayer sanctity.
