Delaying Fard Prayer Due to Fear: Ruling and Analogy
Ruling on delaying fard prayer for a traveler fearing harm, with analogy to combatants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which delaying a fard prayer is permissible in the Hanafi school and apply the analogy to combatants.

Core Idea
Fear of harm permits delaying prayer, as combatants delay for battle—prayer can be made up, battle cannot.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashiya addresses a practical fiqh question: can a traveler delay the obligatory prayer if they fear thieves, wild animals, or floods? The ruling draws an analogy to combatants who delay prayer due to warfare. Beyond the traveler, the passage also extends this concession to making up missed prayers (qada) and discusses the time frame for qada of fasting and other acts. Let's explore the legal reasoning and conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and its Conditions
The passage states that a traveler fearing specific dangers may delay the timely prayer. The condition is fear of serious harm (thieves, beasts, flood). The ruling is permissibility (mubah) with an excuse.
Note that simply being a traveler is not sufficient; fear is the key condition.
2
Trace the Analogy to Combatants
The text explicitly likens the traveler to combatants. Why? Because combatants have an excuse (battle) that cannot be recovered if missed, while prayer can be made up. This is a qiyas (analogy) based on the common illa: an excuse that prevents timely performance.
The illa is the inability to perform the prayer on time due to a pressing harm that cannot be remedied later.
3
Locate the Hadith Proof
The commentary cites the Prophet (ﷺ) delaying four prayers due to preoccupation with polytheists. This serves as a dalil for the permissibility of delaying prayer for a valid excuse.
The hadith is ahad and indicates permissibility (dalala zanni).
4
Examine the Extension to Qada and Other Acts
The passage extends the same concession to making up missed prayers (qada) for an excuse like earning a livelihood. For fasting qada, the delay is allowed until before the next Ramadan. For sajdat al-tilawa and nadhr, there is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars.
This shows that the principle of delay due to excuse applies broadly but with scope differences.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
For sajda and nadhr, al-Tahawi says expansive (permissible to delay), while al-Halwani and al-Amiri say restricted (must be done immediately). This demonstrates that even within the school, subsidiary issues may have differing views.
The mufta bihi on this subsidiary point may need further consultation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أي السائر في فضاء إذا خاف من اللصوص، أو قطاع الطريق) أو من سبع أو سيل (جاز له تأخير الوقتية كالمقاتلين إذا لم يقدروا على الإيماء ركباناً للعذر وكذا يجوز تأخير قضاء الفوائت للعذر كالسعي على العيال، وإن وجب قضاؤها على الفور وأما قضاء الصوم فعلى التراخي ما لم يقرب رمضان الثاني، وأما سجدة التلاوة والنذر المطابق ففيهما الخلاف قيل موسع وقيل مضيق

بالتأخير من القابلة وتمامه في الشرح قوله : (كما أخر النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم الصلاة) أي جنسها فإنّ المشركين شغلوه عن أربع صلوات فقضاهن مرتباً الظهر، ثم العصر ثم المغرب، ثم العشاء. قوله : (أي السائر في فضاء أفاد به أنّ المراد السفر اللغوي، ومثله فيما يظهر ليس بقيد بل كذلك المقيم. قوله: (كالمقاتلين إذا لم يقدروا الخ) لأنهم إذا فاتهم القتال بالإشتغال بالصلاة لا يمكنهم تداركه والصلاة يمكنهم تدارك ما فات منها قوله : قيل موسع) قائله الطحاوي. قوله: (وقيل مضيق) قائله الحلواني ،والعامري، وهذا الخلاف يجري في قضاء رمضان كما في الدر.
A traveler in open land if he fears thieves or highway robbers or a beast or a flood, it is permissible for him to delay the timely prayer, like the combatants when they are unable to gesture while riding due to an excuse. Likewise, it is permissible to delay the making up of missed prayers due to an excuse, such as striving to provide for one's family, although making them up is obligatory immediately. As for making up the fast, it is delayed as long as the second Ramadan does not approach. As for the prostration of recitation and a vowed (nadhr) matching [them], there is a difference of opinion regarding them: some say it is expansive, some say it is restricted. [Commentary:] 'by delaying from the next [prayer] and its completion is in the sharh. He said: (as the Prophet delayed the prayer) meaning its kind, for the polytheists occupied him from four prayers, so he made them up in order: zuhr, then asr, then maghrib, then isha. He said: (a traveler in open land) indicates that what is meant is linguistic travel, and it appears that it is not a condition, rather similarly for a resident. He said: (like the combatants when they are unable) because if they miss the battle by occupying themselves with prayer, they cannot make it up, and prayer they can make up what they missed. He said: (some say expansive) its proponent is al-Tahawi. He said: (some say restricted) its proponent is al-Halwani and al-Amiri, and this difference applies to making up Ramadan as in al-Durr.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on delaying obligatory prayers due to valid excuses, from the hashiya of al-Tahtawi. The text states that a traveler who fears thieves, beasts, or flood may delay the current prayer, analogous to combatants who are unable to pray even by gesture while riding due to warfare. The same permission applies to delaying the qada (make-up) of missed prayers when one has a genuine excuse like earning a livelihood for dependents, although normally qada is required immediately. Fasting qada, however, is delayed until before the next Ramadan. Regarding sajdat al-tilawa (prostration of recitation) and nadhr (vowed supererogatory acts), there is a dispute: al-Tahawi considers them expansive (permissible to delay), while al-Halwani and al-Amiri consider them restricted (must be performed immediately). The commentary explains that the ruling for combatants is based on the fact that battle cannot be recovered, but prayer can. It also clarifies that the mention of 'traveler' is not a strict condition; even a resident may delay if the same fear arises. The hadith of the Prophet delaying four prayers due to preoccupation with polytheists supports the principle.

Key Terms
الوقتية (al-waqtiyyah): The obligatory prayer performed within its prescribed time.
الفوائت (al-fawa'it): Prayers that were missed and require qada (make-up).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Analogy to combatants who delay due to warfare
B) The traveler is generally not required to pray on time
C) Any fear, even minor, justifies delay
D) The hadith of the Prophet delaying zuhr and asr

Key Takeaway
A valid excuse of fear or hardship permits delaying the fard prayer, as long as it is made up later.

Worldly Punishment for Abandoning Salah and Sawm out of Laziness
Ruling on worldly punishment for lazy abandonment of fard

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on punishing one who abandons fard salah/sawm out of laziness, apply the distinction between lazy abandonment and apostasy, and evaluate the cross-madhhab disagreement.

Core Idea
Abandoning prayer out of laziness warrants beating and imprisonment, not death; only denial or scorn makes one an apostate.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi outlines the Hanafi position on the worldly punishment for deliberately neglecting obligatory prayers or fasting out of laziness. While the act is a major sin, the Hanafi school stops short of declaring the offender an apostate or imposing capital punishment. The proof from the hadith of Jabir serves as a warning but is interpreted as not automatically entailing disbelief. In contrast, Shafi'i and Hanbali schools hold stricter views, either killing as a discretionary punishment or as apostasy. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for correctly applying Islamic penal law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is abandoning fard salah/sawm intentionally out of laziness. The ruling is severe beating and imprisonment until the act is performed or the person dies in prison. This is a worldly punishment; the Hereafter punishment is even more severe.
Laziness (kasan) means negligence, not denial or excuse.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the hadith of Jabir: 'Between a man and disbelief is abandoning prayer' (Ahmad, Muslim). This hadith is a warning about the gravity of abandoning prayer.
The hadith is ahad, so its transmission (thubut) is zanni.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Hanafis interpret the hadith as a severe warning, not a declaration that the lazy abandoner becomes a disbeliever. The hadith is zanni al-dalala, and the Hanafi principle is that mere abandonment while acknowledging obligation does not amount to kufr.
If the person denies the obligation or scoffs, then it becomes apostasy.
4
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Shafi'is hold that the offender is killed as a hadd punishment; Hanbalis consider it apostasy (kufr) and kill as an apostate. Hanafis confine capital punishment to cases of denial (jahl) or scorn (istikhfaf), not mere laziness.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is whether a negligent Muslim is executed or imprisoned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتارك الصلاة عمداً كسلاً يضرب ضرباً شديداً حتى يسيل منه الدم و) بعده (يحبس) ولا يترك هملا، بل يتفقد حاله بالوعظ والزجر والضرب أيضاً (حتى يصليها) أو يموت بحبسه وهذا جزاؤه الدنيوي، وأما في الآخرة إذا مات على الإسلام عاصياً بتركها فله عذاب طويل بواد في جهنم أشدها حراً، وأبعدها قعراً فيه بئر يقال له الهبهب، وآبار يسيل إليها الصديد، والقيح، أعدت لتارك الصلاة، وحديث جابر فيه صفته بقوله: بين الرجل وبين الكفر ترك الصلاة رواه أحمد ومسلم (وكذا تارك صوم رمضان) كسلا يضرب كذلك، ويحبس حتى يصوم ولا يقتل) بمجرد ترك الصلاة والصوم مع الإقرار بفرضيتهما إلا إذا جحد افتراض الصلاة أو الصوم لانكاره ما كان معلوماً من الدين إجماعاً (أو استخف بأحدهما) كما لو أظهر الافطار في نهار رمضان بلا عذر تهاوناً، أو نطق بما يدل عليه فيكون حكمه حكم المرتد فتكشف شبهته، ويحبس، ثم يقتل إن أصر .

قوله : (وتارك الصلاة عمداً كسلاً) احترز به عن الترك سهواً، أو لعذر فليس عليه شيء مما ذكر قوله : ( وآبار الخ الواو بمعني، أو وهي لحكاية الخلاف فإنهم اختلفوا في تفسير الغي في قوله تعالى : فسوف يلقون عيا فقيل الضلال، وقال الحسن عذاباً طويلاً، وقال ابن عباس شراً وقيل آبار في جهنم الخ أفاده في الشرح قوله : ( وحديث جابر) مبتدأ خبره قوله فيه صفته أي صفة تارك الصلاة. قوله : (ولا يقتل) وقالت الشافعية يقتل حذا وقال الإمام أحمد : يقتل كفراً كما نقله صاحب المواهب عنه، ونقله ابن تيمية عن أكثر السلف في الرسالة المتعلقة بالسياسة. قوله : (نهاوناً) وأما إذا كان لضرورة فلا قوله أو نطق بما يدل عليه) أي على الاستخفاف كما إذا قال رمضان ثقيل، أو سامج. قوله : ( ويحبس) حبس المرتد مندوب وكذا كشف شبهته والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And one who intentionally abandons prayer out of laziness is beaten severely until blood flows from him, and after that he is imprisoned, and he is not left neglected; rather his state is checked with admonition, rebuke, and also beating until he prays it or dies in his imprisonment. This is his worldly punishment. As for the Hereafter, if he dies as a Muslim, disobedient by leaving it, he will have a long punishment in a valley in Hell that is more severe in heat and deeper in depth; in it is a well called al-Habhub, and wells to which pus and discharge flow, prepared for the one who abandons prayer. And the hadith of Jabir describes it with his saying: 'Between a man and disbelief is abandoning prayer' – narrated by Ahmad and Muslim. Likewise, one who abandons fasting of Ramadan out of laziness is beaten similarly and imprisoned until he fasts, and he is not killed merely for abandoning prayer and fasting while acknowledging their obligation, unless he denies the obligation of prayer or fasting – because he denies what is known of the religion by consensus – or scoffs at one of them, such as if he shows breaking the fast in the day of Ramadan without an excuse out of disdain, or utters something indicating that. Then his ruling is the ruling of an apostate: his doubts are removed, he is imprisoned, then killed if he persists. [Commentary:] 'His saying: (one who intentionally abandons prayer out of laziness) excludes abandoning forgetfully or due to an excuse, for there is nothing of what was mentioned upon him. His saying: (and wells – the waw is in the meaning of 'or', and it is for narrating a difference, for they differed in interpreting 'ghayy' in the verse: fawsa yalqawna ghaiya; some said it means error, al-Hasan said a long punishment, Ibn Abbas said evil, and some said wells in Hell – as stated in the sharh. His saying: (and the hadith of Jabir) is the subject, its predicate is his saying 'its description', i.e. the description of the one who abandons prayer. His saying: (and he is not killed) – the Shafi'is said he is killed as a punishment (hadd), and Imam Ahmad said he is killed as disbelief, as transmitted by the author of al-Mawahib from him, and Ibn Taymiyya transmitted it from most of the Salaf in the treatise related to governance. His saying: (out of disdain) – but if it is due to necessity, then no. His saying: (or utters something indicating it) i.e. indicating scoffing, such as if he says 'Ramadan is heavy' or 'vile'. His saying: (and he is imprisoned) – imprisonment of the apostate is commendable (mandub), and similarly removing his doubts. And Allah knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage addresses the punishment for one who deliberately abandons obligatory prayer or fasting out of laziness (not denial). The Hanafi ruling is that such a person is first beaten severely, then imprisoned until he performs the missed act or dies. In the Hereafter, the punishment is severe. The hadith of Jabir is cited to emphasize that abandoning prayer is a borderline with disbelief, but the Hanafi school does not declare him an apostate for mere abandonment. If the person instead denies the obligation (jahl) or scoffs (istikhfaf), he is treated as an apostate: given a chance to repent, then killed if he persists. The commentary clarifies that the beating and imprisonment apply only to intentional lazy abandonment, not forgetfulness or genuine excuse. The discussion also notes that Shafi'is and Hanbalis differ: Shafi'is kill as a discretionary punishment (hadd), and Hanbalis as apostasy. The Hanafi position is that killing is only for denial or scorn, not mere abandonment.

Key Terms
كسلاً (kasan): Lazily, out of negligence, not due to denial or excuse.
استخفاف (istikhlaf): Scoffing at or showing contempt for a religious obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school punishes lazy abandonment of fard salah/sawm with beating and imprisonment, not death, reserving capital punishment for denial or scorn.

The Legal Status of Witr Prayer in the Hanafi School
Defines witr and reconciles contradictory narrations on its obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on witr, explain the intra-madhhab difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, and apply the concept of fard 'amali to reconcile conflicting reports.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib in practice but not fard in belief—denial does not remove one from Islam.

The status of witr prayer has been a point of discussion within the Hanafi school itself. While the relied-upon position is that witr is wajib (obligatory), there are narrations from Abu Hanifa suggesting it is sunnah or even fard. This lesson unpacks the evidence and the scholarly reconciliation that classifies witr as 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation), a distinct category in Hanafi fiqh that ensures its performance without making its denial an act of disbelief.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three reported views from Abu Hanifa
List the three positions attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa: that witr is wajib (the most correct and last view), that it is sunnah (the view of the Sahibayn), and that it is fard (an earlier view). Note that the Sahibayn's view is considered weaker.
2
Understand the distinction between fard 'ilmi and fard 'amali
Grasp the Hanafi technical distinction: fard 'ilmi is a creedal obligation whose denier becomes a disbeliever; fard 'amali is a practical obligation whose denier is not a disbeliever but still required to perform. The scholars classified witr as fard 'amali to reconcile the reports.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi usul.
3
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith 'Witr is a right; whoever does not perform witr is not from me' is cited as the evidence for obligation. Understand how the Hanafi school derives the ruling of wujub from this hadith, despite its being a solitary (ahad) report.
The command implicit in the hadith is considered binding.
4
Analyze the Hanafi reconciliation of conflicting evidence
The commentary explains that wajib can be of two types: one with the strength of fard (like witr, which can invalidate Fajr if remembered) and one below fard (like reciting Fatiha, whose omission only requires sajda al-sahw). Witr falls into the higher category, explaining its binding nature.
This resolves the objection about witr spoiling Fajr prayer if remembered during it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The text states that witr is wajib according to the most correct view (al-asahh). Practically, this means it must be performed and made up if missed. The Sahibayn's view (sunnah) is considered marjuh (preponderated against).
All Muslims, free or slave, male or female, are obligated to perform witr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الوتر وأحكامه
لما فرغ من بيان الفرض العلمي شرع في العملي، وهو في اللغة الفرد خلاف الشفع بالفتح، والكسر وفي الشرع صلاة مخصوصة، وصفه بقوله الوتر واجب) في الأصح وهو آخر أقوال الإمام وروي عنه أنه سنة وهو قولهما، وروي عنه أنه فرض ووفق المشايخ بين عملاً .
الروايات بأنه فرض . وهو الذي لا يترك واجب اعتقاداً، فلا يكفر جاحده سنة دليلاً لثبوته بها وجه الوجوب قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس مني الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس مني الوتر حق فمن لم يوتر فليس مني) رواه أبو داود والحاكم وصححه والأمر
باب الوتر
قوله : لما فرغ من بيان الفرض العلمي) أي الإعتقادي الذي يكفر جاحده شرع في العملي أي فيما يفترض عمله لا اعتقاده قوله : (صلاة مخصوصة) وهي ثلاث ركعات بتسليمة واحدة وقنوت في الثالثة، وبه فارق المغرب كما فارقها بوجوب قراءة الفاتحة، والسورة في الثالثة قوله : ( وروي عنه أنه سنة) وهي الرواية الثانية. قوله : ( وروي عنه أنه فرض) وهي الرواية الأولى عنه وبها قال الشيخ علم الدين السخاوي المقري وعمل فيه جزا، وساق الأحاديث الدالة على فرضيته ثم قال ولا يرتاب ذوقهم بعد هذا كذا في الشرح قوله : ووفق المشايخ الخ) هذا التوفيق لبعضهم، وأما من لم يوفق بهذا التوفيق، وحمل الوجوب على حقيقته المصطلح عليها فيرد عليه إفساد صلاة الفجر بتذكره والواجب ليس كذلك، ويمكن دفع الأشكال بما ذكره صاحب الكشف في التحقيق أن الواجب نوعان: واجب في قوة الفرض كالوتر عند الإمام حتى منع تذكره صحة الفجر كتذكر العشاء، وواجب دون الفرض في العمل فوق السنة كتعين الفاتحة حتى وجب سجود السهو بتركه ولكن لا يفسد الصلاة اهـ،
ان
وجوبه لا
وذكر الكمال أن الفرض العملي أعلى قسمي الواجب، وبه يظهر آخر، جمع ، وهو أن المراد بالواجب الفرض العملي، ويكون هو المراد لمن عبر بالوجوب مقتصراً، واندفع الإشكال، وأما القول بالسنية : فهو مرجوح إن لم يحمل على الحمل المذكور، واعلم يختص بالبعض دون البعض، بل يعم الناس كلهم من رقيق وأنثى، وغيرهما بعد كونهم أهلاً للوجوب، وحديث الإعرابي حيث قال هل على غيرها أي الخمس فقال : لا إلا أن تطوع لا يدل على عدم وجوب الوتر لأنه كان أول الإسلام، ثم وجب الوتر بعده. قوله : (واجب اعتقاداً) ينافيه ما في البحر من قوله واعتقاد الوجوب لا يجب على الحنفي، ويجاب بأن المراد أنه يجري عليه حكم الواجب في الاعتقاد بحيث إذا أنكر افتراضه لا يكفر . قوله : (والأمر ) أي الضمني المأخوذ من الحديث المذكور، أو الأمر الذي في قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم إن الله زادكم
Chapter of Witr and its rulings. When he finished explaining the theoretical obligation (fard 'ilmi), he started on the practical. Witr linguistically means the odd number, opposite of even (shaf'), with fath or kasr. In Sharia, it is a specific prayer. He described it by saying: 'Witr is obligatory (wajib) according to the most correct view, and it is the last of Imam's statements. And it is narrated from him that it is sunnah, and that is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And it is narrated from him that it is fard. And the mashayikh reconciled the reports by [considering it] fard in practice. And it is a wajib that is not abandoned in belief, so its denier is not declared a disbeliever. It is sunnah in terms of evidence, because it is proven by a solitary report. The basis of obligation is his statement (s): 'Witr is a right; whoever does not perform witr is not from me' – narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Hakim and authenticated. And the command... [Commentary:] His saying: 'When he finished explaining the theoretical fard' meaning the creedal one which the denier becomes a disbeliever; he started on the practical, meaning what is obligatory to do, not to believe. His saying: 'a specific prayer' – it is three rak'ahs with one taslim and qunut in the third, and by this it differs from Maghrib, as it also differs by requiring recitation of Fatiha and a sura in the third. His saying: 'and it is narrated from him that it is sunnah' – that is the second narration. His saying: 'and it is narrated from him that it is fard' – that is the first narration from him, and it is the view of Shaykh 'Alam al-Din al-Sakhawi al-Muqri', who acted upon it and cited hadiths indicating its fardiyyah, then said: 'No one with understanding will doubt after this.' So in the sharh. His saying: 'and the mashayikh reconciled...' – this reconciliation is for some. As for those who did not reconcile with this, and interpreted 'wajib' in its technical sense, they would face the objection that it spoils Fajr prayer if one remembers it during Fajr, whereas wajib does not do that. The objection can be repelled by what the author of al-Kashf mentioned in al-Tahqiq: that wajib is of two types: wajib with the strength of fard, like witr according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), such that its remembrance invalidates Fajr prayer like the remembrance of Isha; and wajib below fard in practice, above sunnah, like the specification of Fatiha, such that sajda al-sahw becomes obligatory for omitting it, but it does not spoil the prayer. End. And al-Kamal mentioned that the practical fard is the higher of the two types of wajib, and by this another reconciliation appears: that what is meant by 'wajib' is the practical fard, and it is what is meant by those who simply said 'obligatory' (wajib), and the problem is resolved. As for the view that it is sunnah, it is preponderated against unless interpreted as mentioned. And know that it is not specific to some, but applies to all people, slave and free, female and others, as long as they are eligible for obligation. And the hadith of the Bedouin when he asked 'Is there any other besides them (the five)?' and he said 'No, except if you volunteer' does not indicate that witr is not obligatory, because that was in early Islam, then witr was made obligatory later. His saying: 'obligatory in belief' – this contradicts what is in al-Bahr: 'And belief in obligation is not obligatory upon the Hanafi.' The response is that what is meant is that it is treated like a wajib in belief, so that if one denies its being fard, he is not declared a disbeliever. His saying: 'and the command' – i.e., the implicit command taken from the aforementioned hadith, or the command in his saying: 'Indeed Allah has increased you...'
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on witr prayer and discusses its legal status. The Hanafi school is known for considering witr as wajib (obligatory), but not fard. The text reports three positions transmitted from Abu Hanifa: (1) it is wajib (the most correct and last view), (2) it is sunnah (the view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and (3) it is fard (an earlier view). The mashayikh reconciled by saying that witr is 'fard 'amali' (practical obligation) – meaning it is obligatory to perform, but not obligatory to believe in its obligation; thus one who denies its obligation is not a disbeliever. The hadith 'Witr is a right...' is cited as the proof for its binding nature. The commentary further explains that wajib can be of two types: one as strong as fard (like witr, which even spoils Fajr prayer if remembered during it) and one below fard (like reciting Fatiha, which requires sajda al-sahw if omitted). The text also addresses the objection from the hadith of the Bedouin where the Prophet mentioned only five prayers, explaining that witr became obligatory later. Finally, it clarifies that witr is obligatory on all Muslims, free or slave, male or female.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after Isha, consisting of three rak'ahs with one taslim and qunut.
الفرض العملي (al-fard al-'amali): Practical obligation: an act that must be performed but denial of its obligation does not render one a disbeliever because the proof is zanni.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the status of witr prayer?
A) Sunnah mu'akkada
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school considers witr wajib (obligatory) in practice, not fard in belief, and this ruling is based on a strong hadith and the principle of fard 'amali.

Salah — Prayer

Witr Prayer: Obligation, Modality, and Recitation Rules
Commentary on the core rulings of Witr prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the obligation of Witr, its rak'ah count, and the required recitations, distinguishing wajib from non-obligatory elements.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib in Hanafi law: three rak'ahs, one taslim, Fatiha and surah in each, with a tashahhud-only sitting after two.

In this passage from al-Tahtawi's hashiyah, we examine the foundational rulings of the Witr prayer. The commentator clarifies that Witr is a wajib prayer in the Hanafi school, performed as three rak'ahs with a single taslim. He details the obligatory recitations and the specific sitting, and notes that one does not open the third rak'ah with a new istiftah. This lesson will walk through these rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the status of Witr
The passage begins by affirming that Witr is wajib. Look at the word 'حق' (right) which implies obligation in Hanafi terminology. The commentator uses the matn's wording to derive this.
Hanafi: wajib, not fard, because the evidence is zanni.
2
Note the number of rak'ahs and taslim
The hadith of the Prophet: he prayed Witr with three rak'ahs and gave taslim only at the end. This establishes the modal for the Hanafi school.
The hadith is authenticated by al-Hakim.
3
Recognize the recitation obligations
In each rak'ah, reciting Fatiha and a surah is wajib. The specific surahs (Al-A'la, Al-Kafirun, Al-Ikhlas) are recommended but not obligatory; the Mu'awwidhatain may be used occasionally.
The hadith of Aisha shows occasional use, not permanent obligation.
4
Understand the sitting after two rak'ahs
Sitting after the second rak'ah is wajib, and only tashahhud is recited (no salawat) because the prayer has a semblance of obligatory nature at that point.
The tashahhud itself is wajib in Hanafi prayer.
5
Observe the ruling on opening supplication
When standing for the third rak'ah, one does not recite the opening supplication (istiftah) because it is not the start of a new prayer—the three rak'ahs are a single unit.
This distinguishes Witr from a series of separate prayers.

قوله : (كالمستغيث من الشيء) كأنه يدفعه عن نفسه. قوله : (ودعاء تضرع) كأن يقول اللهم إني عبدك الذليل الحقير المنكسر خاطره الخائف الوجل قوله : (ودعاء خفية) هذا إنما تحسن مقابلته لما سبق من جهة النطق وعدمه وإلا فدعاء السر لا يخرج عن الثلاثة قبله .
The Book of Prayer: And the word 'right' and 'upon' indicate obligation. (And) its quantity (i.e., Witr) is three rak'ahs, performing them with (one) taslim, because the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) used to pray Witr with three, not giving taslim except at the end of them. Al-Hakim authenticated it and said it is upon the condition of the two Shaykhs. (And he recites) obligatorily (in each rak'ah the Fatiha and a surah) because it is narrated that he (peace and blessings) recited in the first (after Fatiha) 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High,' and in the second 'Say, O disbelievers,' and in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One.' And he performed qunut before ruku'. And in the hadith of Aisha that she recited in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One' and the Mu'awwidhatain. So it is acted upon at some times, acting upon both hadiths, not as an obligation. (And he sits obligatorily at the end of the first two rak'ahs) because of the transmitted tradition (and confines himself to the tashahhud due to the semblance of obligatory nature). (And he does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third) because it is not the beginning of another prayer. And when he finishes reciting the surah in it (the third rak'ah), he raises his hands parallel to his ears as we presented, except when he is praying qada (making up) so that he is not seen as careless by raising his hands in front of those who see him. Then he says takbir (for transition to the state of supplication), and after the takbir he performs qunut standing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform qunut in Witr before ruku'. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa) he places his right hand on his left. From Abu Yusuf he raises them, as Ibn Mas'ud used to raise them to his chest with palms facing the sky. Faraj, the freed slave of Abu Yusuf, narrated: I saw my master Abu Yusuf, when he entered into qunut for Witr, raising his hands in supplication. Ibn Abi Imran said: Faraj is trustworthy. Al-Kamal said: Its justification is the general evidence of raising hands for supplication, but it is replied that it is specific to prayer, due to consensus that there is no raising in the tashahhud supplication. I say: there is consideration in this due to the athar of Ibn Mas'ud mentioned recently. And in al-Mabsut from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: Supplication is four types: supplication of desire—then he places the palms of his hands towards the sky; supplication of fear—then he places the backs of his hands towards his face, like one seeking refuge from something; supplication of humility—then he folds the little finger and ring finger, forms a ring with the thumb and middle finger, and points with the index finger; and hidden supplication—which is what one does in himself. As narrated, he performs qunut (before ruku' for the entire year, and does not perform qunut in other than Witr) except for Fajr, due to the saying of Anas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed qunut in Fajr after ruku', supplicating against some Arab tribes... then he abandoned it, indicating its abrogation. His saying: (In the presence of those who see him) whether in the mosque or elsewhere; if no one is with him, he raises, and in that his prayer of three rak'ahs indicates neglect, and it may be said that raising is even more indicative. His saying: (Then he says takbir) the takbir mentioned is narrated from Ali, Ibn Umar, al-Bara' ibn Azib, and Ibn Mas'ud. The wisdom in combining raising hands and takbir is to inform the excused (deaf and blind). His saying: (And after the takbir he performs qunut standing) once. So the imam in his third rak'ah does not perform qunut in what he makes up (qada) because it is the beginning of his prayer. If a latecomer catches the imam in the ruku' of the third, he catches qunut, so he does not perform qunut in what he makes up. As in al-Fath. His saying: (According to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Abu Yusuf, and it is the most correct. Muhammad said: he lets them hang, as passed in the chapter on manner. Al-Tahawi and al-Karkhi chose it as in al-Nahr and others. His saying: (From Abu Yusuf he raises them) In Jami' al-Fiqh: if he spreads his hands after finishing it (qunut) and wipes his face with them, his prayer is not invalidated. His saying: (Its justification) meaning the justification of Abu Yusuf's action. His saying: (Due to consensus...) The evidence is more specific than the claim. How not, when al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) says raising hands in qunut of Fajr, and there is no consensus except with him. His saying: (In it) meaning in the response by specification. His saying: (Supplication of desire) meaning indicative of it; and likewise for what follows. His saying: (Supplication of fear) like his saying: Our Lord, remove from us the punishment, indeed we are believers; Our Lord, avert from us the punishment of Hell. His saying: (Like one seeking refuge from something) as if he is repelling it from himself. His saying: (Supplication of humility) as if he says: O Allah, I am Your slave, the lowly, the despised, the humble in spirit, the fearful and frightened. His saying: (Hidden supplication) This is only appropriate in contrast to the previous regarding utterance and non-utterance; otherwise, secret supplication does not come out of the three types before it.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Witr prayer. The commentator clarifies that Witr is wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith of the Prophet praying three rak'ahs with one taslim. He explains that in each rak'ah, recitation of Fatiha and a surah is obligatory. The recommended surahs are: after Fatiha in first rak'ah: Surah al-A'la; second: Surah al-Kafirun; third: Surah al-Ikhlas. The hadith of Aisha adds the Mu'awwidhatain, but this is only occasional, not obligatory. The commentator then discusses the sitting after two rak'ahs (only tashahhud, no salawat). When standing for the third, one does not recite the opening supplication. After recitation in the third, one raises hands (except when praying qada' to avoid appearing careless) and says takbir, then performs qunut standing before ruku'. The hand position during qunut is disputed: Abu Hanifa says right hand on left; Abu Yusuf says both raised; Muhammad says they hang down. The most correct view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage also discusses types of supplication, and ends with clarification that qunut is only for Witr, not for Fajr, as the Prophet's qunut in Fajr was abrogated. The commentary refutes the Shafi'i view that hands are raised in qunut of Fajr, arguing that the consensus claimed is not valid.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): A prayer performed after Isha, consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs, specifically three in this text, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony recited in the sitting position, which in the context of Witr after two rak'ahs is limited to the tashahhud without additional blessings (salawat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on reciting the opening supplication (istiftah) when standing for the third rak'ah of Witr?
A) It is wajib to recite it.
B) It is sunnah to recite it.
C) It is not recited because the third rak'ah is not a separate prayer.
D) It is recited only if one forgets the qunut.

Key Takeaway
Witr is a wajib prayer of three rak'ahs with one taslim, requiring Fatiha and surah in each, and a tashahhud-only sitting after two.

Qunut in Witr: Hand Positions, Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf, and the Fajr Qunut Dispute
Commentary on qunut in Witr and related ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi rules for qunut in Witr, including the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on hand placement, and evaluate the cross-madhhab dispute regarding qunut of Fajr.

Core Idea
In Witr, perform qunut standing before ruku'; hands are placed right on left (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) – not raised, and Fajr qunut was abrogated.

The second part of al-Tahtawi's commentary focuses on the qunut supplication in Witr: its timing after raising hands and takbir, and the detailed intra-Hanafi disagreement on hand position during the supplication. The commentator also addresses the Shafi'i practice of raising hands in Fajr qunut, arguing that the Prophet's qunut in Fajr was abrogated. This lesson will dissect these issues and their practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Locate the qunut in the Witr prayer sequence
After reciting the surah in the third rak'ah, one raises hands to the ears, says takbir, and then performs qunut while standing.
Raising hands here is specific to the transition to qunut, not general raising.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on hand placement during qunut
Abu Hanifa: place right hand on left (as in normal standing). Abu Yusuf: raise both hands. Muhammad: let hands hang down. The mufta bihi is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (placing right on left).
The commentator says 'وعند الإمام أي وأبي يوسف وهو الأصح' (according to Imam and Abu Yusuf, it is the most correct).
3
Understand the types of supplication and hand positions
The passage quotes Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah on four types of du'a: du'a al-raghbah (palms up), du'a al-rahbah (backs of hands), du'a al-tadharru' (special finger positioning), and du'a al-khafiyah (silent). This provides a general fiqh of supplication postures.
This is not specific to Witr but is adab of du'a.
4
Analyze the cross-madhhab dispute on Fajr qunut
The Hanafi position: qunut only in Witr, not in Fajr, because the Prophet's qunut in Fajr was abrogated. The Shafi'i position: qunut in Fajr after ruku' is sunnah. The commentator refutes the Shafi'i evidence by arguing that the claimed consensus is invalid because al-Shafi'i opposes it.
The hadith of Anas about qunut on the reciters is used to argue abrogation.
5
Apply the ruling on latecomer catching qunut
If a latecomer catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah, he has caught the qunut and does not need to perform it in his qada' (make-up rak'ahs).
This is a practical extension from the text.

الصبح، ولا إجماع إلا به . قوله: (وفيه) أي في الجواب بالتخصيص. قوله : (دعاء رغبة) أي دال عليها وكذا يقال فيما بعده. قوله : ( ودعاء رهبة كقوله : ربنا اكشف عنا العذاب إنا مؤمنون ربنا اصرف عنا عذاب جهنم قوله : (كالمستغيث من الشيء) كأنه يدفعه عن نفسه. قوله : (ودعاء تضرع) كأن يقول اللهم إني عبدك الذليل الحقير المنكسر خاطره الخائف الوجل قوله : (ودعاء خفية) هذا إنما تحسن مقابلته لما سبق من جهة النطق وعدمه وإلا فدعاء السر لا يخرج عن الثلاثة قبله .
The Book of Prayer: And the word 'right' and 'upon' indicate obligation. (And) its quantity (i.e., Witr) is three rak'ahs, performing them with (one) taslim, because the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) used to pray Witr with three, not giving taslim except at the end of them. Al-Hakim authenticated it and said it is upon the condition of the two Shaykhs. (And he recites) obligatorily (in each rak'ah the Fatiha and a surah) because it is narrated that he (peace and blessings) recited in the first (after Fatiha) 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High,' and in the second 'Say, O disbelievers,' and in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One.' And he performed qunut before ruku'. And in the hadith of Aisha that she recited in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One' and the Mu'awwidhatain. So it is acted upon at some times, acting upon both hadiths, not as an obligation. (And he sits obligatorily at the end of the first two rak'ahs) because of the transmitted tradition (and confines himself to the tashahhud due to the semblance of obligatory nature). (And he does not recite the opening supplication when standing for the third) because it is not the beginning of another prayer. And when he finishes reciting the surah in it (the third rak'ah), he raises his hands parallel to his ears as we presented, except when he is praying qada (making up) so that he is not seen as careless by raising his hands in front of those who see him. Then he says takbir (for transition to the state of supplication), and after the takbir he performs qunut standing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform qunut in Witr before ruku'. According to Imam (Abu Hanifa) he places his right hand on his left. From Abu Yusuf he raises them, as Ibn Mas'ud used to raise them to his chest with palms facing the sky. Faraj, the freed slave of Abu Yusuf, narrated: I saw my master Abu Yusuf, when he entered into qunut for Witr, raising his hands in supplication. Ibn Abi Imran said: Faraj is trustworthy. Al-Kamal said: Its justification is the general evidence of raising hands for supplication, but it is replied that it is specific to prayer, due to consensus that there is no raising in the tashahhud supplication. I say: there is consideration in this due to the athar of Ibn Mas'ud mentioned recently. And in al-Mabsut from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah: Supplication is four types: supplication of desire—then he places the palms of his hands towards the sky; supplication of fear—then he places the backs of his hands towards his face, like one seeking refuge from something; supplication of humility—then he folds the little finger and ring finger, forms a ring with the thumb and middle finger, and points with the index finger; and hidden supplication—which is what one does in himself. As narrated, he performs qunut (before ruku' for the entire year, and does not perform qunut in other than Witr) except for Fajr, due to the saying of Anas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed qunut in Fajr after ruku', supplicating against some Arab tribes... then he abandoned it, indicating its abrogation. His saying: (In the presence of those who see him) whether in the mosque or elsewhere; if no one is with him, he raises, and in that his prayer of three rak'ahs indicates neglect, and it may be said that raising is even more indicative. His saying: (Then he says takbir) the takbir mentioned is narrated from Ali, Ibn Umar, al-Bara' ibn Azib, and Ibn Mas'ud. The wisdom in combining raising hands and takbir is to inform the excused (deaf and blind). His saying: (And after the takbir he performs qunut standing) once. So the imam in his third rak'ah does not perform qunut in what he makes up (qada) because it is the beginning of his prayer. If a latecomer catches the imam in the ruku' of the third, he catches qunut, so he does not perform qunut in what he makes up. As in al-Fath. His saying: (According to Imam (Abu Hanifa) and Abu Yusuf, and it is the most correct. Muhammad said: he lets them hang, as passed in the chapter on manner. Al-Tahawi and al-Karkhi chose it as in al-Nahr and others. His saying: (From Abu Yusuf he raises them) In Jami' al-Fiqh: if he spreads his hands after finishing it (qunut) and wipes his face with them, his prayer is not invalidated. His saying: (Its justification) meaning the justification of Abu Yusuf's action. His saying: (Due to consensus...) The evidence is more specific than the claim. How not, when al-Shafi'i (may Allah be pleased with him) says raising hands in qunut of Fajr, and there is no consensus except with him. His saying: (In it) meaning in the response by specification. His saying: (Supplication of desire) meaning indicative of it; and likewise for what follows. His saying: (Supplication of fear) like his saying: Our Lord, remove from us the punishment, indeed we are believers; Our Lord, avert from us the punishment of Hell. His saying: (Like one seeking refuge from something) as if he is repelling it from himself. His saying: (Supplication of humility) as if he says: O Allah, I am Your slave, the lowly, the despised, the humble in spirit, the fearful and frightened. His saying: (Hidden supplication) This is only appropriate in contrast to the previous regarding utterance and non-utterance; otherwise, secret supplication does not come out of the three types before it.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the rulings of Witr prayer. The commentator clarifies that Witr is wajib (obligatory) based on the hadith of the Prophet praying three rak'ahs with one taslim. He explains that in each rak'ah, recitation of Fatiha and a surah is obligatory. The recommended surahs are: after Fatiha in first rak'ah: Surah al-A'la; second: Surah al-Kafirun; third: Surah al-Ikhlas. The hadith of Aisha adds the Mu'awwidhatain, but this is only occasional, not obligatory. The commentator then discusses the sitting after two rak'ahs (only tashahhud, no salawat). When standing for the third, one does not recite the opening supplication. After recitation in the third, one raises hands (except when praying qada' to avoid appearing careless) and says takbir, then performs qunut standing before ruku'. The hand position during qunut is disputed: Abu Hanifa says right hand on left; Abu Yusuf says both raised; Muhammad says they hang down. The most correct view is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The passage also discusses types of supplication, and ends with clarification that qunut is only for Witr, not for Fajr, as the Prophet's qunut in Fajr was abrogated. The commentary refutes the Shafi'i view that hands are raised in qunut of Fajr, arguing that the consensus claimed is not valid.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in the Witr prayer (and sometimes in Fajr), performed while standing before ruku'. In this passage, it includes specific hand positions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which hand position is considered the most correct (الأصح) for qunut in Witr?
A) Raising both hands, palms facing the sky
B) Placing the right hand on the left
C) Letting both hands hang down
D) Raising hands and then wiping the face

Key Takeaway
Perform qunut in Witr standing before ruku' with hands placed right on left (mufta bihi); do not raise hands in Fajr qunut as it was abrogated.

Hand Position During Qunut in Witr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on qunut in witr with intra-Hanafi hand position dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hand placement during qunut in witr, identify the intra-madhhab disagreement, and explain the tarjih (preferred view).

Core Idea
In witr, the hands are placed, not raised, according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Qunut in witr is a confirmed sunnah, but a subtle disagreement arose among the early Hanafi masters: should the hands be placed (as in standing) or raised (as in general supplication)? This lesson examines the arguments of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the critique by later commentators, and the final tarjih that settles the practice for the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening lines: qunut in witr is performed before ruku. Determine its hukm level – it is a sunnah muakkadah.
The text states 'qunita qā’iman' (perform qunut standing) and that the Prophet did so before ruku.
2
Locate the intra-Hanafi dispute
Find the two positions: Abu Hanifa says place right over left; Abu Yusuf says raise the hands. Note the evidence each uses.
Abu Yusuf's proof is from the general practice of raising hands for du'a and the action of Ibn Mas'ud.
3
Analyze the author's critique
The commentator (al-Tahtawi) responds to the claim that raising hands is general by restricting it to outside prayer, citing consensus (ijma') on no raising in tashahhud.
He says this is debatable due to the narration of Ibn Mas'ud, but ultimately the relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's.
4
Extract the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: whether the congregation raises hands or not. The text clearly gives precedence to Abu Hanifa's view (hands placed).
Al-Tahtawi states that the ashah (most correct) is the position of not raising.

Source Text

ثم كبر لانتقاله إلى حالة الدعاء (و) بعد التكبير (قنت قائماً) لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يقنت في الوتر قبل الركوع وعند الإمام يضع يمينه على يساره وعن أبي يوسف يرفعهما كما كان ابن مسعود يرفعهما إلى صدره وبطونهما إلى السماء روى فرج مولى أبي يوسف قال : رأيت مولاي أبا يوسف إذا دخل في القنوت للوتر رفع يديه في الدعاء قال ابن أبي عمران فرج : ثقة قال الكمال : ووجهه عموم دليل الرفع للدعاء، ويجاب بأنه مخصوص ليس في الصلاة للإجماع على أنه لا رفع في دعاء التشهد اهـ قلت وفيه نظر لأثر ابن مسعود الذي تقدم قريباً، وفي المبسوط عن محمد بن الحنفية قال : الدعاء أربعة دعاء رغبة ففيه يجعل بطون كفيه إلى السماء ودعاء رهبة ففيه يجعل ظهر كفيه إلى وجهه كالمستغيث من الشيء، ودعاء تضرع ففيه يعقد الخنصر والبنصر ، ويحلق الإبهام والوسطى، ويشير بالسبابة ودعاء خفية وهو ما يفعله المرء في نفسه كذا في معراج الدراية ولما رويناه يقنت (قبل الركوع في جميع السنة ولا يقنت في غير الوتر)
Then he says takbir for transitioning to the state of supplication, and after the takbir he performs qunut while standing, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to perform qunut in witr before ruku. According to Imam [Abu Hanifa], he places his right hand over his left; from Abu Yusuf, he raises them as Ibn Mas'ud used to raise them to his chest with the palms facing the sky. Faraj, the freed slave of Abu Yusuf, narrated: I saw my master Abu Yusuf when he entered into qunut for witr, he raised his hands in supplication. Ibn Abi Imran said: Faraj is trustworthy. Al-Kamal said: Its reasoning is the general evidence of raising hands for supplication. It is answered that it is specific to being outside prayer due to consensus that there is no raising of hands in the supplication of tashahhud. I (the commentator) say: This is debatable due to the narration of Ibn Mas'ud mentioned earlier. In al-Mabsut, from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, he said: Supplication is four types: supplication of desire (ragba) — in it the palms are turned towards the sky; supplication of fear (rahba) — in it the backs of the hands are turned towards the face, like one seeking refuge from something; supplication of humility (tadarru') — in it the little finger and ring finger are clenched, the thumb and middle finger form a ring, and the index finger points; and hidden supplication (khafiyya) — it is what a person does within himself. Thus is it in Miraj al-Diraya. And because of what we narrated: he performs qunut before ruku in the entire year, and he does not perform qunut other than in witr.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of qunut in witr and an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding hand placement during the supplication. The central ruling is that qunut in witr is performed before ruku, as established by the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The text then presents the difference between Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf: Abu Hanifa holds that the hands should be placed as in standing (right over left), while Abu Yusuf holds that they should be raised for supplication, based on the general evidence of raising hands during du'a and the practice of Ibn Mas'ud. The author (al-Tahtawi) critiques the argument that raising hands is confined to outside prayer, pointing to the narration of Ibn Mas'ud. The passage then quotes Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah's classification of four types of supplication and the corresponding hand gestures: for desire (ragba) palms up, for fear (rahba) palms facing the face, for humility (tadarru') specific finger positioning, and for hidden supplication (khafiyya) no external gesture. The lesson concludes by affirming that qunut is only performed in witr, not in other prayers.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in a standing posture during witr prayer.
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during qunut supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the position of the hands during qunut in witr?
A) Hands must be raised
B) Hands are placed, right over left
C) Hands are dropped by the sides
D) It is left to personal choice

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qunut in witr is performed before ruku with hands placed (right over left); raising them is a weaker view within the school.

Qunut in Fajr: Calamity-Only vs. Daily Sunnah
Dispute on qunut in Fajr and its permissibility for calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on qunut in Fajr, distinguish it from the Shafi'i position, and evaluate the evidence from the hadith of Anas.

Core Idea
Qunut in Fajr is abrogated according to the Hanafi school; it is only performed during calamities.

The practice of qunut (supplication) in the Fajr prayer has been a point of contention between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. While the Shafi'is consider it a daily sunnah, the Hanafis hold that it was abrogated after the Prophet ﷺ discontinued it following the raid on the reciters. However, the Hanafis do permit qunut in Fajr (and other audible prayers) when a calamity (nāzila) strikes. This lesson examines the key evidences and arguments behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school holds regarding qunut in Fajr: it is not a regular sunnah; it is only performed when a calamity (nāzila) occurs.
The muftā bihī position is clear: no qunut in Fajr without a calamity.
2
Identify the opposing school and their view
Recognize that the Shāfi‘ī school (and a large group of hadith scholars) consider qunut in Fajr as sunnah mu’akkadah, performed daily.
The source text mentions 'جمهور أهل الحديث' as supporters of this view.
3
Follow the Hanafi proof
Examine the hadith of Anas: the Prophet performed qunut in Fajr for a specific reason (against the tribes Ril, Dhakwan, ‘Usayyah) and then abandoned it, indicating abrogation (naskh). Also note the incident of ‘Alī when people disapproved of his qunut.
The Prophet’s abandonment is argued to be permanent, not just due to absence of a new calamity.
4
Analyse the opponent's proof and the Hanafi response
Understand the opponent’s argument: the Prophet’s abandonment was because the calamity ended, not because the act was abrogated. The Hanafi response: if it were a regular sunnah, the Prophet would have continued it; his abandonment and the absence of later practice confirms abrogation.
The source text also mentions that Imām al-Ṭaḥāwī restricts qunut to calamities.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Shāfi‘īs recite qunut in Fajr every day; Hanafis do not, except when a general calamity befalls the Muslims.
This difference affects daily practice and communal response during crises.

Source Text

وهو الصبح لقول أنس: قنت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم في الصبح بعد الركوع يدعو على أحياء من العرب رعل وذكوان وعصية حين قتلوا القراء وهم سبعون أو ثمانون رجلاً، ثم تركه لما ظهر عليهم فدل على نسخه وروى ابن أبي شيبة لما قنت علي رضي الله عنه في الصبح أنكر الناس عليه ذلك فقال : إنما استنصرنا على عدونا، وفي الغاية : إن نزل بالمسلمين نازلة قنت الإمام في صلاة الجهر وهو قول الثوري وأحمد، وقال جمهور أهل الحديث القنوت عند النوازل مشروع في الصلوات كلها اهـ، فعدم قنوت النبي في الفجر بعد ظفره بأولئك لعدم حصول نازلة تستدعي القنوت الله بعدها، فتكون مشروعيته مستمرة، وهو محمل قنوت من قنت من الصحابة رضي الله عنهم بعد وفاته وهو مذهبنا وعليه الجمهور وقال الإمام أبو جعفر الطحاوي رحمه الله تعالى : إنما لا يقنت عندنا في الفجر من غير بلية فإن وقعت فتنة أو بلية فلا بأس به فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أي بعد الركوع كما تقدم والقنوت) من (معناه الدعاء) في الوتر (وهو)
And it is Fajr, due to the saying of Anas: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed qunut in Fajr after ruku, supplicating against some Arab tribes—Ril, Dhakwan, and 'Usayyah—when they killed the reciters, who were seventy or eighty men. Then he abandoned it when he overcame them, which indicates its abrogation. Ibn Abi Shaybah narrated: When Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) performed qunut in Fajr, the people disapproved of that, so he said: 'We only sought victory against our enemy.' And in al-Ghayah: If a calamity befalls the Muslims, the imam performs qunut in the audible prayer; this is the saying of al-Thawri and Ahmad. The majority of hadith scholars said: Qunut at calamities is legislated in all prayers. So the Prophet's abandoning qunut in Fajr after his victory over those people was because there was no calamity that necessitated qunut thereafter; therefore its legislation is ongoing. This is the interpretation of the qunut of those who performed qunut from the Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) after his death, and this is our school and the majority. Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: We only do not perform qunut in Fajr without a calamity; if a trial or calamity occurs, then there is no harm in doing it, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did it after ruku as previously mentioned. And qunut) in its meaning is supplication in witr, and it is...
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This passage addresses the controversial issue of qunut in the Fajr prayer. The Hanafi school's position is that qunut in Fajr is not a regular sunnah; it was performed by the Prophet (peace be upon him) for a specific reason (supplication against enemy tribes) and was later abandoned, indicating abrogation. However, the Hanafis do permit qunut in Fajr (and other audible prayers) if a calamity (nazila) befalls the Muslims, based on the practice of the Prophet and some Companions. This view is aligned with the majority of hadith scholars who consider qunut during calamities as legislated in all prayers, but the Hanafis restrict it to times of need. The passage narrates that when Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) performed qunut in Fajr, people objected, and he explained it was for seeking victory. Imam al-Tahawi clarifies that the Hanafi school does not perform qunut in Fajr without a calamity, but if one occurs, it is permissible. The passage also defines 'qunut' as 'supplication' (du'a), emphasizing that its essence is du'a.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): Supplication (du'a) in prayer; specifically here referring to qunut in Fajr.
النازلة (al-nazila): A calamity or trial that befalls the Muslims, justifying qunut.

The Hanafi Ruling on Qunut in Fajr During Calamities
Dispute on qunut in Fajr prayer during calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qunut in Fajr and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice that restricts it to times of calamity.

Core Idea
Qunut in Fajr is tied to calamity — no calamity, no qunut.

This lesson examines a key difference between the Hanafi school and other scholars regarding qunut in the Fajr prayer. The Hanafi position, as explained in this passage, permits qunut only during a calamity (nazilah), while some schools perform it regularly. We will analyze the incident of 'Ali (ra) and the reasoning behind the Hanafi view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act in question? Performing qunut (supplication) after bowing in the last rak'ah of Fajr. The Hanafis rule it as sunnah muakkadah only during a calamity, otherwise it is not performed.
2
Note the Hanafi position and its evidence
The Hanafi position is that qunut in Fajr is not performed without a calamity. The evidence includes the incident of 'Ali (ra) and the fact that the Prophet (saw) did not perform qunut after victory because there was no calamity. This indicates the continuation of the permission.
3
Understand the opposing school's view
Al-Thawri, Ahmad, and the majority of hadith scholars hold that qunut during calamities is prescribed in all prayers, or generally in Fajr without restriction. The passage notes this as the view of 'the majority of hadith scholars'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to the opposing proof
The Hanafis argue that the Prophet's omission of qunut after victory does not abrogate the practice; it was simply because there was no calamity at that time. Therefore, the general permission continues, as shown by the Companions who performed qunut after his death.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
In practice, a Hanafi imam will only perform qunut in Fajr when a calamity afflicts the Muslims. An imam from another school might do it regularly. This affects congregational prayer expections.

شيبة لما قنت علي رضي الله عنه في الصبح أنكر الناس عليه ذلك فقال : إنما استنصرنا على عدونا، وفي الغاية : إن نزل بالمسلمين نازلة قنت الإمام في صلاة الجهر وهو قول الثوري وأحمد، وقال جمهور أهل الحديث القنوت عند النوازل مشروع في الصلوات كلها اهـ، فعدم قنوت النبي في الفجر بعد ظفره بأولئك لعدم حصول نازلة تستدعي القنوت الله بعدها، فتكون مشروعيته مستمرة، وهو محمل قنوت من قنت من الصحابة رضي بعد وفاته وهو مذهبنا وعليه الجمهور وقال الإمام أبو جعفر الطحاوي رحمه الله تعالى : إنما لا يقنت عندنا في الفجر من غير بلية فإن وقعت فتنة أو بلية فلا بأس به فعله رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أي بعد الركوع كما تقدم والقنوت من معناه الدعاء في الوتر (وهو) الذي روي عن ابن مسعود أشار به إلى أن فيه روايات أخر
When Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) performed qunut in the morning prayer, the people disapproved of that. He said: 'We are just seeking victory over our enemy.' And in al-Ghayah: If a calamity befalls the Muslims, the imam performs qunut in the loud prayer. This is the saying of al-Thawri and Ahmad. The majority of the people of hadith said: Qunut during calamities is prescribed in all prayers. So the Prophet's not performing qunut in Fajr after his victory over those [enemies] was due to the absence of a calamity that would necessitate qunut afterwards. Thus its prescription is continuous. That is the interpretation of the qunut of those Companions who performed it after his death, and it is our madhhab and the opinion of the majority. Imam Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: According to us, qunut is not performed in Fajr without a calamity. If a trial or calamity occurs, then there is no harm in it, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did it after bowing as previously mentioned. Qunut (from its meaning is supplication) in Witr (and it is) that which is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud, indicating that there are other narrations.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi ruling on qunut in the Fajr prayer during calamities. It begins by citing the incident when 'Ali (ra) performed qunut in Fajr and was criticized. He justified it as a prayer for victory. The author then presents the position of al-Ghayah that if a calamity afflicts Muslims, the imam performs qunut in the loud prayer, which is also the view of al-Thawri and Ahmad. The majority of hadith scholars, however, hold that qunut is prescribed in all prayers during calamities. The passage then provides a reasoning: the Prophet (saw) did not perform qunut in Fajr after his victory over the hostile tribes because there was no calamity at that time; thus the general permissibility of qunut continues. This interpretation explains why some Companions performed qunut after the Prophet's death. This is the Hanafi position and the view of the majority. Then it quotes al-Tahawi, who specifies that qunut is not done in Fajr without a calamity, but during a trial it is allowed, as the Prophet did it after bowing. The passage concludes by noting that qunut linguistically means supplication, and it is performed in Witr, with the specific wording narrated from Ibn Mas'ud.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): Supplication, specifically in prayer; in this context, the du'a recited after bowing in the last rak'ah during times of calamity.
النازلة (al-nazilah): A calamity or affliction that befalls the Muslim community.

The Legal Conditions of Repentance (Tawbah) in the Hanafi School
Defines tawbah and its legal pillars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three pillars of tawbah and explain the additional condition of restitution for sins against others.

Core Idea
Valid repentance requires regret, immediate cessation, resolve not to return, and restitution of others' rights.

The qunut supplication includes the plea 'we repent to You.' The classical Hanafi commentary unpacks this into a precise legal definition of repentance (tawbah), specifying its pillars and conditions. Understanding this definition is crucial for proper guidance in confession and spiritual reform.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pillars of tawbah
The text states three pillars: regret (al-nadam), immediate abstention (al-iqla‘ an al-dhanb fi al-hal), and resolve not to return (al-‘azm ‘ala tark al-‘awd). Locate each in the commentary.
Regret is described as the greatest pillar.
2
Note the condition for sins against others
The passage adds that if the sin involves another person's rights (e.g., property, honor), repentance requires seeking forgiveness and making restitution. This is a mandatory condition for validity.
3
Examine the scholarly dispute on the third pillar
Ibn ‘Arabi argued that the resolve not to return is unnecessary because the future is unseen. The commentator refutes this by distinguishing between the unseen return and the present intention. This shows Hanafi insistence on all three pillars.
4
Relate the definition to the Hanafi position on faith
The commentary mentions that faith includes speech and action, linking tawbah to the Hanafi theological framework. This reinforces that tawbah is an act that requires both internal and external components.
5
Apply the definition to a scenario
Given a case of theft, check: Has the person regretted? Have they stopped? Have they resolved never to steal again? Have they returned the stolen item? If any is missing, repentance is incomplete.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باللفظ الذي روي عن ابن مسعود أن يقول اللهم إنا نستعينك ونستهديك ونستغفرك ونتوب إليك ونؤمن بك ونتوكل عليك ونثني عليك الخير كله نشكرك ولا نكفرك ونخلع ونترك من يفجرك. اللهم إياك نعبد ولك نصلي ونسجد وإليك نسعى ونحفد نرجو رحمتك ونخشى عذابك إن عذابك بالكفار ملحق. وكذلك ذكرها الجلال السيوطي في الدر المنثور بألفاظ مختلفة. قوله: (أن يقول اللهم الخ) ذكر السيوطي أن دعاء القنوت من جملة الذي أنزله الله على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وكانا سورتين كل سورة ببسملة وفواصل إحداهما تسمى سورة الخلع وهي بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم إنا نستعينك إلى قوله من يكفرك والأخرى تسمى سورة الحقد وهي بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم اللهم إياك نعبد إلى ملحق، وقد اختلفت الصحابة في نسخهما وكتبهما أبي في مصحفه فعدة سور القرآن عنده وست عشرة سورة. قوله: أي نطلب منك الهداية لما يرضيك المراد من الهداية الوصول لا الدلالة فقط. قوله: ستر عيوبنا الأولى ستر ذنوبنا لأن العيب قد لا يكون ذنبا كالعور، والشلل اللهم إلا أن يقال المراد ما يعيب الشارع عليه، والستر إما بالمحو من الصحيفة أو بعدم المؤاخذة به وإن بقي فيها والأول أرجح. قوله: فلا تفضحنا بفتح التاء والحاء المهملة. قوله: وشرعا الندم وهو أعظم أركانها قوله والإقلاع عنه في الحال أي إن كانت آلة الفعل حاضرة كأن تاب عن السكر وآلته بين يديه فيريقه ويبعد آلته عنه. قوله: والعزم على ترك العود أفاد العارف ابن عربي أن هذا الشرط لا يلزم لأنه غيب فالأولى فيه التسليم، وفيه أن المغيب هو العود فلا ينافي طلب العزم على عدمه في التوبة. قوله: فلا بد من مسامحته وإرضائه أي برد الظلامة إليه إن أمكنه وإن لم يمكنه تصدق بقدرها إن كانت من الأموال، وقال بعضهم أن التوبة تصح عنها في المستقبل، ويكون ما عليه كالديون. قوله: ناطقين بلساننا هذا جرى فيه على أن الإيمان قول وعمل ونسب إلى الإمام أو هو بيان لشرطه الدنيوي الذي تجري عليه الأحكام الظاهرة قوله: فقلنا آمنا بك الخ لما كان الإيمان به تعالى لا يتم إلا بالإيمان بما ذكر بعد قال ذلك. قوله: وبما جاء عندك فيه أنه لا يعم الأنبياء فإن الإيمان بهم لازم. قوله: ورسلك المراد بهم قوله: وباليوم الآخر أي بوقوعه. قوله: وبالقدر خيره وشره القدر إيجاد الله تعالى الأشياء على وفق ما أراده تعالى وكله من الله تعالى وهو من هذه الجهة جميل، وإنما يقبح باكتساب العبد ونسبته إليه قوله: بتفويض الباء للتصوير. قوله: لعجزنا أي عن جلب نفعنا ودفع شرنا.
With the wording narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'O Allah, we seek Your help, we seek Your guidance, we seek Your forgiveness, and we repent to You, and we believe in You, and we rely on You, and we praise You with all goodness, we thank You and do not disbelieve in You, and we renounce and forsake those who disobey You. O Allah, You alone we worship, and to You we pray and prostrate, and towards You we strive and hasten, we hope for Your mercy and fear Your punishment; indeed, Your punishment will overtake the disbelievers.' Likewise, al-Suyuti mentioned it in al-Durr al-Manthur with different wordings. (Commentary:) His saying: 'to say: O Allah...' al-Suyuti mentioned that the qunut supplication is among what Allah revealed to the Prophet (peace be upon him), and they were two surahs, each with a basmalah and verses; one is called Surah al-Khal' (beginning with 'O Allah, we seek Your help' up to 'whoever disbelieves in You'), and the other called Surah al-Haqd (beginning with 'O Allah, You alone we worship' to the end). The Companions differed over their abrogation, and Ubayy included them in his mushaf, so the number of surahs of the Qur'an according to him was 116. His saying: 'We seek from You guidance to what pleases You' — the intended meaning of guidance is reaching, not just indication. His saying: 'Cover our faults' — the primary meaning is cover our sins, because a fault may not be a sin like being one-eyed or paralyzed, unless it is said that what is meant is what the Lawgiver considers blameworthy. And covering is either by erasing from the scroll or by not taking to account even if it remains, the first being more preponderant. His saying: 'so do not disgrace us' — with a fatha on the ta' and the ha'. His saying: 'and legally, regret' — it is the greatest of its pillars. His saying: 'and abstaining from it immediately' — i.e., if the instrument of the act is present, like if he repents from drinking and the vessel is before him, he pours it out and removes the vessel. His saying: 'and resolve not to return' — al-‘Arif Ibn ‘Arabi stated that this condition is not necessary because it is the unseen, so it is better to submit. But it is argued that what is unseen is the return, so it does not contradict seeking resolve against it in repentance. His saying: 'so it is necessary to forgive him and satisfy him' — i.e., by returning the wrongdoing to him if possible; if not possible, he gives charity equal to its value if it is wealth. Some scholars said that repentance is valid for it in the future, and it becomes like a debt. His saying: 'uttering with our tongues' — this proceeds on the basis that faith is speech and action, attributed to Imam Abu Hanifa, or it is an explanation of its worldly condition by which the apparent rulings are applied. His saying: 'so we said we believe in You, etc.' — because faith in Him is not complete except with faith in what is mentioned after. His saying: 'and in what came from You' — it does not include the prophets, for faith in them is obligatory. His saying: 'and Your messengers' — they are meant. His saying: 'and in the Last Day' — i.e., its occurrence. His saying: 'and in destiny, its good and bad' — destiny is Allah's creation of things according to His will; it is all from Allah and beautiful in this respect, and it is only considered evil by the acquisition of the servant and its attribution to him. His saying: 'by delegation' — the ba' is for illustration. His saying: 'due to our inability' — i.e., to bring benefit and ward off harm from ourselves.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage provides the full wording of the qunut supplication as narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (ra), followed by detailed commentary on its phrases. The commentator begins by noting that al-Suyuti in al-Durr al-Manthur recorded that the qunut du'a was revealed as two separate surahs (al-Khal' and al-Haqd) with basmalah and verses, and that the Companions differed over their abrogation; Ubayy included them in his mushaf, making the total number of surahs 116. The commentator then explains each phrase: 'We seek Your help' means asking for assistance in obedience; 'guidance' means being led to what pleases Allah (reaching, not just indication); 'forgiveness' means covering sins (the best interpretation is erasing from the record); 'repentance' (tawbah) legally requires regret, immediate cessation if the means are present, and resolve not to return (though Ibn ‘Arabi noted that the latter is not strictly necessary as it pertains to the unseen). The condition of restoring rights of others requires returning the wrong if possible, otherwise giving charity. The phrase 'we believe in You' implies verbal confirmation and is explained as the basis for the worldly rulings of faith (following the Hanafi definition of faith as speech and action). The phrases about praising, thanking, and renouncing those who disobey are straightforward. The explanation of 'destiny' clarifies that its evil is only due to the servant's acquisition, not from Allah's creation. Finally, 'we rely on You' means delegating affairs due to our inability to benefit or harm ourselves. The commentary reinforces the Hanafi theological positions (e.g., faith is speech and action, qadr is not evil in itself) and clarifies the legal implications of tawbah.

Key Terms
التوبة (al-tawbah): Legally, regret for past sin, immediate abstention, and resolve not to return; if it involves others' rights, they must be satisfied.
الهداية (al-hidayah): In the qunut, it means reaching (not just showing) what pleases Allah.
الستر (al-sitr): Covering sins, either by erasing from the record or by not taking to account; the first is more preponderant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Not punishing the sin
B) Erasing the sin from the record
C) Hiding the sin from people
D) Transforming the sin into good deeds

Key Takeaway
Valid repentance in the Hanafi school requires three pillars (regret, cessation, resolve) and, for sins against others, restitution.

Grammatical and Theological Commentary on 'Iyyaka Na'budu'
Linguistic commentary on qunut du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the grammatical parsing of the phrase 'wa nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr kullihi' and the theological concept that Allah's self-praise is the only adequate praise.

Core Idea
No one can fully praise Allah; only His own praise of Himself suffices.

This passage from al-Tahtawi's Hashiya unpacks the linguistic and theological layers of the qunut du'a. The commentator meticulously explains the grammar of each phrase, showing how the words emphasize that all praise is a favor from Allah, not an obligation. Understanding this deepens one's appreciation of the du'a in salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the du'a
Note that after a request, the du'a returns to praise (thana') and specifies worship for Allah's essence alone.
2
Parse 'khayr' as a masdar
In 'nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr kullihi', the word 'khayr' is interpreted as a verbal noun (masdar) meaning 'praise of goodness' for emphasis.
Alternatively, it could be the object of 'nuthni' or with a preposition removed.
3
Distinguish 'ifdalan' from wujub
'Ifdalan minka' means the blessing is a pure favor, not an obligation or necessity on Allah.
4
Analyze 'anta kama athnayta'
Multiple interpretations: the 'ka' as 'ala' (upon), as extra (za'ida), or as emphasis of the pronoun. All stress the inability of creation to properly praise Allah.
5
Unpack the metaphor of 'nakhla'u ribqat al-kufr'
The 'rope of disbelief' is everything displeasing to Allah; casting it off means dissociating from disbelief and its followers.
