اللهم إياك نعبد) عود للثناء وتخصيص لذاته بالعبادة أي قوله: (ونثني عليك الخير كله قال في المغرب والخير منصوب على المصدر أي ثناء الخير فيفيد نوعاً من التأكيد اهـ، أو على أنه مفعول نثني أو على نزع الخافض أي بالخير . قوله: (إفضالاً منك أي حال كونها إفضالاً أو لأجل الإفضال أي وليست بطريق الإيجاب ولا الوجوب . قوله : (بصرف جميع ما أنعمت به الخ) أشار به إلا أنه ليس تأكيد النثني بل تأسيس فتدبر. قوله: (أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك أنت مبتدأ، والكاف بمعنى على أي أنت على الوجه الذي أثنيت به على نفسك، أو الكاف زائدة أي أنت الذي أثنيت على نفسك، أو هو تأكيد للضمير المجرور بعلى أي لا نطيق ثناء عليك كثنائك على نفسك، أو المعنى أنت كالذي أثنيته على نفسك أي ثناؤك المعتبر هو كالثناء الذي أثنيت به على نفسك. قوله: (ونزيل ربقة الكفر) أي الكفر الشبيه بالربقة أي عروة الحبل، وظاهره أن مفعول نخلع محذوف، والذي يقتضيه اللفظ أن مفعوله قوله من يفجرك قوله : ( وريقة كل ما لا يرضيك) شبه ما لا يرضيه تعالى بشخص له حبل يضعه في العنق وإسناد الربقة تخييل. قوله : نتحاشى عنه) عطف على قوله نفارق . قوله : ( بأن نفرضه عدماً) الباء للسببية. قوله : (المتفضل) أخص من المنعم لأن المنعم قد ينعم لمقابلة نعم عليه قوله : (الموجود) أي وجوداً كاملاً وهو الواجب. قوله : (المستحق) أي الذي كل المحامد حقه. قوله : (والمخالف لهذا الخ) أي فنتركه، ولا نميل إليه هذه من جهة الدين، وأما النكاح فمن قبيل المعاملات فليس في تزوج الكتابية ميل إليها من الجهة. قال في الذخيرة : إذا دخل يهودي الحمام هل يباح للخادم المسلم أن يخدمه طمعاً في فلوسه، فلا بأس به، وإن فعل ذلك تعظيماً له إن كان ليميل قلبه إلى الإسلام، فلا بأس به وإن فعل ذلك تعظيماً له. غير أن من ينوي شيئاً مما ذكرناه كره ذلك، وكذا إذا دخل ذمي على مسلم شيئاً ينوي . فقام له إن قام طمعاً أ في ميله إلى الإسلام فلا بأس وإن فعل ذلك تعظيماً من غير أن مما ذكرناه، أو قام تعظيماً لغناه كره له ذلك اهـ.
'O Allah, You alone we worship' - this is a return to praise and specification of His Essence for worship, i.e., His saying: (and we praise You with all good). He said in al-Mughrib: 'al-khayr' is in the accusative as a verbal noun, i.e., we praise (thana') of goodness, which gives a kind of emphasis; or it is the object of 'nuthni', or with the removal of the preposition, i.e., with goodness. His saying: 'as favors from You' i.e., as a state of being favors, or for the purpose of favor, i.e., it is not by way of obligation or necessity. His saying: 'to spend all what You have bestowed, etc.' - he indicated by it that it is not an emphasis of 'nuthni' but a new assertion, so consider. His saying: 'You are as You have praised Yourself' - 'anta' is the subject, and the 'ka' is in the meaning of 'ala' (upon), i.e., You are upon the manner in which You praised Yourself; or the 'ka' is extra, i.e., You are the One who praised Yourself; or it is an emphasis of the pronoun in 'ala', i.e., we cannot encompass praise of You like Your praise of Yourself; or the meaning is: You are like the one I praised Yourself with, i.e., Your considered praise is like the praise with which You praised Yourself. His saying: 'and we remove the rope of disbelief' i.e., disbelief similar to the rope, i.e., the loop of the rope; apparently the object of 'nakhla'u' is omitted, but what the wording requires is that its object is 'man yafjuruka' (whoever disbelieves in You). His saying: 'and the rope is everything that does not please You' - he likened what does not please Allah Almighty to a person who has a rope placed around the neck, and the attribution of the rope is imaginative. His saying: 'we avoid him' - this is a conjunction to his saying 'we separate from'. His saying: 'by assuming him non-existent' - the 'ba' is for causation. His saying: 'the Bestower' - it is more specific than 'the Benefactor' because the benefactor may give in exchange for a favor upon him. His saying: 'the Existing' i.e., complete existence, which is the Necessary Being. His saying: 'the Deserving' i.e., to Whom all praises are due. His saying: 'and the one who opposes this, etc.' i.e., so we abandon him and do not incline towards him. This is with respect to religion. As for marriage, it is from the category of transactions (mu'amalat), so marrying a Kitabi woman does not constitute inclination towards her from this perspective. It is said in al-Dhakhira: If a Jew enters the bathhouse, is it permissible for a Muslim servant to serve him out of desire for his money? There is no harm in it. And if he does it to honor him, intending to incline his heart to Islam, there is no harm in it. However, if one intends anything other than what we have mentioned, it is disliked. Likewise, if a dhimmi enters upon a Muslim and he stands up for him, if he stands out of hope for his inclination to Islam, there is no harm; but if he does it out of honor without any of what we mentioned, or he stands to honor his wealth, it is disliked for him. End.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the qunut du'a, specifically the phrase 'Allahumma iyyaka na'budu' (O Allah, You alone we worship). The author explains that this is a return to praise (thana') and specifies worship for Allah's essence alone. The commentary then analyzes grammatical points: in 'nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr kullihi' (we praise You with all good), the word 'khayr' is interpreted as a verbal noun (masdar) meaning 'praise of goodness,' giving emphasis; alternatively it could be the object of 'nuthni' or with a preposition removed.

The phrase 'ifdalan minka' (as favors from You) is explained to mean that these praises and blessings are purely favors, not due to any obligation or necessity from Allah. The author notes that 'sarf jami' ma an'amta' (spending all what You have bestowed) is not simply a repetition of the earlier praise but a new assertion (ta'sis).

The commentary on 'anta kama athnayta 'ala nafsik' (You are as You have praised Yourself) offers multiple grammatical interpretations, emphasizing that no created being can fully praise Allah; only Allah can praise Himself adequately.

The metaphor of 'nakhla'u' (we cast off) is further explained: it means removing the 'ribqat al-kufr' (rope of disbelief) from our necks. The 'ribqah' is everything displeasing to Allah, likened to a halter. The apparent object of 'nakhla'u' is omitted, but the context requires that it be 'man yafjuruka' (whoever disbelieves in You). Thus, the du'a means we disassociate from disbelievers and their attributes, even considering them non-existent to exalt Allah.

The passage then transitions to a practical fiqh ruling from al-Dhakhira, dealing with social interactions with dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state). The issue: is it permissible for a Muslim servant to serve a Jewish person in a bathhouse? The ruling distinguishes intention: if the servant serves for the sake of gaining money (tama'an fi fulusihi), it is permissible (la ba'sa bihi). If he serves to honor the Jew with the intention of inclining his heart to Islam (li-yumila qalbahu ila al-Islam), it is also permissible. However, if he does it out of sheer respect (ta'ziman lahu) without any of these noble intentions, it becomes disliked (makruh). Similarly, if a dhimmi enters upon a Muslim, and the Muslim stands up for him, the ruling depends on intention: if he stands hoping for the dhimmi's conversion, it is allowed; if he stands to honor him purely or to honor his wealth, it is disliked. This shows the Hanafi school's nuanced approach: actions are judged by intentions, and interactions with non-Muslims are generally permissible if done for worldly or da'wah purposes, but avoided if they imply religious veneration.

Key Terms
الربقة (al-ribqah): The rope or halter; used metaphorically for the rope of disbelief (ribqat al-kufr) that is cast off from the neck of the believer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tahtawi's commentary, what is the grammatical function of 'al-khayr' in the phrase 'nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr kullihi'?
A) It is a subject.
B) It is a verbal noun (masdar) for emphasis.
C) It is a direct object.
D) It is a preposition.

Key Takeaway
The du'a 'iyyaka na'budu' is a return to praise, emphasizing that all praise is a favor from Allah and no one can praise Him adequately.

Hanafi Ruling on Serving a Dhimmi: Intention Matters
Practical fiqh ruling on interactions with dhimmis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on serving a dhimmi, distinguishing between permissible (mubah) and disliked (makruh) scenarios based on intention.

Core Idea
Serving a dhimmi is permissible for worldly gain or da'wah, but disliked if done purely out of respect.

This ruling from al-Dhakhira, cited by al-Tahtawi, addresses a practical social interaction: a Muslim servant working in a bathhouse when a Jewish (dhimmi) customer enters. The Hanafi school evaluates the act based on the servant's intention. This illustrates the broader principle that actions are judged by intentions (al-umur bi-maqasidiha).

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and the question
The scenario is a Jew entering a bathhouse where a Muslim servant works. The question: is it permissible to serve him?
2
Identify the three intentions
The text mentions three possible intentions: (1) desire for money (tama' fi flus), (2) desire to incline his heart to Islam (da'wah), (3) pure respect (ta'zim) without any noble intent.
3
Apply the ruling for each intention
For money: permissible (la ba'sa). For da'wah: permissible. For pure respect: disliked (makruh).
4
Extend the principle to standing
Similarly, if a dhimmi enters and a Muslim stands, it is permissible if intending da'wah, disliked if honoring purely or honoring his wealth.
5
Note the authority level
The ruling is from al-Dhakhira, a later Hanafi fatwa collection (fatawa mutakhkhirin), not from the core zahir al-riwayah texts.

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the qunut du'a, specifically the phrase 'Allahumma iyyaka na'budu' (O Allah, You alone we worship). The author explains that this is a return to praise (thana') and specifies worship for Allah's essence alone. The commentary then analyzes grammatical points: in 'nuthni 'alayka bi'l-khayr kullihi' (we praise You with all good), the word 'khayr' is interpreted as a verbal noun (masdar) meaning 'praise of goodness,' giving emphasis; alternatively it could be the object of 'nuthni' or with a preposition removed.

The phrase 'ifdalan minka' (as favors from You) is explained to mean that these praises and blessings are purely favors, not due to any obligation or necessity from Allah. The author notes that 'sarf jami' ma an'amta' (spending all what You have bestowed) is not simply a repetition of the earlier praise but a new assertion (ta'sis).

The commentary on 'anta kama athnayta 'ala nafsik' (You are as You have praised Yourself) offers multiple grammatical interpretations, emphasizing that no created being can fully praise Allah; only Allah can praise Himself adequately.

The metaphor of 'nakhla'u' (we cast off) is further explained: it means removing the 'ribqat al-kufr' (rope of disbelief) from our necks. The 'ribqah' is everything displeasing to Allah, likened to a halter. The apparent object of 'nakhla'u' is omitted, but the context requires that it be 'man yafjuruka' (whoever disbelieves in You). Thus, the du'a means we disassociate from disbelievers and their attributes, even considering them non-existent to exalt Allah.

The passage then transitions to a practical fiqh ruling from al-Dhakhira, dealing with social interactions with dhimmis (non-Muslim citizens of the Islamic state). The issue: is it permissible for a Muslim servant to serve a Jewish person in a bathhouse? The ruling distinguishes intention: if the servant serves for the sake of gaining money (tama'an fi fulusihi), it is permissible (la ba'sa bihi). If he serves to honor the Jew with the intention of inclining his heart to Islam (li-yumila qalbahu ila al-Islam), it is also permissible. However, if he does it out of sheer respect (ta'ziman lahu) without any of these noble intentions, it becomes disliked (makruh). Similarly, if a dhimmi enters upon a Muslim, and the Muslim stands up for him, the ruling depends on intention: if he stands hoping for the dhimmi's conversion, it is allowed; if he stands to honor him purely or to honor his wealth, it is disliked. This shows the Hanafi school's nuanced approach: actions are judged by intentions, and interactions with non-Muslims are generally permissible if done for worldly or da'wah purposes, but avoided if they imply religious veneration.

Key Terms
الذمي (al-dhimmi): A non-Muslim citizen living under Muslim rule, protected by the dhimma contract. In this text, the ruling applies to a Jew (yahudi) as a dhimmi.

The Opening Supplication (Thana): Meanings, Rules, and Balance of Hope and Fear
Critical refinement of the thana's meanings and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the meanings of the phrases in the opening supplication (thana) and identify which pronunciation changes invalidate the prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The thana is a sunnah praise of Allah; mispronouncing even one letter can invalidate the prayer if it changes meaning to foreign speech.

The opening supplication (thana) is a beloved sunnah that sets the tone for the prayer. This passage from al-Tahtawi's hashya on Maraqi al-Falah meticulously unpacks each phrase of the thana, clarifying its theological depth and legal import. Beyond the mere meanings, the commentary warns against a common pronunciation error that renders the prayer invalid, and it culminates in the critical principle of balancing hope and fear of Allah—a hallmark of Ahl al-Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the structure of the thana
Read the opening supplication as presented in the source (from 'We praise You with all good' to 'we are between hope and fear'). List the main components: praise, gratitude, renouncing disbelief, focusing worship on Allah, prayer, prostration, striving, hastening, hope, and fear.
The thana is not a single statement but a sequence of affirmations.
2
Analyze the key theological concepts
Focus on the definitions given: 'kufr' is the opposite of thankfulness, covering blessings by denial. 'Khala'' means casting off the rope of disbelief—i.e., renouncing anything displeasing to Allah. Note that the supplication asserts we do not deny any of Allah's blessings nor attribute them to others.
These definitions reinforce tawhid and gratitude.
3
Examine the rule on pronunciation change
The text states: 'If one substitutes the dal (د) with a dhal (ذ) in the word 'nahfid' (نحفد), his prayer becomes invalid because it becomes foreign speech with no meaning.' Identify the original word and the altered word, and understand that any change that produces meaningless speech invalidates prayer.
This is a specific example of a general principle: speaking foreign words intentionally or unintentionally that have no meaning in Arabic invalidates salat.
4
Understand the balance of hope and fear
The supplication ends with 'we hope for Your mercy and we fear Your punishment'. The commentary says 'this is an indication of the true school, for feeling secure from Allah's plan is disbelief.' Appreciate the middle path: hope and fear must coexist; overconfidence in mercy or despair from punishment are both blameworthy.
This principle is based on Quranic verses and hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة بصرف جميع ما أنعمت به الخ) أشار به إلا أنه ليس تأكيد النثني بل تأسيس فتدبر. ونثني عليك الخير (كله أي نمدحك بكل خير مقرين بجميع آلائك افضالاً منك (نشكرك) به من الجوارح إلى ما خلقته لأجله سبحانك لك الحمد لا نحصي ثناء عليك أنت كما أثنيت على نفسك ولا) نكفرك أي لا نجحد نعمة لك علينا، ولا نضيفها إلى غيرك الكفر نقيض الشكر، وأصله الستر يقال كفر النعمة إذا لم يشكرها كأنه سترها بجحوده وقولهم كفرت فلاناً على حذف مضاف والأصل كفرت بنعمته ومنه لا نكفرك ونخلع بثبوت حرف العطف أي نلقي ونطرح ونزيل ربقة الكفر من أعناقنا، وربقة كل ما لا يرضيك يقال خلع الفرس رسنه ألقاه ( ونترك) أي نفارق (من يفجرك) بجحده نعمتك وعبادته غيرك نتحاشى عنه وعن صفته بأن نفرضه عدماً تنزيهاً لجنابك إذ كل ذرة في الوجود شاهدة بأنك المنعم المتفضل الموجود المستحق لجميع المحامد الفرد المعبود، والمخالف لهذا هو الشقي المطرود (اللهم إياك نعبد) عود للثناء وتخصيص لذاته بالعبادة أي لا نعبد إلا إياك إذ تقديم المفعول للحصر (ولك نصلي أفردت الصلاة بالذكر لشرفها بتضمنها جميع العبادات ( ونسجد) تخصيص بعد تخصيص إذ هو أقرب حالات العبد Book of Prayer. He pointed with (spending all that You have bestowed) that it is not a confirmation of al-thenā but an establishment, so reflect. And we praise You with all good (i.e., we praise You with every good, acknowledging all Your favors as a favor from You. (We thank You) with the limbs for what You created them for. Glory be to You, Yours is praise; we cannot enumerate praise upon You; You are as You have praised Yourself). And (we do not) disbelieve You (i.e., we do not deny any blessing from You upon us, nor do we attribute it to other than You. Kufr is the opposite of thankfulness, and its origin is covering. It is said, 'he disbelieved the blessing' when he does not thank it, as if he covered it by his denial. Their saying 'we disbelieved so-and-so' is with an omitted genitive construction, the original being 'we disbelieved in his blessing'; from this is 'we do not disbelieve You'. And we cast off (with the conjunctive particle) i.e., we throw, discard, and remove the rope of disbelief from our necks; the rope is everything that displeases You. It is said, 'the horse cast off its halter' i.e., threw it. And (we leave) i.e., we separate from (whoever disobeys You) by denying Your blessing and worshiping other than You; we avoid him and his description by deeming him non-existent, to exalt Your presence, for every atom in existence witnesses that You are the Benefactor, the Bestower, the Existent, the Deserving of all praise, the Unique, the Worshipped; and whoever contradicts this is the wretched, the expelled. (O Allah, You alone we worship) a return to praise and specification of His essence with worship, i.e., we worship none but You, because advancing the object indicates restriction. (And to You we pray) prayer is mentioned specifically due to its honor of encompassing all acts of worship. (And we prostrate) a specification after specification, for it is the closest state of the servant to the Lord worshiped. (And to You we strive) and it is an indication to the hadith narrated from Him, exalted: 'Whoever comes to Me walking, I come to him running.' The meaning is: we exert effort in action to attain what brings us near to You. (And we hasten) we hasten in attaining Your worship with vigor, because 'hafd' means speed; hence servants are called 'hafadah' for their speed in serving their masters. It is with fatha on the nun, and it is permissible to have damma, with the unpointed ha and kasra of the fa, and the unpointed dal. It is said 'hafada' and 'ahfada' as a dialect. If one substitutes the dal with a pointed dhal, his prayer becomes invalid because it is foreign speech with no meaning. (We hope) i.e., we desire (Your mercy) i.e., its continuity, abundance, and the extent of Your giving by performing Your service and working in obedience to You, and You are Generous so You do not disappoint the one who hopes in You. And we fear Your punishment while avoiding what You have forbidden us, so we are not secure from Your scheme. Thus we are between hope and fear, and this is an indication of the true school, for feeling secure from Allah's plan is disbelief.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement (hashiya) from al-Tahtawi's commentary on Maraqi al-Falah, explaining the meanings and legal implications of phrases in the opening supplication (thana) of prayer. The commentary is a parsing exercise that breaks down each phrase to clarify its theological and legal significance. The author emphasizes that the thana is an act of praise and gratitude, defining key terms like kufr (disbelief) as the opposite of gratitude, and khala (casting off) as removing the rope of disbelief. The explanation of 'la nafkuruka' (we do not disbelieve You) highlights that disbelief is essentially ingratitude, and the supplication affirms we attribute all blessings to Allah alone. The phrase 'wa nakhla'u' (and we cast off) is interpreted as discarding anything displeasing to Allah. The text then discusses 'Allahumma iyyaka na'budu' (O Allah, You alone we worship), noting that advancing the object (iyyaka) indicates restriction, meaning we worship none but Him. The commentary distinguishes between worship and worldly transactions, citing from al-Dhakhirah that serving a Jew out of hope for money or to incline his heart to Islam is permissible, but if done out of veneration for his wealth, it is disliked. The explanation of 'wa laka nusalli' (and to You we pray) states that prayer is singled out for mention due to its honor of encompassing all acts of worship. 'Wa nasjudu' (and we prostrate) is a further specification because prostration is the closest state of the servant to his Lord. 'Wa ilayka nas'a' (and to You we strive) is linked to the hadith qudsi 'Whoever comes to Me walking, I come to him running,' meaning we exert effort in worship. 'Wa nahfidu' (and we hasten) is defined as speed, and altering the letter dal to dhal invalidates the prayer because it becomes meaningless speech. The supplication ends with hope and fear: we hope for Allah's mercy and fear His punishment, maintaining a balance between hope and fear, which is the correct path, as feeling secure from Allah's plan is disbelief. The entire text serves to clarify the precise meanings of the thana, reinforcing tawhid and proper adab in prayer.

Key Terms
ثناء (thana): The opening supplication in prayer, praising Allah.
كفر (kufr): Linguistically covering, legally ingratitude or disbelief; in this context, denying Allah's blessings.
خلع (khala'): To cast off or remove; here, discarding the rope of disbelief.
حفد (hafd): Haste or speed; in the supplication, to hasten in worship.
رجاء وخوف (raja' wa khawf): Hope for Allah's mercy and fear of His punishment; maintaining balance between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the consequence of substituting the letter dal (د) with dhal (ذ) in the word 'nahfid' (نحفد) during prayer?
A) The prayer becomes invalid because the meaning changes to a foreign word.
B) The prayer is still valid but compensation (sajdah sahw) is required.
C) The prayer is completely valid because the substitution is minor.
D) The prayer is invalid only if done intentionally.

Key Takeaway
The thana is a sunnah praise; mispronouncing 'nahfid' as 'nahfidh' invalidates prayer, and the Muslim must maintain a balance of hope and fear of Allah.

Salah — Prayer

The Ruling on Sending Blessings on the Prophet in Qunoot
Ruling and proof on sending blessings in qunoot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sending blessings on the Prophet in qunoot and identify the dalil that supports it.

Core Idea
Sending blessings on the Prophet in qunoot is mustahabb, supported by hadith and the choice of later Hanafi authorities.

The qunoot supplication is a sunnah act in the witr prayer, and its wording includes various supplications. This lesson examines whether it is prescribed to send blessings on the Prophet during qunoot. The Hanafi school, based on a hadith from Al-Nasa'i and the preferred view of Faqih Abu al-Layth, holds that it is recommended (mustahabb) to include 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad' in qunoot.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
Determine what act is being ruled upon (sending blessings in qunoot) and classify it within the acts of prayer.
The act is a supplication (du'a) within a sunnah act of prayer.
2
Locate the dalil cited
The passage cites a hadith from Al-Nasa'i from Zayd ibn Kharijah on how to send blessings and the importance of doing so in supplication.
The hadith is hasan and includes the command: 'Say: Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad.'
3
Determine the hukm from the dalil
In Hanafi usul, a command (amr) generally indicates obligation unless there is a qarinah (contextual indicator) shifting it to recommendation. Here, since qunoot itself is sunnah, the command to send blessings within it becomes mustahabb.
The context of supplication (du'a) and the hadith's phrasing support recommendation.
4
Identify the tarjih (preferred view)
Faqih Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi chose the view that sending blessings in qunoot is mustahabb, and this is the mufta bihi in the later Hanafi school.
Some early scholars held it not prescribed, but the tarjih is in favor of inclusion.

Source Text

نعتقد ونقول (إن هذابك الجد) أي الحق، وهو بكسر الجيم اتفاقاً بمعنى الحق، وهو ثابت في مراسيل أبي داود، فلا يلتفت لمن قال أنه لا يقول الجدّ (بالكفار (ملحق أي لا حق بهم بكسر الحاء أفصح، وقيل : بفتحها يعني أن الله سبحانه وتعالى ملحقه بهم ولما روى النسائي بإسناد حسن إن في حديث القنوت وصلى الله على النبي صلينا عليه صلى الله عليه (و) على (آله وسلم) كما عن علته، معناه أنه يوصل إليه بسبب استرساله في المعاصي. قال تعالى: فلا يأمن مكر الله إلا القوم الخاسرون) . قوله : (كالقنوط من الرحمة) أي اليأس منها والجزم بأنه من أهل العذاب فإنه يؤدي إلى تقليل العمل وإنكار الرحمة وفيه ما تقدم في الأمن قال تعالى : إنه لا يأس من روح الله إلا القوم الكافرون) . قوله : أني) يرجى (نواله أي إنعامه ونكاله عقابه. قوله: (لا يجتمعان الخ) قد علمت أنّ الرجاء لا يتحقق إلا مع الأعمال الصالحة وإلا فهو طمع. قوله : (بالأركان) أي الأعضاء قوله : (ممتثلين لأمرك حال مؤكدة قوله : (لا) مقتصرين على القلب واللسان) بأن يرجو بقلبه، أو ينطق بلسانه من غير عمل الأركان قوله : (ذوي البهتان) هو الكذب، وفسره في القاموس بأن يقول على الشخص ما لم يفعل قوله : (نعتقد ونقول) معلول مؤخر وهو قوله : فلإنعامك علينا بالإيمان، ولا شك أن هذا الإعتقاد، والقول علته الإنعام بالإيمان قوله : (بكسر الحاء) قال النووي: هذا هو المشهور، وقال الجزري : هكذا روينا. قوله: (وقيل بفتحها) قاله ابن قتيبة ،وغيره ونص الجوهري على أنه صواب. قوله: (وصلى الله على النبي) هذا هو الذي رواه النسائي فقط بدون، وعلى آله وسلم كما يفهم من الشرح. قوله : ( صلينا) معلول لقوله، ولما روى النسائي. قوله : (وعلى آله وسلم) في الواقعات بعد ما ذكر اختيار الفقيه أبي الليث أنه يصلي قال : والمستحب في كل دعاء أن يكون فيه الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد اهـ فهذا يفيد أنّ كيفية الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت بهذه الكيفية، ويشهد له ما أخرجه النسائي بسند صحيح عن زيد بن خارجة قال : سألت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كيف الصلاة عليك فقال: صلوا علي واجتهدوا في الدعاء وقولوا اللهم صل على محمد وعلى آل محمد وعنه : الدعاء موقوف بين السماء، والأرض لا يصعد حتى يصلى علي فلا تجعلوني كغمر الراكب صلوا علي في أوّل الدعاء وأوسطه وآخره
We believe and say: Indeed this, Your majesty, is the truth, and it is with kasra on the jim by agreement meaning the truth, and it is established in the mursal of Abu Dawud, so do not pay attention to those who say he does not say al-jadd (with the disbelievers) attached, i.e., joined with them, with kasra on the ha being more eloquent, and it is said with fatha, meaning that Allah Almighty joins him to them because of his persistence in sins. He said: The Exalted said: 'So none feels secure from the deception of Allah except the losing people.' He said: (Like despairing of mercy) i.e., despondency and certainty that one is among the people of punishment, for it leads to reducing action and denying mercy, and in it is what preceded about security. He said: The Exalted said: 'Indeed, no one despairs of the Spirit of Allah except the disbelieving people.' He said: (I hope) for His favor, i.e., His bounty, and His retribution, i.e., His punishment. He said: (They do not gather) etc. You have learned that hope is only realized with righteous deeds, otherwise it is wishful thinking. He said: (With the limbs) i.e., the body parts. He said: (Complying with Your command) an emphasized circumstantial clause. He said: (Not) restricted to the heart and tongue, by hoping in his heart or speaking with his tongue without action of the limbs. He said: (People of falsehood) which is lying, and it is explained in the Qamus as saying about a person what he did not do. He said: (We believe and say) is a postponed cause, which is his saying: For Your favor upon us with faith, and there is no doubt that this belief and saying is caused by the favor of faith. He said: (With kasra on the ha) Al-Nawawi said: This is the well-known, and Al-Jazari said: This is how we narrated. He said: (And it is said with fatha) Ibn Qutaybah and others said it, and Al-Jawhari stated it is correct. He said: (And may Allah bless the Prophet) this is what Al-Nasa'i narrated only, without 'and upon his family and grant them peace' as understood from the commentary. He said: (We prayed) is caused by his saying, and because Al-Nasa'i narrated. He said: (And upon his family and grant them peace) in the incidents after mentioning the choice of Faqih Abu al-Layth that he prays, he said: It is recommended in every supplication that it include blessings on the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, and he said: O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad. This indicates that the manner of sending blessings on the Prophet in qunoot is in this manner, and it is supported by what Al-Nasa'i narrated with a sound chain from Zayd ibn Kharijah who said: I asked the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, how to send blessings on you, and he said: Send blessings on me and strive in supplication, and say: O Allah, bless Muhammad and the family of Muhammad. And from him: Supplication is suspended between heaven and earth; it does not ascend until blessings are sent upon me, so do not make me like the vessel of a rider; send blessings on me at the beginning, middle, and end of supplication.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement on the qunoot supplication in prayer. The author explains that the phrase 'inna hadha bika al-jadd' means 'this is Your majesty, the truth.' He clarifies the pronunciation of 'al-jadd' and 'ilhaaq'. Then he discusses the ruling on sending blessings (salat) on the Prophet during qunoot. Citing a hasan narration from Al-Nasa'i, the author establishes that it is recommended (mustahabb) to say 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad' in qunoot. The commentary includes the hadith of Zayd ibn Kharijah on how to send blessings and the importance of including blessings in supplication for it to ascend. The legal conclusion is that the recommended form of sending blessings in qunoot is as stated, and this should not be omitted.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunoot): A supplication recited in the standing posture of prayer, typically after ruku' in the witr prayer, but also in other prayers as per Hanafi fiqh.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salatu 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings on the Prophet Muhammad, typically using the phrase 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad'.
الجد (al-jadd): In this context, it means 'majesty' or 'greatness' as a name/attribute of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the hukm of sending blessings on the Prophet during the qunoot supplication according to the Hanafi school, based on the hadith cited?
A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Mustahabb (recommended)
C) Makruh (disliked)
D) Haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends sending blessings on the Prophet in the qunoot supplication using the wording 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad wa 'ala aali Muhammad'.

Follower's Recitation in Qunut: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Preferred Wording
Intra-Hanafi dispute and preferred supplication text in qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the follower's recitation in qunut, identify the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position, and recite the preferred qunut supplication from the hadith of al-Hasan ibn Ali.

Core Idea
The follower recites qunut with the imam (the asahh view); the hadith of al-Hasan ibn Ali provides the preferred wording.

Qunut is a sunnah supplication in witr, but what should the follower do when the imam recites it? This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this dispute not only clarifies the ruling but also demonstrates how the Hanafi school handles ikhtilaf among its own authorities. Additionally, the passage provides the preferred wording for the qunut supplication, based on a well-known hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
The imam begins the qunut supplication. The issue is whether the follower recites along or simply says 'amin'.
The qunut consists of two parts: an initial praise (e.g., 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka...') followed by the supplication ('Allahumma ihdina...'). The dispute applies to both.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position
Abu Yusuf holds that the follower recites the same supplication with the imam, treating qunut like any other recitation in prayer (e.g., Fatiha).
3
State Muhammad's position
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that the follower should only say 'amin' and not recite, arguing that qunut is a supplication, and saying 'amin' suffices, as in other supplications.
Muhammad's evidence includes the practice of the Prophet who said 'amin' after the imam recited qunut.
4
Identify the relied-upon position
The commentator, al-Tahtawi, indicates that 'al-asahh' (the most correct view) is that the follower recites, as previously stated. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
5
Note the preferred wording
After the initial established part, it is better to recite the qunut taught by al-Hasan ibn Ali, which is a well-known hadith (in singular form). The text provides the full supplication.
The hadith: 'Allahumma ihdini fiman hadayt...' (O Allah, guide me among those You have guided...).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا شرع الإمام في الدعاء وهو اللهم اهدنا الخ كما سنذكره بعدما تقدم من قوله اللهم إنا نستعينك الخ قال أبو يوسف رحمه الله يتابعونه ويقرؤنه معه أيضاً وقال محمد لا يتابعونه فيه ولا في القنوت الذي هو اللهم إنا نستعينك ونستغفرك ولكن يؤمنون على دعائه والدعاء قال طائفة من المشايخ: إنه لا توقيت فيه والأولى أن يقرأ بعد المتقدم قنوت الحسن بن علي رضي الله عنهما قال: علمني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كلمات أقولهن في الوتر، وفي لفظ في قنوت الوتر ورواه الحاكم وقال فيه : إذا رفعت رأسي، ولم يبق إلا السجود اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت وعافني فيمن عافيت وتولني فيمن توليت وبارك لي فيما أعطيت وقني شر ما قضيت إنك تقضي ولا يقضى عليك وإنه لا يذل من واليت تباركت وتعاليت وحسنه الترمذي، وزاد البيهقي بعد واليت ولا يعز من عاديت، وزاد النسائي بعد وتعاليت وصلى الله على النبي فهو كما ترى بصيغة الإفراد فيه وفي المروي عنه حال
And when the imam begins the supplication, which is 'O Allah, guide us...' as we will mention later after what preceded from his saying 'O Allah, we seek Your help...', Abu Yusuf said: They follow him and recite it with him as well. Muhammad said: They do not follow him in it nor in the qunut which is 'O Allah, we seek Your help and seek Your forgiveness', but they say amin to his supplication. And the supplication — a group of scholars said: There is no fixed time in it, and it is better to recite after what preceded the qunut of al-Hasan ibn Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both). He said: The Messenger of Allah taught me words that I say in the witr, and in another wording: in the qunut of the witr. Al-Hakim narrated it and said in it: When I raise my head and nothing remains except prostration: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided, and grant me health among those You have granted health, and take care of me among those You have taken care of, and bless me in what You have given, and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed You decree and none decrees against You, and indeed he is not humiliated whom You protect. Blessed and Exalted are You.' Al-Tirmidhi classified it as hasan. Al-Bayhaqi added after 'whom You protect': 'and he is not honored whom You oppose.' Al-Nasa'i added after 'Exalted are You': 'and may Allah bless the Prophet.' So it is, as you see, in the singular form in it and in what is narrated from him.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani regarding the follower's role during the qunut supplication. When the imam begins the specific supplication 'O Allah, guide us...' (the second part of qunut after the initial praise), Abu Yusuf holds that the follower should recite along with the imam, similar to the initial part. Muhammad, however, says the follower should not recite along but should only say amin, and this applies to both parts of the qunut. The commentator does not definitively choose here but earlier indicated that the most correct view (al-asahh) is that the follower recites like the imam. The passage then discusses the preferred wording of the supplication after the initial established part. A group of scholars say there is no fixed time for this supplication, but the better choice is to recite the qunut taught by al-Hasan ibn Ali, which is a well-known hadith. The hadith is presented in the singular form, indicating the individual nature of the supplication, though it is recited in congregation. This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school on the exact wording and method of qunut.

Key Terms
المتابعة (al-mutaba'ah): Following the imam in recitation; here specifically whether the follower recites the same qunut supplication.
التأمين (al-ta'min): Saying 'amin' after the imam's supplication; Muhammad's position is that the follower should do this rather than recite.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the disagreement between Abu Yusuf and Muhammad regarding the follower's action in qunut?
A) Abu Yusuf says the follower says amin; Muhammad says the follower recites.
B) Abu Yusuf says the follower recites; Muhammad says the follower says amin.
C) Both agree the follower recites.
D) Both agree the follower says amin.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the follower recites qunut with the imam (mufta bihi), and the preferred wording is the hadith of al-Hasan ibn Ali.

Follower's Qunut Recitation: Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad
Intra-Hanafi dispute on follower's recitation in qunut and exposition of the preferred du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the follower's action during qunut and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Abu Yusuf: follower recites; Muhammad: follower says 'amin'; the school prefers recitation.

When the imam recites the qunut supplication in witr, what should the follower do? Is it better to recite along or simply affirm with 'amin'? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and then turns to the actual content of the qunut du'a as taught by the Prophet to Hasan ibn Ali.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested issue
The issue is whether the follower (mu'tamm) recites the qunut supplication along with the imam or merely says 'amin'.
This is an intra-Hanafi difference, not a dispute with another school.
2
State the position of Imam Abu Yusuf
Abu Yusuf holds that the follower recites the qunut with the imam. His reasoning is based on the principle of following the imam in all acts of prayer.
This view is given precedence in the school according to a general tarjih rule.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani
Muhammad holds that the follower does not recite but says 'amin'. His reasoning is that the imam is the supplicant and the follower's role is to affirm the du'a.
Some later scholars like Ibn al-Humam preferred this view based on Companion practice.
4
Analyze the tarjih mechanism
Examine why the school gives precedence to Abu Yusuf and the counter-argument. A general principle prioritizes Abu Yusuf's opinion, but Ibn al-Humam argued that the Companions' practice supports Muhammad's view.
The text does not fully resolve; the mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If following Abu Yusuf, the follower recites quietly; if following Muhammad, the follower remains silent and says 'amin'.
Both positions are valid within the Hanafi school.

قنوت الفجر لما كان يفعله قال الكمال بن الهمام: لكنهم أي المشايخ لفقوه من حديث في حق الإمام عام لا يخص القنوت فقالوه بنون الجمع اللهم اهدنا وعافنا وتولنا الخ اهـ قلت : ومنهم صاحب الدرر والغرر والبرهان والدعاء الذي قالوه (هو هذا اللهم اهدنا) ورواية الحسن اهدني كما نبهنا عليه أصل الهداية الرسالة والبيان كقوله تعالى : وإنك لتهدي إلى صراط مستقيم فأما قوله إنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء فهي من الله تعالى التوفيق والإرشاد فطلب المؤمنين مع كونهم مهتدين بمعنى طلب التثبت عليها أو معنى المزيد منها (بفضلك لا بوجوب عليك وهذه الزيادة ليست في قنوت الحسن اللهم اهدني فيمن هديت) أي مع من هديته في حال اليتيم لأنه سبحانه ينظر في أمور من تولاه بالعناية فيمن توليت) أي مع من توليت أمره من عبادك المقربين وبارك لنا فيما أعطيت البركة الزيادة من الخير فطلبت ترقياً على قوله: (من حديث في حق الإمام (عام) هو لا يؤم عبد قوماً فيخص نفسه بدعوة دونهم فإن فعل فقد خانهم رواه أبو داود وحسنه الترمذي. قوله: (أصل الهداية الرسالة، والبيان) الذي في القاموس الهد بضم الهاء، وفتح الدال الرشاد، والدلالة وتذكر النهار هداه هدى وهدياً وهداية، وهدية بكسرهما أرشده فتهدي واهتدى وهداه الله الطريق، وإليه وله اهـ فلم توجد بمعنى الإرسال والبيان إلا أن البيان لازم الرشاد والدلالة قوله: (وإنك لتهدي) أي لتدل . قوله: (إنك لا تهدي أي لا ،توصل ولكن الله يهدي أي يوصل قوله : (فهي من الله التوفيق) الأولى حذف قوله من الله لأنها تفسر بالتوفيق الملزوم للإيصال في قوله تعالى إنك لا تهدي كما تفسر به فيما بعد قوله : ( فطلب (المؤمنين أي إذا علمت أنها من الله التوفيق، والمؤمن موفق فطلبه مع حصوله يحمل على طلب الدوام عليه، أو المزيد منه، ومنه اللهم إهدنا. قوله : (بفضلك أي بإحسانك، والباء للسببية. قوله: (والبلايا والمحن) أي دنيا، وأخرى فهي لفظ عام تحته كل خير، والمفاعلة على غير بابها. قوله: (من الناس) أي من شرورهم قوله: (ويعافيهم منك) هذا بيان للمفاعلة التي تكون من الجانبين. قوله: (وتولنا) ولاية الله تعالى لعبده إرادة توفيقه وتأييده وتقريبه، وإكرامه كذا في الشرح. قوله: (من توليت الشيء) ويجوز أن يكون من وليت الشيء إذا لم يكن بينك وبينه واسطة والمعنى أنه يقطع الوسائط بينه وبين الله سبحانه وتعالى حتى يصير في مقام المراقبة والمشاهدة، وهو مقام الإحسان كذا في الشرح قوله : الزيادة من الخير) وقيل حلول الخير الإلهي في الشيء. قوله: (ترقياً على المقامين السابقين وهما مقام المعافاة، ومقام الموالاة يعني أنه يطلب الزيادة فيهما
The jurist Abu al-Layth (may Allah have mercy on him) chose that he sends blessings upon the Prophet in the qunut, and the follower recites the qunut like the imam according to the most correct view. The imam and the people recite quietly; that is correct, but it is recommended for the imam to recite loudly in non-Arab lands so that they learn, as Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) recited the praise loudly when a delegation from Iraq came to him. Therefore, some scholars distinguished: if the people do not know, then it is better for the imam to recite loudly so that they learn; otherwise, quiet recitation is better. (And when the imam begins the supplication) which is 'Allahumma ihdina' etc., as we will mention after what has preceded from his saying 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' etc. (Abu Yusuf said: They follow him and recite with him) as well. (And Muhammad said: They do not follow him) in that nor in the qunut which is 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka wa nastaghfiruka', but they say 'amin' to his supplication. (And the supplication) A group of scholars said: There is no fixed time for it, but it is better to recite after the preceding the qunut of al-Hasan ibn Ali (may Allah be pleased with them both). He said: The Messenger of Allah taught me words that I say in witr, and in another wording: in the qunut of witr. Al-Hakim narrated it and said in it: When I raise my head, and nothing remains except prostration: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided, and grant me well-being among those You have granted well-being, and take me into Your charge among those You have taken into Your charge, and bless me in what You have given, and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed. Indeed, You decree and none decrees against You. Indeed, he whom You support is not humiliated. Blessed and Exalted are You.' Al-Tirmidhi declared it good. Al-Bayhaqi added after 'and he whom You support': 'and he whom You oppose is not honored.' Al-Nasa'i added after 'Exalted are You': 'and may Allah send blessings upon the Prophet.' So it is, as you see, in the singular form in it and in what is narrated from him. 'Al-ghamr' (with a kasra under the ghayn) means a small cup. His statement: (as Abu al-Layth chose) In al-Halabi, from Ibn al-Humam: It is not appropriate to deviate from this statement, and it is the truth, as in al-Bahr and Ibn Amir Hajj. His statement: (it is the correct one) The most correct as in al-Muhit, and the chosen as in al-Majma' and al-Hidayah. In al-Dhakhirah: The imam should be moderate in reciting the qunut, neither very loud nor very quiet, so that the follower can recite behind him; that is the chosen view. His statement: (Abu Yusuf said: They follow him) From the principles: The statement of Abu Yusuf is given precedence over the statement of Muhammad in absolute terms. Al-Mulla Ali said in Sharh al-Husn: It is appropriate to give precedence to this because it is more correct. Ibn al-Humam said: It is better to delay it because the Companions agreed on 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' etc. His statement: (And the supplication) The subject, its predicate is his statement 'A group said', and the author removed it from its grammatical analysis. His statement: (There is no fixed time for it) It is better for the supplication to be fixed in time because the supplicant may be ignorant and supplicate with something that cuts off the prayer, and he does not know that, as in Ghayat al-Bayan. Muhammad's statement that there is no fixed supplication in qunut means other than 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' etc. and 'Allahumma ihdina', and Ibn Amir Hajj gave it preponderance due to what preceded and as a blessing from the reported. His statement: 'When I raise my head' this does not support the school, but it is opposed by what is more authentic from the people of the school, so they gave it precedence. His statement: 'among those You have guided' i.e., with them. His statement: 'and protect me from the evil of what You have decreed' i.e., a decreed decree, or protect me from its evil of importance so that it occurs gently. His statement: 'he whom You support' i.e., he whom You have been a supporter of. His statement: 'similar to what he used to do' i.e., in his supplication against some Arab tribes. His supplication in the qunut of fajr was similar to what he used to do. Al-Kamal ibn al-Humam said: But they, i.e., the scholars, compiled it from a hadith concerning the imam in general, not specific to qunut, so they said it with the plural 'nun': 'Allahumma ihdina wa 'afina wa tawallana' etc. I say: Among them are the author of al-Durar wa al-Ghurar and al-Burhan. The supplication that they said is this 'Allahumma ihdina'. And the narration of al-Hasan is 'ihdini' as we pointed out. The origin of guidance is the message and clarification, as in His statement: 'And indeed you guide to a straight path' (42:52). As for His statement: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but Allah guides whom He wills' (28:56), it is from Allah, meaning success and direction. So the request of the believers, while they are guided, means seeking steadfastness in it or increase from it. (By Your grace, not as an obligation upon You) This addition is not in the qunut of al-Hasan: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided' i.e., with those You have guided. (And grant us well-being) Well-being is safety from ailments, calamities, and trials. Mutual well-being is that Allah protects you from people and protects them from you. (among those You have granted well-being) i.e., with those You have granted well-being. (And take us into Your charge) from 'tawallayt al-shay'' if you took care of it and looked after it with benefits, as the guardian looks after the orphan, because He looks into the affairs of those He takes charge of with care. (among those You have taken into Your charge) i.e., with those You have taken charge of their affairs from Your close servants. (And bless us in what You have given) Blessing is increase in good, so it is requesting advancement upon His statement: (from a hadith concerning the imam in general: 'A man should not lead a people in prayer and single himself out with a supplication without them; if he does, he has betrayed them.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and declared good by al-Tirmidhi. His statement: (The origin of guidance is the message and clarification) In al-Qamus: 'al-huda' with damm on ha' and fatha on dal means right direction and guidance, and remembering the day; 'hada' (to guide), etc. So it is not found in the meaning of sending and clarification, except that clarification is necessary for right direction and guidance. His statement: ('And indeed you guide' (42:52)) i.e., you show the way. His statement: ('Indeed, you do not guide' (28:56)) i.e., you do not cause to arrive, but Allah guides i.e., causes to arrive. His statement: ('It is from Allah, meaning success') It is better to remove 'from Allah' because it is interpreted as success which necessitates arrival in His statement 'Indeed, you do not guide' as it is interpreted by what comes after. His statement: ('So the request of the believers') i.e., when you know that guidance is from Allah meaning success, and the believer is successful, so his request while it is obtained is interpreted as a request for continuance upon it or increase from it, including 'O Allah, guide us'. His statement: ('By Your grace' i.e., by Your favor, and the ba is for causality. His statement: ('and calamities and trials') i.e., worldly and otherworldly, so it is a general word that includes every good, and the mutual form (mufa'ala) is not in its usual sense. His statement: ('from people') i.e., from their evils. His statement: ('and protects them from you') This is an explanation of the mutual form that is from both sides. His statement: ('And take us into Your charge') The guardianship of Allah to His servant is the will to grant him success and support, bring him near, and honor him, as in the commentary. His statement: ('from tawallayt al-shay'') It is also possible to be from 'waliyta al-shay'' if there is no intermediary between you and it, meaning that he cuts off intermediaries between him and Allah until he reaches the station of watchfulness and witnessing, which is the station of excellence, as in the commentary. His statement: ('increase from good') It is said: the descent of divine good into the thing. His statement: ('advancement upon the two previous stations') which are the station of mutual well-being and the station of taking charge, meaning that he seeks increase in them.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses two main issues regarding qunut in witr prayer. First, it presents an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani on whether the follower (mu'tamm) recites the qunut supplication along with the imam or merely says 'amin'. Abu Yusuf holds that the follower recites along with the imam, while Muhammad holds that the follower does not recite but only says 'amin' to the imam's supplication. The text notes that there is a general principle (qā'ida) that Abu Yusuf's opinion is given precedence over Muhammad's in absolute terms, though Ibn al-Humam considered it preferable to delay (i.e., to prefer Muhammad's view) because the Companions agreed on the wording 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka'. The author also discusses issues of loud versus quiet recitation: the imam should moderate his voice so followers can recite, but in lands where people are ignorant, the imam may recite loudly to teach them, as 'Umar did.

Second, the passage discusses the content of the qunut supplication. It states that the preferred (awla) supplication is the one taught by the Prophet to al-Hasan ibn 'Ali, known as 'Qunut al-Hasan'. The text provides the hadith: 'O Allah, guide me among those You have guided...' in the singular form (ihdini), noting that later scholars adapted it to the plural form (ihdina) based on a general hadith about the imam not singling himself out with supplication. The commentary then explains the meanings of each phrase in the supplication: guidance as showing the way and also as granting success (tawfiq), well-being as safety from afflictions, taking into charge as care akin to a guardian's care, blessing as increase in good, and protection from evil decrees. It also clarifies that the request for guidance from already guided people is for steadfastness or increase. The passage thus combines a ruling on the follower's action with a textual proof for the recommended du'a and its linguistic and theological explanation.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer, particularly after raising the head from bowing.
مؤتم (mu'tamm): The person who prays behind an imam; the follower.
يؤمن (yu'min): To say 'amin' in response to the imam's supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the position of Imam Muhammad regarding the follower's action during the imam's qunut supplication?
A) The follower recites the qunut along with the imam.
B) The follower says 'amin' and does not recite.
C) The follower remains completely silent.
D) The follower recites a different supplication.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid views on the follower's qunut recitation; the relied-upon view is that the follower recites quietly along with the imam.

The Wording of Qunut in Fajr: Plural Form and Its Significance
Explaining wording and meaning of qunut du'a

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the correct wording of the qunut in Fajr according to the Hanafi school, explain why the plural form is used, and distinguish between the two meanings of guidance (hidayah).

Core Idea
The Hanafi qunut uses 'ihdina' (guide us) to include the congregation, based on a hadith prohibiting an imam from singling himself out.

The qunut supplication in Fajr is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) in the Hanafi school. This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi explains the precise wording of the du'a, emphasizing that it should be in the plural form to include the congregation. The commentary also clarifies the meaning of 'guidance' (hidayah) as requested in the du'a, distinguishing between the guidance of message (from prophets) and the guidance of success (from Allah alone). We will explore the textual basis for this ruling and the nuanced understanding of the du'a's phrases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the qunut supplication in Fajr prayer. According to the Hanafi school, it is a sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah) after ruku. Note the school's position and that it is not fard or wajib.
Cross-madhhab: Shafi'i recites qunut before ruku in Fajr and also in Witr; Maliki/Hanbali do not recite in Fajr.
2
Recognize the textual basis for the plural wording
The hadith 'la ya'ummu 'abdun qawman fayakhussu nafsahu bidu'atin dunahum' prohibits imam from singling himself out in supplication. Therefore, the qunut must use the plural 'us' (na) not singular 'me'.
Hadith reported by Abu Dawud and Tirmidhi; its chain is hasan.
3
Understand the dua phrases and their meanings
Analyze key phrases: 'ihdina' (guide us) - not initial guidance but steadfastness; 'afina' (pardon us) - mutual safety; 'tawallana' (take charge of us) - Allah's care; 'barik lana' (bless for us) - increase in good. Each phrase is explained in the hashiya.
The distinction in 'hidayah' is between irshad (message) and tawfiq (success).
4
Apply the ruling in practice
When reciting qunut as imam or alone, use the plural form 'Allahumma ihdina' etc. The supplication is after ruku in the last rak'ah of Fajr.
If one recites the singular inadvertently, the prayer is still valid but contrary to sunnah; it is recommended to repeat the qunut in plural.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement from the hashiya, explaining the wording of the qunut du'a. The author clarifies that the du'a should be in the plural form (نا) because it is based on a hadith that forbids an imam from singling himself out in supplication. The hashiya then explains each phrase: 'guide us' means requesting steadfastness, not initial guidance; 'pardon us' refers to mutual safety; 'take charge of us' means Allah's care; 'bless us' asks for increase. The commentary also distinguishes between guidance as message (from prophets) and guidance as success (from Allah). The entire discussion is built on Hanafi principles of fiqh and hadith interpretation.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A specific supplication recited in the Fajr prayer after bowing according to the Hanafi school.
الهداية (al-hidayah): Guidance, but here distinguished between guidance as message (رسالة/بيان) and guidance as success/tawfiq from Allah.
المعافاة (al-mu'afat): Mutual safety and well-being between a person and others; that Allah protects you from people and them from you.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qunut in Fajr uses plural 'ihdina' based on a hadith that an imam must not single himself out in supplication, reflecting the communal nature of prayer.

Alternatives for Qunut and Following a Shafi'i Imam
Ruling on alternatives for qunut and following a mukhalif imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the permissible alternatives for qunut and explain the conditions under which a Hanafi may follow a Shafi'i imam in prayer.

Core Idea
You may use alternative supplications if you don't know qunut; you may also follow a Shafi'i imam if he observes Hanafi precautions.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies two practical issues for Hanafis in prayer. First, it provides alternative supplications for those who cannot recite the full qunut du'a, emphasizing that even those who know it may use them. Second, it addresses the case of praying behind a Shafi'i imam who performs qunut, establishing that it is permissible if the imam takes certain precautions in matters where the schools differ.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage covers two acts: reciting alternative supplications in qunut, and following a Shafi'i imam who performs qunut. Both are ruled permissible (mubah).
2
List the three alternative supplications
From al-Faqih Abu al-Layth: 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times. From al-Tajnis: 'Rabbana atina...'. From al-Sadr al-Shahid: 'Ya Rab' three times.
The hashiya notes the difference is over preference, not permissibility.
3
Understand the refinement
The base text restricts alternatives to those who do not know the du'a. The hashiya removes this restriction, making alternatives permissible for all.
This is an example of critical refinement of a ruling.
4
Apply the principle of iqtida' bi al-mukhalif
The passage states that following a Shafi'i imam is permissible. The hashiya adds conditions: the imam must observe Hanafi precautions (ihtiyat) in matters of difference.
5
Identify the required precautions
The five precautions listed: renew wudu after blood, wipe quarter of head in wudu, wash or rub off semen from garment, do not end witr with salutation before tashahhud, arrange missed prayers in order.
These ensure the imam's prayer is valid per Hanafi standards.

Source Text

ومن لم يحسن) دعاء القنوت) المتقدم قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله تعالى : (يقول اللهم اغفر لي) ويكررها ثلاث مرات أو يقول (ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار) قال في التجنيس وهو اختيار مشايخنا (أو) يقول يا رب يا رب يا رب ثلاثاً ذكره الصدر الشهيد فهذه ثلاثة أقوال مختارة (وإذا اقتدى بمن يقنت في الفجر) كشافعي (قام معه 
قوله: (ومن لم يحسن الخ) التقييد به ليس بشرط بل يجوز لمن يعرف الدعاء المعروف أن يقتصر على واحد مما ذكر أفاده صاحب البحر .
قوله: (أو يقول ربنا آتنا الخ) قال صاحب البحر : الظاهر أن الإختلاف في الأفضلية لا في الجواز، وإن قوله ربنا الخ أفضل لشموله

Whoever does not know the aforementioned qunut supplication, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He says 'O Allah, forgive me' and repeats it three times, or he says 'Our Lord, grant us good in this world and good in the Hereafter and protect us from the punishment of the Fire.' It is said in al-Tajnis, and it is the choice of our scholars: or he says 'O Lord, O Lord, O Lord' three times. Al-Sadr al-Shahid mentioned this. These are three chosen statements. And if he follows an imam who performs qunut in Fajr, like a Shafi'i, he stands with him. [Margin notes: The condition 'if he does not know' is not a condition; it is permissible for one who knows the well-known du'a to limit himself to one of these. The difference is over preference, not permissibility. The verse 'Rabbana atina' is better because it is comprehensive. The issue indicates the permissibility of following a mukhalif, meaning a Shafi'i or other, provided he takes precautions in matters of difference, such as renewing wudu for blood, wiping a quarter of the head, washing or rubbing semen from the garment, not cutting the witr with a salutation, and arranging missed prayers.]
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage provides Hanafi rulings on two related matters. First, it gives alternatives for someone who does not know the full qunut du'a: repeating 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times, reciting the Quranic verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah...', or saying 'Ya Rab' three times. The hashiya clarifies that these alternatives are not limited to those who don't know the du'a; even those who know it may use them, and the difference is only over which is best. The verse 'Rabbana atina' is considered best because it is comprehensive. Second, if a Hanafi prays behind a Shafi'i imam who performs qunut in Fajr, the Hanafi should stand with the imam and follow him in the qunut. This is based on the general principle that following a mukhalif imam is permissible if the imam takes precautions in matters of difference. The hashiya lists several such precautions: renewing wudu after blood, wiping a quarter of the head in wudu, washing or rubbing semen from the garment (instead of requiring full washing), not ending witr with a salutation before the tashahhud, and arranging missed prayers in order. The overall ruling is that following a mukhalif imam is valid when he observes these precautions.

Key Terms
الاقتداء بالمخالف (al-iqtida' bi al-mukhalif): Following an imam who belongs to a different school of thought.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Taking precautions to satisfy the conditions of the Hanafi school while following a mukhalif imam.
القنوت (al-qunut): A special supplication recited during the witr prayer or in the Fajr prayer (according to Shafi'is).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) They are permissible for anyone, but ‘Rabbana atina’ is considered best.
C) They are only for individuals praying alone, not in congregation.
D) They are invalid if the person knows the original du'a.

Key Takeaway
If you don't know the qunut du'a, use any of the three alternatives; you may also follow a Shafi'i imam if he observes Hanafi precautions.

Alternative Supplications for Qunoot for Those Who Do Not Know It
Ruling on permissible alternative du'as in qunoot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three alternative supplications for qunoot and explain the ruling on their permissibility and superiority.

Core Idea
The qunoot can be performed with simple alternatives, and even one who knows the full du'a may choose these, though the Quranic verse is best.

In Witr prayer, the qunoot is a wajib supplication. Not everyone memorizes the lengthy traditional wording. The Hanafi school provides three simple alternatives, as stated by al-Faqih Abu al-Layth. This lesson clarifies that these alternatives are not only for those who don't know the full supplication, but are permissible for all, with a preference for the Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the supplication (du'a) in qunoot during Witr prayer, which is wajib. The passage provides alternatives for those who do not know the traditional wording.
Qunoot itself is wajib, but the specific wording is sunnah; alternatives are permissible.
2
List the three alternatives
Extract the three quoted supplications: 'Allahumma ighfir li' repeated three times, 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah...', and 'Ya Rabb' three times.
These are taken from the text of al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, al-Tajnīs, and al-Sadr al-Shahīd.
3
Analyze the condition of the ruling
Note that the phrase 'whoever does not know' is not a restrictive condition. Even one who knows the full du'a may limit himself to one of these alternatives.
This is stated by Sāhib al-Bahr and is a key clarification.
4
Understand the preference (afdaliyyah)
The difference among the alternatives is one of superiority, not permissibility. The verse 'Rabbana atina' is considered better because it is comprehensive.
The chosen opinion of our mashāyikh (as in al-Tajnīs) selects the verse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(ومن لم يحسن دعاء القنوت) المتقدم قال الفقيه أبو الليث رحمه الله تعالى : (يقول اللهم اغفر لي) ويكررها ثلاث مرات أو يقول (ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار) قال في التجنيس وهو اختيار مشايخنا (أو) يقول يا رب يا رب يا رب ثلاثاً ذكره الصدر الشهيد فهذه ثلاثة أقوال مختارة . قوله: (ومن لم يحسن الخ) التقييد به ليس بشرط بل يجوز لمن يعرف الدعاء المعروف أن يقتصر على واحد مما ذكر أفاده صاحب البحر . قوله: (أو يقول ربنا آتنا الخ) قال صاحب البحر : الظاهر أن الإختلاف في الأفضلية لا في الجواز، وإن قوله ربنا الخ أفضل لشموله
And whoever does not know well the previously mentioned qunoot supplication, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth (may Allah have mercy on him) said: He says: 'O Allah, forgive me' and repeats it three times, or he says: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' – it is stated in al-Tajnīs that this is the choice of our mashāyikh – or he says: 'O Lord, O Lord, O Lord' three times, mentioned by al-Sadr al-Shahīd. These are three chosen sayings. His statement: ('And whoever does not know' etc.) The restriction to this is not a condition; rather it is permissible for one who knows the well-known supplication to limit himself to one of what was mentioned, as stated by Sāhib al-Bahr. His statement: ('Or he says: Our Lord, give us' etc.) Sāhib al-Bahr said: It appears that the difference is regarding superiority (afdaliyyah), not permissibility, and that his saying 'Our Lord, give us' is better because of its comprehensiveness.

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on what a person should recite in the qunoot supplication if they do not know the full traditional wording. The author, al-Faqih Abu al-Layth, gives three options: repeating 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times, reciting the Quranic verse 'Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanah...', or saying 'Ya Rabb' three times. The commentary clarifies that these are not restricted only to those who do not know the full qunoot; even someone who knows it may choose one of these, though the difference is one of preference (afdaliyyah) not permissibility. According to Sāhib al-Bahr, the Quranic verse is considered better because it is comprehensive. The chosen opinion of our scholars is the second option (the verse), as stated in al-Tajnīs.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunoot): A special supplication recited in the Witr prayer (and sometimes in Fajr) after rising from ruku' in the last rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school provides three permissible alternatives for qunoot, with the Quranic verse 'Rabbana atina' being the most preferred due to its comprehensiveness.

Following a Shafi'i Imam in Fajr Qunoot
Ruling on Hanafi muqtadi following a Shafi'i imam in Fajr qunoot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muqtadi following a Shafi'i imam in Fajr qunoot and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
In Fajr prayer, a Hanafi muqtadi stands silently during a Shafi'i imam's qunoot because qunoot is abrogated in the Hanafi school.

When a Hanafi Muslim prays behind a Shafi'i imam who performs the qunoot in Fajr, a question arises: should the muqtadi recite the qunoot with the imam or remain silent? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling, the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, and the practical implications for prayer validity.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on Fajr qunoot
The Hanafi school holds that qunoot in Fajr is abrogated (mansukh). Therefore, it is not a sunnah act in the prayer.
2
Identify the scenario
A Hanafi muqtadi is praying behind a Shafi'i imam who recites qunoot in the second rak'ah of Fajr.
3
Analyze the obligation of following the imam
Following the imam in actions (like standing, ruku) is wajib. The question is whether reciting the qunoot is considered part of the actions to follow.
4
Compare the two views within the Hanafi school
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: remain silent (qunoot is abrogated). Abu Yusuf: recite with the imam (qunoot is a matter of ijtihad, analogous to 'Id takbirs).
5
Apply the condition for valid following
The muqtadi's prayer is valid only if the imam performs the prayer with one taslim (i.e., does not separate the prayer).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وإذا اقتدى بمن يقنت في الفجر) كشافعي (قام معه في) . حال (قنوته ساكناً في الأظهر) لوجوب متابعته في القيام ولكن عندهما يقوم ساكتاً، وقال أبو يوسف : يقرؤه معه لأنه تبع للإمام، والقنوت مجتهد فيه فصار كتكبيرات العيدين والقنوت في الوتر بعد الركوع ويرسل يديه في جنبيه لأنه ذكر ليس مسنوناً قوله: (والقنوت في الوتر بعد الركوع) بالجر عطفاً على تكبيرات يعني أنه يتابعه فيه، ويقرؤه لأنه مجتهد فيه فصار كتكبيرات العيدين ولهما أن قنوت الفجر منسوخ على ما تقدم فصار كما لو كبر خمساً في الجنازة فإنه لا يتابعه ويصح الإقتداء فيه بمن يراه سنة لكن بشرط أن يؤديه بتسليمة واحدة وإلا يصح على ما عليه الأكثر .
And if one follows (as muqtadi) someone who performs qunoot in Fajr, like a Shafi'i, he stands with him during his qunoot, remaining silent in the more apparent view, due to the obligation of following him in standing; but according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he stands silently; and Abu Yusuf said: he recites it with him because he is a follower of the imam, and qunoot is a matter of ijtihad, so it becomes like the takbirs of the two 'Ids; and qunoot in Witr is after ruku', and he releases his hands by his sides because it is a dhikr that is not sunnah. His statement: ('And qunoot in Witr is after ruku'') by jar, conjoined to 'takbirs', meaning he follows him in it and recites it because it is a matter of ijtihad, so it becomes like the takbirs of the two 'Ids; and for them (the two) the qunoot of Fajr is abrogated as previously stated, so it becomes like if he said five takbirs in the funeral prayer – he does not follow him; and it is valid to follow one who considers it sunnah, but on condition that he performs it with one taslim; otherwise it is not valid according to the majority.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage deals with a Hanafi muqtadi following a Shafi'i imam who performs qunoot in the Fajr prayer. The matn states that the muqtadi stands with the imam silently during the qunoot, according to the more apparent view. The commentary explains the reasoning: the muqtadi must follow the imam in standing (qiyam), so he stands, but remains silent. However, Abu Yusuf holds that he should recite the qunoot along with the imam, because qunoot is a matter of ijtihad (not definitively abrogated in Fajr), and following the imam in reciting it is analogous to following in the extra takbirs of 'Id prayer. The passage also notes that qunoot in Witr is after ruku', and during it the muqtadi should let his hands hang by his sides, as it is not a sunnah dhikr (like raising hands). The commentary further explains the analogy: the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider Fajr qunoot abrogated, so following the imam in it is like following him in saying five takbirs in janazah – the muqtadi does not follow. However, it is valid to follow an imam who considers qunoot sunnah, provided he performs the prayer with one taslim; otherwise the following is not valid according to the majority.

Key Terms
متابعة الإمام (mutāba'at al-imām): Following the imam in the actions of prayer, which is wajib (obligatory) for the muqtadi.
قنوت الفجر (qunoot al-fajr): The special supplication recited in the Fajr prayer after ruku' in the second rak'ah, considered sunnah by Shafi'is but mansukh (abrogated) by Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the more apparent view in this passage, what should a Hanafi muqtadi do when following a Shafi'i imam who performs qunoot in Fajr?
A) Recite the qunoot with the imam
B) Leave the prayer immediately
C) Stand silently during the qunoot
D) Raise his hands and make dua silently

Key Takeaway
When a Hanafi follows a Shafi'i imam who recites Fajr qunoot, the muqtadi should stand silently; reciting the qunoot is not allowed according to the relied-upon Hanafi view due to abrogation.
