Rulings on Forgetting Qunoot in Witr and Muqtadi's Actions
Rulings on forgetting qunoot

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when qunoot is forgotten in Witr and apply the rules for the muqtadi's options in following the imam.

Core Idea
If qunoot is forgotten and remembered after ruku', it is not performed; sajda al-sahw compensates, and the muqtadi must balance qunoot with following the imam.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi delves into two key scenarios: what to do if you forget the qunoot in Witr, and how a muqtadi (follower) should act when the imam performs or omits qunoot. Understanding these rulings protects the validity of your prayer and ensures you fulfill the wajib (obligatory) elements correctly. We will walk through the rulings step by step, analyzing the reasoning behind each rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue: forgetting qunoot in Witr
Recognize that qunoot in the third rak'ah of Witr is a wajib. The passage deals with cases where it is forgotten and later remembered during or after ruku'.
Remember that qunoot is a wajib; its omission or delay necessitates sajda al-sahw.
2
Apply the ruling for the individual praying alone
If qunoot is forgotten and remembered during ruku' or after rising from it, the sound opinion is: do not perform qunoot now, and perform sajda al-sahw at the end. If he mistakenly performed qunoot after ruku', he does not repeat ruku' but still does sajda sahw.
The reasoning: qunoot is not time-bound in the apparent narration; what was performed suffices, but the delay of the wajib requires compensation.
3
Apply the ruling for the muqtadi (follower)
The muqtadi must balance two wajibs: reciting qunoot and following the imam (wajib al-mutaba'ah). If he fears missing the imam's ruku', he should follow the imam. If he can still catch ruku' after qunoot, he should perform qunoot. If the imam omits qunoot, the muqtadi performs it himself if he can still catch the ruku'.
The principle: following the imam takes priority when conflict arises, but if possible, combine both obligations.
4
Understand the reasoning (talil)
The commentary explains that in the first case (forgetting qunoot), the ruling is based on qunoot not being time-bound. In the second case (muqtadi's choice), the ruling balances the two wajibs, with following the imam taking precedence when necessary.
The 'sound opinion' (sahih) is that qunoot is not made up after ruku'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا نسي القنوت في ثالثة الوتر وتذكره في الركوع أو في الرفع منه أي من الركوع لا يقنت على الصحيح لا في الركوع الذي تذكره فيه ولا بعد الرفع منه ويسجد للسهو ولو قنت بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع لا يعيد الركوع ويسجد للسهو لزوال القنوت عن محله الأصلي وتأخير الواجب ولو ركع الإمام قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة القنوت أو قبل شروعه فيه وخاف فوت الركوع مع الإمام تابع إمامه لأن اشتغاله بذلك يفوت واجب المتابعة فتكون أولى وإن لم يخف فوت المشاركة في الركوع يقنت جمعاً بين الواجبين ولو ترك الإمام القنوت يأتي به المؤتم إن أمكنه مشاركة الإمام في الركوع لجمعه بين الواجبين بحسب الإمكان وإن كان لا يمكنه المشاركة تابعه لأن متابعته أولى ولو أدرك الإمام في ركوع الثالثة من الوتر كان مدركاً للقنوت حكماً فلا يأتي به فيما سبق به كما لو قنت المسبوق قوله: (على الصحيح هذا مرتبط بقوله، وتذكره في الركوع، وأما في الصورة الثانية وهي ما بعد الرفع فإنه لا يعيده إتفاقاً، ولو أخر قوله، وتذكره في الركوع ليربطه به لكان أولى أفاده السيد قوله : (لا يعيد الركوع) ظاهره أنه عليه إعادته لا يحرم لإتيانه بما ليس من الصلاة، وفي شرح السيد مراده من عدم إعادة الركوع أن صحة صلاته لا تتوقف على إعادته، وليس المراد أنه ممنوع من إعادته ،أهـ، والظاهر ما قلنا. قوله: وتأخير الواجب عطف مرادف. قوله: لأن اشتغاله الخ وتعلل المسئلة الأولى بأن القنوت ليس بمؤقت في ظاهر الرواية فما أتى به منه يكفيه قوله : يفوت واجب المتابعة أي المتابعة الواجبة قد يقال في المسئلة الثانية أنّ القنوت واجب أيضاً فمقتضاه التخيير له، بل يدعي أن الإتيان بالقنوت أولى لأنه لا يمكنه تداركه بخلاف الركوع .
And if one forgets the qunoot in the third rak'ah of Witr and remembers it in ruku' or in rising from it, i.e. from ruku', he does not perform qunoot according to the sound opinion — neither in the ruku' in which he remembered it nor after rising from it — and he performs sajda al-sahw. And if he performed qunoot after raising his head from ruku', he does not repeat the ruku' and performs sajda al-sahw because the qunoot left its proper place and the obligation was delayed. And if the imam bows before the muqtadi finishes reciting the qunoot or before he starts it, and he fears missing the ruku' with the imam, he follows his imam because occupying himself with that (qunoot) would cause him to miss the obligatory following, so following is better. And if he does not fear missing participation in ruku', he performs qunoot to combine both obligations. And if the imam leaves the qunoot, the muqtadi performs it if he can participate with the imam in ruku', to combine both obligations as much as possible. And if he cannot participate, he follows him because following him is better. And if he catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah of Witr, he is considered to have caught the qunoot in judgment, so he does not perform it for what preceded, just as if a latecomer (masbuq) performed qunoot. His statement: ('According to the sound opinion, this is connected to his saying 'and he remembers it in ruku'') — as for the second case, which is after rising, he does not repeat it by agreement. And if he delayed his saying 'and he remembers it in ruku' to connect it to it, it would be better, as stated by al-Sayyid. His statement: ('He does not repeat the ruku'') — its apparent meaning is that he is not required to repeat it; it is not prohibited because he performed something not part of the prayer. In Sharh al-Sayyid, his intended meaning of not repeating ruku' is that the validity of his prayer does not depend on repeating it, not that he is forbidden from repeating it. And what we have said is apparent. His statement: 'And delaying the obligation' is a synonymous conjunction. His statement: 'Because his occupation with that' etc. — the first case is reasoned by saying that qunoot is not time-bound in the apparent narration, so what he performed of it suffices him. His statement: 'He misses the obligation of following' — i.e., the obligatory following. It could be said in the second case that qunoot is also obligatory, so the implication is that he has a choice; rather, he claims that performing qunoot is better because he cannot make it up later, unlike ruku'.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage comprehensively covers the rulings related to forgetting the qunoot in the Witr prayer and the muqtadi's options when the imam performs qunoot. The matn states that if one forgets qunoot in the third rak'ah and remembers during ruku' or after rising from it, he does not perform qunoot — neither in that ruku' nor after — and he must perform sajda al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) to compensate for the delay. If he mistakenly performs qunoot after raising his head from ruku', he does not need to repeat the ruku', but he still performs sajda al-sahw because the qunoot was performed out of its proper place and an obligation (wajib) was delayed. The passage then addresses the muqtadi's situation: if he is reciting qunoot and the imam goes into ruku', he must follow the imam in ruku' if he fears missing it, because following the imam is an obligatory duty (wajib al-mutaba'ah). However, if he is confident he can still catch the ruku' after finishing qunoot, he should complete the qunoot to fulfill both obligations. If the imam omits the qunoot entirely, the muqtadi should perform it if he can still catch the ruku' with the imam; otherwise, he follows the imam. A final ruling: if the muqtadi joins the imam during the ruku' of the third rak'ah, he is considered to have caught the qunoot in judgment, so he does not need to recite it for the part he missed. The commentary clarifies that in the case of remembering after rising from ruku', there is agreement that qunoot is not repeated. It also explains that the phrase 'he does not repeat ruku'' means it is not obligatory to repeat, though it is not forbidden. The reasoning for not repeating qunoot in the first case is that qunoot is not time-bound in the apparent narration; what was done suffices. In the second case (where the muqtadi can choose), some argue that performing qunoot is better because it cannot be made up, unlike ruku' which can be caught.

Key Terms
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness in prayer leading to sajda al-sahw (prostration of forgetfulness) to compensate for leaving out or delaying a wajib.
مؤتم (mu'tamm): The follower in congregational prayer (muqtadi). The passage discusses his obligations regarding qunoot and following the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person performing Witr remembers that he forgot the qunoot after he has already raised his head from ruku', what should he do?
A) He should immediately go back to ruku' and then perform qunoot
B) He should perform qunoot after ruku' and then repeat the ruku'
C) He should not perform qunoot and instead perform sajda al-sahw at the end
D) He should repeat the entire rak'ah

Key Takeaway
When qunoot is forgotten in Witr, it is not made up after ruku'; sajda al-sahw suffices, and the muqtadi must balance reciting qunoot with the obligation to follow the imam.

Qunut in Witr: Follower's Recitation and Scenarios of Forgetfulness
Multiple rulings on qunut in witr with intra-Hanafi disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation during qunut in witr and apply the rules for forgetting or delaying qunut.

Core Idea
The follower remains silent during qunut in witr; forgetting qunut requires sajda al-sahw, not repetition.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi details the Hanafi rulings on qunut in witr prayer, focusing on the follower's action and various scenarios of forgetfulness and timing. It also resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding whether the follower recites qunut when the imam is silent. The relied-upon view is that the follower remains silent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling on the follower's qunut
Read the first ruling: when the imam is silent during qunut, the follower is silent. This is the most apparent view (al-azhar). Why? Because following the imam in standing is wajib.
2
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the follower recites qunut because qunut is a matter of ijtihad, like the takbirs of 'Id. Identify their dalil and the Hanafi response.
The dispute is about the nature of qunut: Is it a fixed recitation (thus follower silent) or a variable supplication (thus follower recites)?
3
Apply the rulings for forgetting qunut
If one forgets qunut and remembers during ruku' or after rising, he does not go back but performs sajda al-sahw. If he intentionally delays qunut after ruku', it is permissible but sajda al-sahw is required.
4
Determine the follower's action when imam bows early
If the imam bows before the follower finishes qunut and the follower fears missing the ruku', he must follow the imam. If he does not fear missing it, he completes qunut then bows to combine both wajibs.
5
Understand the concept of 'catching qunut'
If a latecomer catches the imam in the ruku' of the third rak'ah, he is considered to have caught the qunut in ruling and does not need to repeat it later.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في) . حال (قنوته ساكناً في الأظهر) لوجوب متابعته في القيام ولكن عندهما يقوم ساكتاً، وقال أبو يوسف : يقرؤه معه لأنه تبع للإمام، والقنوت مجتهد فيه فصار كتكبيرات العيدين والقنوت في الوتر بعد الركوع ويرسل يديه في جنبيه لأنه ذكر ليس مسنوناً (وإذا نسي القنوت في ثالثة الوتر) وتذكره في الركوع أو ) في الرفع منه أي من الركوع (لا يقنت) على الصحيح لا في الركوع الذي تذكره فيه ولا بعد الرفع منه ويسجد للسهو (ولو قنت بعد رفع رأسه من الركوع لا يعيد الركوع ويسجد للسهو لزوال القنوت عن محله الأصلي) وتأخير الواجب ولو ركع الإمام قبل فراغ المقتدي من قراءة القنوت أو قبل شروعه فيه وخاف فوت الركوع) مع الإمام (تابع إمامه لأن اشتغاله بذلك يفوت واجب المتابعة فتكون أولى وإن لم يخف فوت المشاركة في الركوع يقنت جمعاً بين الواجبين (ولو ترك الإمام القنوت يأتي به المؤتم إن أمكنه مشاركة الإمام في الركوع لجمعه بين الواجبين بحسب الإمكان (وإن كان ( لا) يمكنه المشاركة (تابعه) لأن متابعته أولى ولو أدرك الإمام في ركوع الثالثة من الوتر كان مدركاً للقنوت) حكماً فلا يأتي به فيما سبق به) كما لو قنت المسبوق ، أن لا يتحقق منه ما يفسد صلاته بناء على أنّ المعتبر رأي المقتدي وهو الصحيح الذي عليه الأكثرون، وقيل رأى الإمام وعليه الهندواني، وجماعة وقال في النهاية أنه الأقيس، وعليه فيصح الإقتداء وإن لم يحط نهر، وغيره وتظهر الثمرة فيما إذا رأى من إمامه ما يفسد الصلاة عند ذلك الإمام دون المقتدي وقد شرع في الصلاة غير عالم به تجوز صلاته على قول الأكثر لا على قول الهندواني، وفي شرح السيد وكل من القولين مرجح قوله: (والقنوت في الوتر بعد الركوع) بالجر عطفاً على تكبيرات يعني أنه يتابعه فيه، ويقرؤه لأنه مجتهد فيه فصار كتكبيرات العيدين ولهما أن قنوت الفجر منسوخ على ما تقدم فصار كما لو كبر خمساً في الجنازة فإنه لا يتابعه ويصح الإقتداء فيه بمن يراه سنة لكن بشرط أن يؤديه بتسليمة واحدة وإلا يصح على ما عليه الأكثر . قوله : على الصحيح هذا مرتبط بقوله، وتذكره في الركوع، وأما في الصورة الثانية وهي ما بعد الرفع فإنه لا يعيده إتفاقاً، ولو أخر قوله، وتذكره في الركوع ليربطه به لكان أولى أفاده السيد قوله : (لا يعيد الركوع) ظاهره أنه عليه إعادته لا يحرم لإتيانه بما ليس من الصلاة، وفي شرح السيد مراده من عدم إعادة الركوع أن صحة صلاته لا تتوقف على إعادته، وليس المراد أنه ممنوع من إعادته ،أهـ، والظاهر ما قلنا. قوله: (وتأخير الواجب) عطف مرادف. قوله: (لأن اشتغاله الخ) وتعلل المسئلة الأولى بأن القنوت ليس بمؤقت في ظاهر الرواية فما أتى به منه يكفيه قوله : ( يفوت واجب المتابعة) أي المتابعة الواجبة قد يقال في المسئلة الثانية أنّ القنوت واجب أيضاً فمقتضاه التخيير له، بل يدعي أن الإتيان بالقنوت أولى لأنه لا يمكنه تداركه بخلاف الركوع .  معه كتاب الصلاة في الثالثة أجمعوا أنه لا يقنت مرة أخرى فيما يقضيه لأنه غير مشروع وعن أبي الفضل تسويته بالشاك، وسيأتي في سجود السهو
During the state of his qunut, he is silent in the most apparent view, because of the obligation to follow him in standing. But according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), he remains silent. Abu Yusuf said: He recites it with him because he is a follower of the imam, and qunut is a matter of ijtihad, so it becomes like the takbirs of the two 'Ids. And qunut in witr is after the bowing, and he lets his hands hang by his sides because it is a remembrance that is not sunnah. And if he forgets the qunut in the third rak'ah of witr and remembers it during the bowing or during the raising from it, i.e., from the bowing, he does not perform qunut according to the correct view—neither during the bowing in which he remembered it nor after rising from it, and he performs prostrations of forgetfulness. And if he performed qunut after raising his head from bowing, he does not repeat the bowing and performs prostrations of forgetfulness because the qunut left its original place and caused delay of an obligatory act. And if the imam bows before the follower finishes reciting the qunut or before he starts it and fears missing the bowing with the imam, he follows his imam because his preoccupation with that would miss the obligatory following, so following takes precedence. And if he does not fear missing participation in the bowing, he performs qunut to combine the two obligations. And if the imam leaves the qunut, the follower performs it if he can participate with the imam in the bowing, to combine the two obligations as much as possible. And if he cannot participate, he follows him because his following is better. And if he catches the imam in the bowing of the third rak'ah of witr, he is considered to have caught the qunut in terms of ruling, so he does not perform it in what he was preceded by, just as if a latecomer performed qunut. That he is not certain of something that invalidates his prayer, based on the fact that the consideration is the view of the follower, and it is the correct view that the majority hold. And it was said: the view of the imam, and upon it is al-Hindwani and a group. And in al-Nihaya it is said that it is the stronger analogy, and upon it, following is valid even if he does not encompass. And the practical difference appears when he sees from his imam something that invalidates prayer according to that imam but not according to the follower, and he started the prayer unaware of it: his prayer is permissible according to the majority, not according to al-Hindwani. And in Sharh al-Sayyid, each of the two views is considered. His statement: 'And the qunut in witr is after the bowing'—by jar, as an apposition to 'takbirs' means that he follows him in it and recites it because it is a matter of ijtihad, so it became like the takbirs of the two 'Ids. And according to them (the two), the qunut of Fajr is abrogated as previously mentioned, so it becomes like one who said five takbirs in the funeral prayer: he does not follow him. And following is valid with one who considers it sunnah, but on condition that he performs it with one taslimah, otherwise it is not valid according to the majority. His statement: 'on the correct view' is connected to his statement 'and he remembers it during the bowing.' As for the second case, i.e., after raising, he does not repeat it by agreement. If he had delayed his statement 'and he remembers it during the bowing' to connect it to it, it would have been better. The sayyid informed us. His statement: 'he does not repeat the bowing'—apparently it is upon him to repeat it, but it is not prohibited because he performed something not part of the prayer. In Sharh al-Sayyid, his meaning of not repeating the bowing is that the validity of his prayer does not depend on its repetition; it is not meant that he is forbidden from repeating it. End. And the apparent is what we said. His statement: 'and delay of the obligatory' is a explanatory conjunction. His statement: 'because his preoccupation with that'—and he explains the first case by saying that the qunut is not time-specific in the apparent narration, so what he performed of it suffices him. His statement: 'would miss the obligatory following'—i.e., the obligatory following. It may be said in the second case that the qunut is also obligatory, so the requirement would be that he has a choice. Rather, he claims that performing the qunut is better because he cannot make it up, unlike the bowing. With it, the book of prayer: In the third, they agreed that he does not perform qunut again in what he makes up because it is not legislated. And from Abu al-Fadl, equating him with the one who doubts, and it will come in the prostrations of forgetfulness.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings about qunut in witr prayer from the Hashiya al-Tahtawi. It begins with the case of a follower reciting qunut when the imam is silent. The relied-upon position (al-azhar) is that the follower remains silent, because he must follow the imam in standing (qiyam). However, according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn), the follower should recite it, because qunut is a matter of ijtihad and thus like the takbirs of the two 'Ids. Abu Hanifa's view is the one taken. Then it states that qunut in witr is after ruku', and the follower should let his hands hang by his sides. Then it covers scenarios of forgetting qunut, doing it after ruku', the imam bowing before the follower finishes, and the follower catching the imam in ruku'. Each scenario has a ruling and a reason. The passage also discusses whose view is considered regarding invalid actions in prayer—the mature opinion is that the follower's view is considered. The practical difference appears when the imam does something invalid in his own view but not in the follower's, and the follower joined unaware: according to the majority his prayer is valid. The text ends with a note that the qunut position is after ruku', supporting the earlier ruling. Finally, it mentions that if one catches the imam in the third rak'ah's bowing, he does not repeat qunut in his makeup, and this will be discussed later in sujud al-sahw.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in witr prayer after ruku', considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
المقتدي (al-muqtadi): The follower in congregational prayer who is led by the imam.
سجود السهو (sujud al-sahw): Prostrations of forgetfulness performed to compensate for errors or omissions in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school, what should a follower do during qunut in witr if the imam is silent?
A) Recite the qunut silently.
B) Remain silent and not recite anything.
C) Recite the qunut aloud.
D) Leave the congregation.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the follower remains silent during qunut in witr, and forgetting qunut requires sajda al-sahw, not repetition.

Witr with Congregation in Ramadan: Ruling and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on witr with congregation in Ramadan and the debate over its preferability

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witr with congregation in Ramadan and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its preferability.

Core Idea
Witr with congregation is recommended only in Ramadan; the debate over its preferability shows the depth of Hanafi ijtihad.

Witr (odd-numbered prayer) holds a special place in Ramadan. Many Muslims pray it in congregation, but is that the best way? The Hanafi school has a nuanced position: congregation is mustahabb only in Ramadan, and even within the school, there is a dispute over whether congregation or solitary prayer is superior. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the tarjih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Witr with congregation is mustahabb (recommended) only in Ramadan by consensus of Muslims. Outside Ramadan, congregation in supererogatory acts is disliked (makruh).
2
Note the tada'i exception
The dislike of congregation in supererogatory prayers applies when it is organized by mutual calling (tada'i). If one or two followers join spontaneously, it is not disliked.
This distinguishes formal announcements from incidental gatherings.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Qadikhan holds that congregation in Ramadan is better; other scholars say it is better to pray alone at home. The dispute revolves around the evidence of 'Umar's practice and the fear of obligation.
4
Analyze the evidence
Qadikhan cites 'Umar leading witr and the rightly guided caliphs. Opponents cite lack of consensus among Companions and fear that congregation might lead to it being considered obligatory.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
According to al-Tahtawi, the relied-upon view is Qadikhan's because the fear of obligation is removed by restricting it to Ramadan, and the caliphs' practice is strong evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويوتر بجماعة استحباباً (في رمضان فقط) عليه إجماع المسلمين لأنه نفل من وجه والجماعة في النفل في غير التراويح مكروهة فالاحتياط تركها في الوتر خارج رمضان وعن شمس الأئمة أنّ هذا فيما كان على سبيل التداعي أما لو اقتدى واحد بواحد أو اثنان بواحد لا يكره وإذا اقتدى ثلاثة بواحد اختلف فيه وإن اقتدى أربعة بواحد كره اتفاقاً (وصلاته) أي الوتر (مع الجماعة في رمضان أفضل من أدائه منفرداً آخر الليل في اختيار قاضي قاضيخان (قال قاضيخان رحمه الله (هو الصحيح) لأنه لما جازت الجماعة كانت أفضل ولأن عمر رضي الله عنه كان يؤمهم في الوتر (وصحح غيره) أي غير قاضيخان (خلافه) قال في النهاية : بعد حكاية هذا واختار علماؤنا أن يوتر في منزله لا بجماعة لعدم اجتماع الصحابة على الوتر بجماعة في رمضان لأن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنه كان يؤمهم فيه وأبي بن كعب كان لا يؤمهم، وفي الفتح والبرهان ما يفيد أن قول قاضيخان أرجح لأنه الله أوتر بهم فيه ثم بين عذر الترك، وهو خشية أن يكتب علينا قيام رمضان، وكذا الخلفاء الراشدون صلوه بالجماعة، ومن تأخر عن الجماعة فيه أحب صلاته آخر الليل، والجماعة إذ ذاك متعذرة، فلا يدل على أن الأفضل فيه ترك الجماعة أول الليل اهـ، وإذا صلى الوتر قبل النوم، ثم تهجد لا يعيد الوتر لقوله : لا وتران في ليلة . قوله : (لأنه غير مشروع) أي الإتيان به مرة ثانية قوله : ( وعن أبي الفضل الخ) راجع إلى المصنف للإجماع على الثانية أو للثانية والرواية هذه لا تعتبر لخرقها الإجماع قوله: فالاحتياط تركها في الوتر خارج (رمضان) وما في النوازل عن المغني الإقتداء في الوتر خارج رمضان جائز فلا ينافي الكراهة لأن معناه صحيح. قوله : (أن) (هذا) أي كراهة الجماعة في النفل، أو ما في حكمه كالوتر إذا كان على سبيل التداعي أي طريق يدعو الناس للإجتماع عليهم قوله : (لا) يكره لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أم ابن عباس في صلاة الليل وكان يوقظ عائشة فتوتر معه، وصح أنه أم أنسا واليتيم، والعجوز فصلى بهم ركعتين، وكانت نافلة. قوله: (اختلف فيه والأصح عدم الكراهة. قوله : (قال) في النهاية) ومثله في الظهيرية، والذخيرة قال في النهر، وهو يقتضي أن المذهب خلاف ما في الخانية، وأنه ترجيح منه لا اختيار في المذهب اهـ . قوله: (وهو خشية أن يكتب علينا لأنه زمن تجدد الفرائض قوله : (دذاك) أي آخر الليل قوله: (لا وتران في ليلة لا عاملة عمل ليس أو عمل إن وجرى على لغة من يلزم المثنى الألف في جميع أحواله والمعنى لا يوتر لليلة ،وتران فلا ينافي أنه يقضي وترين وأكثر في ليلة والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم، وأستغفر الله العظيم.
And he performs witr with congregation as recommended (only in Ramadan) by consensus of Muslims, because it is voluntary in one aspect, and congregation in voluntary acts other than Tarawih is disliked. So precaution is to avoid it in witr outside Ramadan. And from Shams al-A'imma that this applies when it is done by mutual calling; but if one follows one, or two follow one, it is not disliked. If three follow one, there is disagreement; if four follow one, it is disliked by agreement. And his prayer, i.e., witr, with congregation in Ramadan is better than performing it alone at the end of the night according to the choice of Qadi Qadikhan. Qadikhan (may Allah have mercy on him) said: it is correct because when congregation is permitted, it is better, and because 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) used to lead them in witr. And others, i.e., other than Qadikhan, declared the opposite. In al-Nihaya: after relating this, our scholars chose that one should perform witr in his home, not with congregation, due to the lack of consensus of the Companions on witr with congregation in Ramadan, because 'Umar led them in it but Ubayy ibn Ka'b did not lead them. In al-Fath and al-Burhan, that Qadikhan's view is more likely because Allah (or he?) led them in it, then he explained the excuse for leaving it: the fear that it might be written as an obligation. Similarly, the rightly guided caliphs prayed it with congregation. And whoever delayed from congregation in it preferred his prayer at the end of the night, but congregation then is difficult, so it does not indicate that leaving congregation at the beginning of the night is better. End. And if he prays witr before sleep, then performs tahajjud, he does not repeat witr because of the saying: 'there are no two witrs in a night.' His statement: 'because it is not legislated' means performing it a second time. His statement: 'and from Abu al-Fadl' refers to the author's consensus on the second or for the second, and this narration is not considered because it breaks consensus. His statement: 'so precaution is to avoid it in witr outside Ramadan' and what is in al-Nawazil from al-Mughni: following in witr outside Ramadan is permissible, so it does not contradict the dislike because its meaning is correct. His statement: 'that this' i.e., the dislike of congregation in supererogatory prayers, or what is in its ruling like witr, if it is done by mutual calling, i.e., a way that calls people to gather for them. His statement: 'it is not disliked' because the Prophet (peace be upon him) led Ibn 'Abbas in night prayer and used to wake 'Aisha so she performed witr with him, and it is confirmed that he led Anas, the orphan, and the old woman, and prayed two rak'ahs with them, and it was supererogatory. His statement: 'there is disagreement, and the soundest is no dislike.' His statement: 'he said in al-Nihaya' and similar in al-Zahira and al-Dhakhira; he said in al-Nahr: it implies that the school is contrary to what is in al-Khaniyya, and it is his preference, not a choice in the school. End. His statement: 'and it is the fear that it might be written as an obligation because it was a time of renewed obligations.' His statement: 'that' i.e., the end of the night. His statement: 'there are no two witrs in a night' — it is a common expression, and the meaning is that one does not perform two witrs for one night, so it does not contradict that one may make up two or more witrs in a night. And Allah the Exalted knows best, and I seek forgiveness from Allah the Great.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on performing witr in congregation. It states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to pray witr with congregation in Ramadan only, by consensus of Muslims. Outside Ramadan, congregation in supererogatory prayers is disliked (makruh) except in Tarawih. Therefore, precaution is to avoid witr congregation outside Ramadan. Shams al-A'imma explains that this applies when it is organized by mutual calling; if one follower joins one imam, it is not disliked. The passage then presents a dispute: Qadikhan says that witr with congregation in Ramadan is better than praying alone at the end of the night, and this is the correct view. Others hold that it is better to pray witr at home alone, because the Companions did not all agree on congregation for witr in Ramadan. The passage favors Qadikhan's view, citing that 'Umar led them in witr and the rightly guided caliphs prayed it in congregation. The text ends with a note that if one prays witr before sleep and then stands for night prayer, he does not repeat witr because there are no two witrs in one night. The commentary further explains that congregation outside Ramadan is not absolutely disliked; it is permissible and not disliked in certain cases. The final line clarifies that the prohibition of two witrs is for the same night, not for making up missed witr.

Key Terms
الاستحباب (al-istihbab): Recommendation, a level between sunnah and mubah; performing it is rewarded, leaving it is not sinful.
التداعي (al-tada'i): Mutual calling or organizing congregation by announcement; implies formality.
المكروه (al-makruh): Disliked; here it refers to makruh tanzihan (abstention is better but not sinful).

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Throughout the year.
B) Only in Ramadan.
C) Only on Fridays.
D) Only in the last ten nights of Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
Witr with congregation is recommended only in Ramadan, and the relied-upon Hanafi view is that it is better than praying alone.

Witr in Congregation: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on witr congregation in Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi opinions on performing witr in congregation during Ramadan, identify the evidence for each, and evaluate which view is preferred (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi jurists.

Core Idea
Witr congregation in Ramadan is better per Qadikhan; solitary is better per al-Nihaya – both within the Hanafi school.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi addresses a key internal Hanafi ikhtilaf: whether it is better to pray witr in congregation during Ramadan or to pray it alone. The author presents the positions of Qadi Qadikhan and the scholars of al-Nihaya, along with their proofs, and indicates the preferred view. Understanding this dispute helps appreciate how later Hanafi masters resolve apparent contradictions within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two opinions on witr congregation
Locate in the text the statement that Qadi Qadikhan says congregation is better (afdal), and that other scholars (from al-Nihaya) say solitary prayer is better. Understand the core issue: whether witr in congregation is recommended only in Ramadan or not.
The text explicitly says: 'Wa salatuhu ma'a al-jama'ah fi Ramadan afdal min ada'ihi munfaridan' is Qadikhan's choice.
2
Examine Qadikhan's dalil
Read Qadikhan's reasoning: congregation is permitted, so it is better; and the practice of 'Umar leading witr in congregation supports it. Note that the text also mentions al-Fath and al-Burhan supporting this view.
The hadith 'La witrayn fi laylah' is about not repeating witr, not directly about congregation, but it is cited separately.
3
Examine the opposing view from al-Nihaya
The scholars of al-Nihaya argue that the Companions did not consistently gather for witr, fearing it might become obligatory. They cite Ubayy ibn Ka'b not leading the congregation for witr.
The text says 'Ubayy ibn Ka'b was not leading them' – implying he did not participate in group witr.
4
Understand the tarjih (preponderance) given by later authorities
The text notes that al-Fath and al-Burhan consider Qadikhan's view more preponderant (arjah), reasoning that the fear of obligation is no longer relevant after the Shari'ah was completed. The author of al-Nahr suggests the madhhab may be contrary to al-Khaniyya but does not override the tarjih.
The phrase 'wa fi al-Fath wa al-Burhan ma yufid anna qawl Qadikhan arjah' is the key tarjih statement.
5
Apply: practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Determine the mufta bihi: According to the preferred view, one should seek congregation for witr in Ramadan, but if one cannot, praying alone is valid. Outside Ramadan, congregation is makruh unless casual (not tada'i).
The text also discusses conditions of tada'i vs. casual following for makruh determination.

In the third [witr], they unanimously agreed that one does not recite qunut again in what he makes up, because it is not legislated. And from Abu al-Fadl is the equating it with the doubting person. It will come in Sujud al-Sahw. (And he performs witr with congregation) as a recommendation (only in Ramadan) upon which there is consensus of the Muslims, because it is nafil from one perspective, and congregation in nafil other than tarawih is makruh, so the precaution is to leave it in witr outside Ramadan. And from Shams al-A'imma that this applies when it is on the basis of mutual call (tada'i). But if one person follows one, or two follow one, it is not makruh. If three follow one, there is disagreement. If four follow one, it is makruh by agreement. (And his prayer) i.e., witr (with congregation in Ramadan is better than performing it alone at the end of the night) in the choice of Qadi Qadikhan. Qadikhan said: It is the sahih, because when congregation is permitted, it is better, and because 'Umar used to lead them in witr. (And others corrected) i.e., other than Qadikhan (his contrary view). He said in al-Nihaya: After narrating this, our scholars chose that one should pray witr at home not with congregation, because the Companions did not gather on witr in congregation, because 'Umar would lead them in it, but Ubayy ibn Ka'b would not lead them. And in al-Fath and al-Burhan, what indicates that Qadikhan's view is more preponderant, because Allah performed witr with them in it. Then he explained the excuse for leaving it: the fear that it would be prescribed upon us. Likewise, the Rightly Guided Caliphs performed it with congregation. And whoever delayed from congregation in it preferred his prayer at the end of the night, and congregation at that time is impossible, so it does not indicate that leaving congregation at the beginning of the night is better. End quote. And if one prays witr before sleeping, and then performs tahajjud, he does not repeat witr because of the hadith: 'There are not two witrs in a night.' His saying: (Because it is not legislated) i.e., performing it a second time. His saying: (And from Abu al-Fadl etc.) refers back to the author for consensus on the second, or for the second, and this narration is not considered because it breaches consensus. His saying: So precaution is to leave it in witr outside Ramadan. And what is in al-Nawazil from al-Mughni: following in witr outside Ramadan is permissible, so it does not contradict the karahah because its meaning is valid. His saying: (That) (this) i.e., the dislike of congregation in nafil or what is like it, such as witr, if it is on the basis of mutual call, i.e., a way that calls people to gather upon them. His saying: (No) dislike because the Prophet led Ibn 'Abbas in night prayer and used to wake 'Aisha and she would pray witr with him, and it is authentic that he led Anas, the orphan, and the old woman, and prayed with them two rak'ahs, and it was nafila. His saying: (It is disputed, and the most correct is no dislike). His saying: (He said in al-Nihaya) and similar in al-Zahiriyya and al-Dhakhira. He said in al-Nahr: And this implies that the madhhab is contrary to what is in al-Khaniyya, and that it is a preponderance from him, not a choice in the madhhab. End quote. His saying: (And it is the fear that it would be prescribed upon us because it was a time of descending obligations). His saying: (dhadhak) i.e., the end of the night. His saying: (No two witrs in a night) is like 'la' (not) acting like 'laysa' or acting like 'in' and it is in the language of those who make the dual with alif in all its states. The meaning: One does not perform two witrs in a night. So it does not conflict with making up two or more witrs in a night. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya discusses two interrelated rulings on witr prayer. First, regarding qunut: if one is in doubt about the number of rak'ahs in witr, he does not recite qunut again in the additional rak'ah because qunut is not legislated again. Second, the main topic is the ruling on performing witr in congregation. The text states that witr with congregation is recommended (istihbaban) only in Ramadan, based on consensus, because witr has an aspect of nafil, and congregation in nafil other than tarawih is disliked (makruh). However, the commentator Shams al-A'imma distinguishes between congregational prayer based on mutual call (tada'i) and casual following by one or two individuals. There is a detailed dispute: Qadi Qadikhan holds that witr with congregation in Ramadan is better, citing the practice of Umar and the fact that when congregation is allowed, it is better. Others, based on al-Nihaya, hold that one should pray witr at home, citing that the Companions did not consistently gather for witr, and that the fear was that it might become obligatory. The text mentions that al-Fath and al-Burhan favor Qadikhan's view. The hadith 'No two witrs in a night' is cited to show that if one prays witr before sleeping and then prays tahajjud, he does not repeat witr. The commentary then explains the meaning of 'non-legislated' and the karahah details.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): Odd-numbered prayer after 'isha, considered wajib in Hanafi school.
القنوت (al-qunut): Supplication recited in witr before or after ruku'.
التداعي (al-tada'i): Mutual call or summoning for congregation, which may be disliked in nawafil.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of giving preponderance to one legal opinion over another within the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the mufta bihi regarding witr congregation in Ramadan?
A) Congregation is better, following Qadi Qadikhan
B) Solitary is better, following al-Nihaya
C) Both views are equally valid
D) Congregation is makruh regardless

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school's preferred view is that witr congregation in Ramadan is better, based on Qadikhan's position supported by later authorities.

Nawafil and the Sunnah of Fajr in Hanafi Fiqh
Defining nawafil and sunnah, and the strongest sunnah prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define nafilah and sunnah in Hanafi terminology, explain the wisdom behind supererogatory prayers, and state the ruling of the two rak'ahs before Fajr.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are the strongest sunnah muakkadah in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Hashiya al-Tahtawi clarifies the key terms 'nafl' and 'sunnah' and highlights the elevated status of the two rak'ahs before Fajr. You will learn not only the definitions but also the deeper purposes behind supererogatory acts according to Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish nafilah from sunnah
Note that nafilah is more general: every sunnah is nafilah, but not every nafilah is sunnah. Understand the linguistic and technical definitions from the passage.
Nafilah linguistically means increase; in Shari'a it includes all voluntary worship beyond obligations, while sunnah is a recommended practice that the Prophet consistently performed.
2
Grasp the purpose of nawafil
Read the explanations of Qadi Abu Zaid (compensating deficiencies in obligations) and Qadikhan (cutting off the devil's hope). Identify how these purposes apply to prayers.
The hadith about the first deed being prayer supports the compensatory function.
3
Identify the muakkadah sunnah
The passage states that the Prophet instituted a muakkadah sunnah, and the strongest of these is the two rak'ahs before Fajr. Confirm the ruling and note the authority of Abu Hanifa.
This is the most emphasized sunnah prayer in the Hanafi school.

فصل في بيان النوافل
عبر بالنوافل دون السنن لأن النقل أعم إذ كل سنة نافلة ولا عكس والنفل لغة الزيادة وفي الشرع فعل ما ليس بفرض ولا واجب ولا مسنون من العبادة، والسنة لغة مطلق الطريقة مرضية أو غير مرضية، وفي الشريعة الطريقة المسلوكة في الدين من غير افتراض ولا وجوب، وقال القاضي أبو زيد رحمه الله : النوافل شرعت لجبر نقصان تمكن في الفرض لأن العبد وإن علت رتبته لا يخلو عن تقصير، وقال قاضيخان : السنة قبل المكتوبة شرعت لقطع طمع الشيطان فإنه يقول : من لم يطعني في ترك ما لم يكتب عليه فكيف يطيعني في ترك ما كتب عليه والسنة مندوبة ومؤكدة وبين المؤكد بقوله : (سن سنة مؤكدة) منها (ركعتان قبل صلاة الفجر) وهي أقوى السنن حتى روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه
قوله: (لأن النقل أعم والتطوّع بمعناه، وهو خير يأتي به المرء طوعاً من غير إيجاب. قوله : (لغة الزيادة) ومنه سميت الغنيمة نفلاً. قال تعالى : يسئلونك عن الأنفال) لأنها زيادة على أصل موضوع الجهاد، وهو إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى، وتطلق على ولد الولد، ومنه قوله تعالى : ووهبنا له اسحق ويعقوب نافلة ) أي عطية زائدة على ما طالبه، وهو إسحق عليهم السلام قوله : (ولا مسنون من العبادة هذا ينافي قوله إذ كل سنة نافلة فإنه ظاهر في إطلاقه عليها، ويجاب بأن للنفل إطلاقين الأول ما قابل الفرض والواجب، والثاني ما تبرع به الشخص من غير أمر به خاص، فأشار أولاً وآخراً إليهما . قوله: (والسنة الخ) الأولى ما فعله في الشرح حيث أخر الكلام على السنة عند قوله : سن الخ. قوله : (أو غير مرضية) منه ومن سن سنة سيئة فعليه ،وزرها ووزر من عمل بها إلى يوم القيامة قوله : (وفي الشريعة الطريقة الخ) تقدم الكلام عليها مستوفى في الطهارة قوله : شرعت لجبر نقصان) يمكن حمله على البعدية فلا ينافي ما بعد، أو أنها تكون لجبر النقصان، ولو كانت متقدمة، ويدل عليه ما في الحديث الصحيح: أول ما يحاسب به العبد يوم القيامة من عمله صلاته، فإن صحت فقد أصلح وأنجح، وإن فسدت فقد خاب وأجنح وخسر وإن انتقص من فريضته شيئاً. قال الرب سبحانه وتعالى : انظروا هل لعبدي من تطوع فيكمل به ما انتقص من الفريضة، ثم يكون سائر عمله على ذلك قوله : (تمكن في الفرض) أي وقع فيه قوله : (لأن العبد الخ) قال تعالى: (وما قدروا الله حق قدره [الأنعام / ٦] قال السيد عازياً إلى ما في المصنف، وهذا بالنسبة لغير الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، فإنّ النوافل في جانبهم لزيادة الدرجات لهم، وفي جانب غيرهم لجبر الخلل إذ لا خلل في صلاة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام. قوله: (منها ركعتان الأولى حذف منها لأنه على هذا الحل لا يكون لسن نائب فاعل. قوله : (وهي أقوى
Chapter on Explaining the Supererogatory Prayers. He used the term nawafil instead of sunan because nafilah is more general: every sunnah is nafilah but not the reverse. Nafilah linguistically means increase. In the Shari'a, it is an act of worship that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah. Sunnah linguistically means a way, whether good or bad. In the Shari'a, it is the path followed in the religion without obligation. Qadi Abu Zaid said: Supererogatory acts were legislated to compensate for deficiencies that occur in obligations, because the servant, even if his rank is high, is not free from shortcomings. Qadikhan said: The sunnah before the prescribed prayer was legislated to cut off the hope of the devil, for he says: 'The one who does not obey me in leaving what is not obligatory upon him, how will he obey me in leaving what is obligatory upon him?' And the sunnah is divided into mandubah and muakkadah. He explained the muakkadah by saying: 'He instituted a muakkadah sunnah, from them are two rak'ahs before the Fajr prayer.' And it is the strongest of the sunan, as narrated by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa. His saying: (Because nafilah is more general) and tatawwu' has the same meaning, and it is a good deed that a person performs voluntarily without obligation. His saying: (Linguistically: increase) hence ghanimah is called nafal. Allah says: 'They ask you about the anfal (spoils of war)' because it is an increase over the original purpose of jihad, which is to elevate the word of Allah. It is also used for grandchildren, as in His saying: 'And We bestowed upon him Ishaq and Ya'qub as nafilah (a grant)' i.e., an additional gift beyond what he asked for, which was Ishaq. His saying: (And not masnun from worship) this contradicts his saying 'every sunnah is nafilah' for it appears to be unrestricted. It is answered that nafilah has two meanings: first, what is opposed to fard and wajib; second, what a person voluntarily does without a specific command. So he indicated both meanings. His saying: (And sunnah etc.) The first thing he did in the sharh was to delay the discussion of sunnah until his saying 'sanna'. His saying: (Or not good) from it is 'and whoever sets a bad sunnah, upon him is its sin and the sin of those who act upon it until the Day of Judgment.' His saying: (In the Shari'a, the path etc.) The discussion on this has already been covered in Taharah. His saying: (Legislated to compensate for deficiency) can be carried on the post-nawafil sense so it does not conflict with what follows, or that they are for compensation even if they are prior. Evidence is the authentic hadith: 'The first of the servant's deeds for which he will be called to account on the Day of Resurrection will be his prayer. If it is sound, he will have succeeded; if it is defective, he will have failed and lost. And if something is deficient from his obligatory prayer, Allah says: Look, does My servant have any voluntary prayers to complete what is deficient from his obligatory prayer. Then the rest of his deeds will be treated similarly.' His saying: (occurs in the obligation) i.e., it fell into it. His saying: (Because the servant etc.) Allah says: 'They did not regard Allah with the regard He is due.' The commentator says, attributing to what is in the book, that this applies to non-prophets. For prophets, nawafil are for increasing ranks, while for others they are for compensating flaws, for there is no flaw in the prayers of prophets. His saying: (From them are two rak'ahs) the first word 'minha' is omitted because according to this solution, 'sanna' would not have a subject. His saying: (And it is the strongest)
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage from the hashiya explains the terminology of nawafil (supererogatory prayers) and sunnah. It begins by distinguishing nafilah from sunnah: nafilah is more general. The linguistic and legal definitions are given. Qadi Abu Zaid explains that nawafil are legislated to compensate for deficiencies in obligatory acts, because no servant is perfect. Qadikhan gives another wisdom: before the obligatory prayer, sunnah severs the devil's hope of causing neglect. The text then states that the Prophet instituted a muakkadah sunnah, and the strongest of these is the two rak'ahs before Fajr. The commentary elaborates on the meanings of nafilah and sunnah, including linguistic derivation from spoils and grandchildren. It addresses an apparent contradiction in the definition of nafilah and resolves it by noting two usages. The hadith about the first deed being prayer is cited to support the compensatory purpose of nawafil. The commentary also notes that for prophets, nawafil are for elevation rather than compensation. The passage ends mid-sentence discussing the two rak'ahs before Fajr.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Linguistically: increase; legally: an act of worship that is not fard, wajib, or sunnah.
السنة (al-sunnah): A path followed in religion without being obligatory; it is a recommended practice.
المؤكدة (al-muakkadah): A stressed sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged.
ركعتان قبل الفجر (rak'atan qabl al-fajr): The two rak'ahs of sunnah prayed before the Fajr obligatory prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) To increase the devil's frustration
B) To compensate for deficiencies in obligatory acts
C) To make the obligatory acts invalid
D) To be performed only by prophets

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs before Fajr are the strongest sunnah muakkadah, legislated to compensate for deficiencies and sever the devil's hope.

Definition of Nafl and Sunnah and the Wisdom Behind Nawafil
Defines nafl and sunnah, explains the purpose of nawafil.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of nafl and sunnah, and explain the purpose of nawafil in compensating for deficiencies in obligatory prayers.

Core Idea
Nafl includes all voluntary acts; sunnah is its subset; nawafil compensate for fard shortcomings.

This passage from the Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah clarifies two key terms—nafl and sunnah—and then reveals a profound wisdom behind voluntary prayers: they are not merely optional extras but serve to make up for any deficiencies in our obligatory acts of worship. The author supports this with a well-known hadith about the Day of Judgment and notes an important exception for prophets.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definitions of nafl
Read the first part of the passage where nafl is defined linguistically (increase) and technically (act of worship not fard, wajib, or sunnah).
Nafl is broader than sunnah.
2
Distinguish nafl from sunnah
Note the statement 'every sunnah is a nafl but not vice versa'. Understand the hierarchical relationship.
Sunnah is a specific type of nafl.
3
Extract the two wisdoms for nawafil
Find Qadi Abu Zayd's view (compensation for deficiency) and Qadikhan's view (cutting off Satan's hope).
Both purposes are mentioned in the text.
4
Examine the hadith proof
Read the hadith quoted later in the passage: voluntary prayers complete the deficient fard prayers on the Day of Judgment.
This hadith is the main evidence for the compensation purpose.
5
Note the prophetic exception
The commentary states that the compensation function applies to non-prophets; for prophets, nawafil increase their ranks.
Prophetic prayers are free from deficiency.

المكتوبة شرعت لقطع طمع الشيطان فإنه يقول : من لم يطعني في ترك ما لم يكتب عليه فكيف يطيعني في ترك ما كتب عليه والسنة مندوبة ومؤكدة وبين المؤكد بقوله : (سن سنة مؤكدة) منها (ركعتان قبل صلاة الفجر) وهي أقوى السنن حتى روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة رحمه قوله: (لأن النفل أعم والتطوّع بمعناه، وهو خير يأتي به المرء طوعاً من غير إيجاب. قوله : (لغة الزيادة) ومنه سميت الغنيمة نفلاً. قال تعالى : يسئلونك عن الأنفال) لأنها زيادة على أصل موضوع الجهاد، وهو إعلاء كلمة الله تعالى، وتطلق على ولد الولد، ومنه قوله تعالى : ووهبنا له اسحق ويعقوب نافلة ) أي عطية زائدة على ما طالبه، وهو إسحق عليهم السلام قوله : (ولا مسنون من العبادة هذا ينافي قوله إذ كل سنة نافلة فإنه ظاهر في إطلاقه عليها، ويجاب بأن للنفل إطلاقين الأول ما قابل الفرض والواجب، والثاني ما تبرع به الشخص من غير أمر به خاص، فأشار أولاً وآخراً إليهما . قوله : (والسنة الخ) الأولى ما فعله في الشرح حيث أخر الكلام على السنة عند قوله : سن الخ. قوله : (أو غير مرضية) منه ومن سن سنة سيئة فعليه وزرها ووزر من عمل بها إلى يوم القيامة قوله : (وفي الشريعة الطريقة الخ) تقدم الكلام عليها مستوفى في الطهارة قوله : شرعت لجبر نقصان) يمكن حمله على البعدية فلا ينافي ما بعد، أو أنها تكون لجبر النقصان، ولو كانت متقدمة، ويدل عليه ما في الحديث الصحيح: أول ما يحاسب به العبد يوم القيامة من عمله صلاته، فإن صحت فقد أصلح وأنجح، وإن فسدت فقد خاب وأجنح وخسر وإن انتقص من فريضته شيئاً. قال الرب سبحانه وتعالى : انظروا هل لعبدي من تطوع فيكمل به ما انتقص من الفريضة، ثم يكون سائر عمله على ذلك قوله : (تمكن في الفرض) أي وقع فيه قوله : (لأن العبد الخ) قال تعالى: (وما قدروا الله حق قدره [الأنعام / ٦] قال السيد عازياً إلى ما في المصنف، وهذا بالنسبة لغير الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام، فإنّ النوافل في جانبهم لزيادة الدرجات لهم، وفي جانب غيرهم لجبر الخلل إذ لا خلل في صلاة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام.
Section on explaining the supererogatory prayers. He used 'nawafil' instead of 'sunan' because 'nafl' is more general; every sunnah is a nafl but not vice versa. Nafl linguistically means increase, and in sacred law it is an act of worship that is not obligatory, nor incumbent, nor sunnah. Sunnah linguistically means an absolute path, whether praiseworthy or blameworthy, and in sacred law it is the path followed in religion without being obligatory or incumbent. Qadi Abu Zaid said: Nawafil were legislated to make up for deficiency that occurs in the obligatory [prayer], because the servant, even if high in rank, is not free from shortcomings. Qadikhan said: The sunnah before the prescribed prayer was legislated to cut off the hope of Satan, for he says: 'He did not obey me in abandoning what was not written upon him, so how will he obey me in abandoning what was written upon him?' The sunnah is recommended and emphasized, and he clarified the emphasized with his statement: 'He set an emphasized sunnah,' among which are two rak'ahs before the Fajr prayer, and they are the strongest of the sunnahs, as al-Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa. Then the commentator said: His statement: 'Because nafl is more general' and tatawwu' has the same meaning, it is a good deed that one performs voluntarily without obligation. His statement: 'Linguistically, increase' - from this the spoils of war are called nafal, because they are an increase over the original subject of jihad, which is exalting the word of Allah. It is also applied to the child's child, from His statement: 'And We bestowed upon him Isaac and Jacob as a nafilah (additional gift).' His statement: 'nor sunnah of worship' contradicts his statement 'every sunnah is a nafl,' for that is apparent in applying it to it. The answer is that nafl has two meanings: first, what is opposite of obligatory and incumbent; second, what one volunteers without a specific command. He indicated both initially and finally. His statement: 'and sunnah etc.' - it would have been better what he did in the Sharh, where he deferred the discussion on sunnah to his statement 'He set...'. His statement: 'or blameworthy' includes 'whoever sets an evil sunnah, upon him is its burden and the burden of those who act upon it until the Day of Judgment.' His statement: 'and in sacred law the path etc.' - the discussion on this has already been covered sufficiently in the section on purification. His statement: 'Legislated to make up for deficiency' can be interpreted as subsequent, so it does not contradict what follows, or that they are to make up for deficiency even if they are performed before, as indicated in the authentic hadith: 'The first deed of the servant that will be taken into account on the Day of Judgment is his prayer. If it is sound, he has succeeded and prospered; if it is corrupt, he has failed and lost. If there is any deficiency in his obligatory prayer, the Lord says: Look and see if My servant has any voluntary prayers to complete what is lacking of his obligatory prayer. Then the rest of his deeds will be treated similarly.' His statement: 'in the obligatory' means 'occurred in it.' His statement: 'because the servant etc.' - the Exalted said: 'They have not appraised Allah with true appraisal.' The master, attributing to what is in the book, said this applies to other than the prophets, for nawafil for them are to increase ranks, and for others to compensate for flaws, since there is no flaw in the prayers of the prophets.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and wisdom-oriented section from the Hashiya on Maraqi al-Falah. It opens by distinguishing between 'nafl' and 'sunnah', explaining that 'nafl' is a broader term encompassing all voluntary acts, while 'sunnah' refers specifically to a path followed in religion without being obligatory. The author then cites two scholarly opinions on the purpose of nawafil: Qadi Abu Zayd states they compensate for deficiencies in the obligatory prayers, while Qadikhan says the sunnah before the fard cuts off Satan's hope that the worshipper will neglect the fard. The commentator supports the compensation view with a hadith from the Prophet (peace be upon him) about the Day of Judgment, where voluntary prayers are used to make up for any shortcomings in the fard prayers. Importantly, the commentator notes that this compensatory function applies only to non-prophets, as the prayers of prophets are free from deficiency; for them, nawafil increase their ranks. This passage establishes the foundational understanding of voluntary prayers in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
النفل (al-nafl): Linguistically means increase; in sacred law, an act of worship that is not obligatory (fard) nor incumbent (wajib) nor sunnah; it is broader than sunnah (every sunnah is nafl but not vice versa).
السنة (al-sunnah): In sacred law, a path followed in religion without being obligatory or incumbent; includes both emphasized (muakkadah) and non-emphasized sunnahs.
التطوع (al-tatawwu'): A good deed performed voluntarily without obligation; synonymous with nafl in this context.
جبر النقصان (jabr al-nuqsān): Compensation for deficiency; nawafil are meant to make up for shortcomings in the obligatory prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary purpose of nawafil according to the text?
A) To increase reward only
B) To compensate for deficiencies in fard prayers
C) To cut off Satan's hope
D) Both B and C

Key Takeaway
Nawafil are legislated primarily to compensate for deficiencies in obligatory prayers, as supported by the hadith and scholarly statements.

The Sunnah of Fajr: Virtue, Ruling, and Dispute on Most Afdal Sunnah
Discusses the Fajr sunnah's superiority, its ruling as wajib or not, and ranks sunnahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi mufta bihi ruling on the Fajr sunnah and explain the evidence for it being sunnah muakkadah, and identify the most virtuous sunnah after Fajr according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is the most virtuous sunnah, yet its ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.

This passage from Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on Maraqi al-Falah delves into the unique status of the Fajr sunnah. It addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether this sunnah is wajib or emphatically recommended, and then explores a ranking of other sunnah prayers. The discussion illustrates how Hanafi scholars weigh hadith evidence and practice to determine the most virtuous optional prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Fajr sunnah's ruling
Note the two views: a report from Abu Hanifa that it is wajib, and the majority view that it is sunnah muakkadah. Determine which is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position.
The commentator questions the consensus claim for wujub.
2
Examine the evidence for sunnah muakkadah
The permissibility of praying Fajr sunnah sitting without excuse is used as evidence against wujub. Also, the text mentions that the consensus is on emphasis, not obligation.
The mu'tamad is that it is sunnah muakkadah.
3
Explore the dispute on the next most virtuous sunnah
List the opinions: Al-Halwani (Maghrib sunnah), the equal view, and the view that the four before Dhuhr are most emphasized.
Al-Hasan and later scholars prefer the four before Dhuhr.
4
Apply the tarjih for the four before Dhuhr
The hadith threat ('Whoever leaves the four before Dhuhr, my intercession will not reach him') is the key evidence. Note that beginning with them in al-Mabsut is not evidence of superiority.
This is the al-ashahh view.

Source Text

قوله: (منها ركعتان الأولى حذف منها لأنه على هذا الحل لا يكون لسن نائب فاعل. قوله : (وهي أقوى الله تعالى : لو صلاها قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز وروى المرغيناني عن أبي حنيفة رحمه الله أنها واجبة، وقال : لا تدعوهما وإن طردتكم الخيل وقال : ركعتا الفجر أحب إلي من الدنيا وما فيها وفي لفظ : خير من الدنيا وما فيها، ثم اختلف في الأفضل بعد ركعتي سنة الفجر قال :الحلواني ركعتا المغرب، ثم التي بعد الظهر ثم التي بعد العشاء ثم التي قبل الظهر ثم التي قبل العصر ثم التي قبل العشاء، وقيل التي بعد العشاء والتي قبل الظهر وبعده وبعد المغرب كلها سواء وقيل التي قبل الظهر أكد قال الحسن وهو الأصح وقد ابتدأ في المبسوط بها قوله: (فاتت السنن) لكثرة ما ورد فيها من المرغبات قوله : (أنها واجبة) أجمعوا على أنها لا تصح قاعداً من غير عذر كما في الخلاصة، ويخشى على جاحدها الكفر كما في المضمرات، وتقضى إذا مع الفرض دون غيرها، والأصح أنها تصاب بمطلق النية وفي مسلم عن أبي هريرة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قرأ في ركعتي الفجر قل يا أيها الكافرون) وقل هو الله أحد) وفي مسند الإمام أحمد ابن عباس في الأولى بخاتمة البقرة، وفي الثانية قل يا أهل الكتاب تعالوا الآية فتستحب قراءة هاتين السورتين، وهذه الآيات على سبيل المناوبة أياماً، واستحسن الغزالي أن يقرأ في الأولى ألم نشرح وفي الثانية ألم تر كيف وقال: إنّ ذلك يردّ شر اليوم كذا في ابن أمير حاج لكنه لم يرد في السنة كما في مقاصد السخاوي، والأفضل في سنة الفجر أداؤها في أول الوقت مع التخفيف ، وقيل : يفضل الأسفار وفي البناية عن المبسوط : يكره الكلام بعد إنشقاق الفجر لأنها ساعة تشهدها ملائكة الليل وملائكة النهار كما في تأويل إن قرآن الفجر كان مشهوداً فلا ينبغي أن يشهدهم إلا على خير، وفي حكاية الإجماع على أنها لا تصلي من قعود نظر، بل المجمع عليه إنما هو تأكدها، والمعتمد جوازها من قعود كما يأتي في الشرح. قوله : (وإن طردتكم الخيل المقصود الحث على الفعل، وإلا فترك الفرد عند طرد الخيل يباح لعدم التمكن قوله : ( أحب إلي من الدنيا وما فيها باعتبار ما يترتب على فعلها من الثواب . قوله : (ثم اختلف في الأفضل أي من المؤكدات والمستحبات . : ، قوله: (قال الحلواني ركعتا المغرب) فإنه لم يدعهما سفراً، ولا حضراً كذا في الشرح قوله : (ثم التي بعد الظهر لأنها سنة متفق عليها بخلاف التي قبلها لأنه قيل أنها للفصل بين الأذان والإقامة كذا في الشرح. قوله : (وهو الأصح) كذا صححه في الدراية، والعناية والنهاية وعلله في البحر بأنه ورد فيها، وعيد هو قوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من ترك الأربع التي قبل الظهر لم تنله شفاعتي وكذا ذكر تصححه العلامة نوح قوله : (وقد ابتدأ) أي الإمام محمد في المبسوط بها، وهو لا يدل على أفضليتها لأنّ الظهر أول صلاة في الوجود.
His statement: 'Among them are two rak'ahs' – 'the first' is omitted because in this construction 'sunnah' does not have a clear agent. His statement: 'and they are the strongest' – Allah says: If he prays them sitting without excuse, it is not permissible. Al-Marghinani narrated from Abu Hanifa that they are obligatory. He said: Do not leave them even if horses chase you. He said: The two rak'ahs of Fajr are more beloved to me than the world and what is in it; in another wording: better than the world and what is in it. Then there is disagreement about the most virtuous after the two rak'ahs of Fajr sunnah. Al-Halwani said: the two rak'ahs of Maghrib, then after Dhuhr, then after Isha, then before Dhuhr, then before Asr, then before Isha. And it is said that after Isha and before and after Dhuhr and after Maghrib are all equal. And it is said that before Dhuhr is more emphasized; al-Hasan said this is the most correct, and Imam Muhammad began with them in al-Mabsut. His statement: 'the sunnahs have passed' due to the many encouragements reported concerning them. His statement: 'that they are obligatory' – they have agreed that they are not valid sitting without excuse as in al-Khulasa, and one who denies them fears disbelief as in al-Mudmarat, and they are made up if missed along with the fard unlike others. The most correct is that they are intended by absolute intention. In Muslim from Abu Huraira that the Prophet recited in the two rak'ahs of Fajr 'Say: O disbelievers' and 'Say: He is Allah, the One'. In the Musnad of Imam Ahmad from Ibn 'Abbas that in the first he recited the end of Surat al-Baqara and in the second 'Say: O People of the Scripture, come to a word...' So it is recommended to recite these two surahs, and these verses on a rotating basis daily. Al-Ghazali considered it good to recite in the first 'Have We not opened' and in the second 'Have you not seen', saying that this repels the evil of the day, as in Ibn Amir Haj, but it is not reported in the sunnah as in Maqasid al-Sakhawi. The best for the Fajr sunnah is to perform it at the beginning of the time with brevity, and it is said that making it later is better. In al-Binaya from al-Mabsut: It is disliked to speak after the break of dawn because it is an hour witnessed by the angels of the night and the angels of the day, so one should not have them witness except good. The claim of consensus that it cannot be prayed sitting is questionable; rather the consensus is on its emphasis, and the relied-upon position is that it is permissible to pray it sitting, as will come in the Sharh. His statement: 'even if horses chase you' is intended to urge action; otherwise, leaving the individual [prayer] when horses chase is permitted due to inability. His statement: 'more beloved to me than the world and what is in it' is with regard to the reward resulting from performing it. His statement: 'then they differed about the most virtuous' i.e., among the emphasized and recommended [sunnahs]. His statement: 'Al-Halwani said: the two rak'ahs of Maghrib' – for he did not leave them in travel or residence, as in the Sharh. His statement: 'then after Dhuhr' because it is a sunnah agreed upon, unlike the one before it, for it is said that it is for separation between the adhan and iqama. His statement: 'and it is the most correct' – thus it is corrected in al-Diraya, al-Inaya, and al-Nihaya, and he gave the reason in al-Bahr because a threat is reported concerning it: 'Whoever leaves the four before Dhuhr, my intercession will not reach him.' Similarly, it is authenticated by Allama Nuh. His statement: 'and he began' i.e., Imam Muhammad in al-Mabsut with them, and this does not indicate their superiority because Dhuhr is the first prayer in existence.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage focuses on the sunnah of Fajr. It begins by affirming that the two rak'ahs before Fajr are the strongest of the sunnah prayers, so much so that a report from Abu Hanifa (through al-Marghinani) deems them obligatory (wajib). However, the commentator clarifies that the consensus is on their emphasis, not obligation, and the relied-upon position is that they are an emphasized sunnah (sunnah muakkadah). The text details their virtues: they are more beloved than the entire world, and they are not left even in times of danger. It then discusses the recommended recitations (Surat al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas, or other options) and the best time to perform them (early with brevity, though some prefer delay). The passage also addresses the ruling on praying them sitting: it is permissible albeit with a difference of opinion. Finally, it enters a intra-Hanafi dispute about which sunnah is most virtuous after the Fajr sunnah. Several opinions are cited: Al-Halwani ranks Maghrib sunnah highest, then after Dhuhr, etc.; others say they are equal; still others hold that the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr are most emphasized. The commentator states that the most correct view (al-ashahh) is that the four before Dhuhr are most emphasized, citing a hadith about the Prophet's threat to those who neglect them. However, he notes that Imam Muhammad beginning with them in al-Mabsut was not due to superiority but because Dhuhr was the first prayer prescribed.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah muakkadah): Emphasized sunnah; acts that the Prophet consistently performed and recommended strongly, but are not wajib. Their omission is disliked but does not incur sin.
أفضلية النوافل (afdaliyyat al-nawafil): The ranking of voluntary prayers in terms of virtue; after the Fajr sunnah, the four before Dhuhr are considered most virtuous.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Maghrib sunnah
B) Four before Dhuhr
C) After Dhuhr
D) All equal

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is the strongest sunnah but not wajib; after it, the most emphasized sunnah is the four rak'ahs before Dhuhr.

Sunnah of Dhuhr: Two Rak'ahs After Dhuhr and Recommendation of Adding Two More
States the sunnah of Dhuhr and the recommendation to add two rak'ahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the two rak'ahs after Dhuhr, distinguish between sunnah muakkadah and mustahab, and identify the preferred method of performing the additional two rak'ahs.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after Dhuhr are sunnah muakkadah; adding two more is mustahab, preferably with one taslim.

In this short passage, the Hanafi jurist clarifies the sunnah prayers associated with Dhuhr. While the default is two rak'ahs after Dhuhr (part of the rawatib), it is recommended to add an additional two rak'ahs, making four in total. The worshipper has a choice in how to perform them, but the preferred method is to pray all four with a single taslim, as a four-rak'ah unit. Understanding this distinction helps you correctly categorise the ruling and practice of these voluntary prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that among the sunnah prayers are 'two rak'ahs after Dhuhr'. Identify that this is a sunnah muakkadah (emphasised sunnah) from the rawatib.
The term 'sunnah' here implies sunnah muakkadah, as per Hanafi classification.
2
Distinguish the additional two rak'ahs
The phrase 'yundab an yadumma ilayhimā rak'atayn' indicates that adding two more is recommended (mustahab), not at the level of sunnah muakkadah.
The word 'yundab' (it is recommended) is a lower category than 'sunnah' in Hanafi terminology.
3
Note the options for performance
The worshipper may pray the four rak'ahs with one taslim (i.e., as a four-rak'ah unit) or with two taslims (two separate two-rak'ah units). The text says 'wa al-úlā' (the first is better), meaning one taslim is preferred.
This choice only applies if one chooses to add the extra two; the basic sunnah of two rak'ahs is always performed with one taslim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و) منها (ركعتان بعد الظهر ويندب أن يضم إليهما ركعتين) قوله: (ويندب أن يضم إليهما ركعتين) وهو مخير إن شاء جعلها بسلام واحد، وإن شاء جعلها بسلامين، والأولى
And among them are two rak'ahs after Dhuhr, and it is recommended to add two more to them. His statement: 'and it is recommended to add two more to them' – he has the choice: if he wishes, he makes them with one taslim, and if he wishes, he makes them with two taslims, and the first is better.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This short passage states a clear ruling: among the sunnah prayers are two rak'ahs after the Dhuhr prayer. Additionally, it is recommended (yundab) to add two more rak'ahs, making a total of four after Dhuhr. The commentator clarifies that the worshipper has a choice: he may pray all four with a single taslim (i.e., a four-rak'ah unit) or with two taslims (i.e., two separate two-rak'ah units). The preferred option (al-ula) is to pray them with one taslim. This ruling is part of the Hanafi enumeration of sunnah prayers associated with the five daily prayers.

Key Terms
ركعتان بعد الظهر (rak'atān ba'da al-zuhr): Two rak'ahs performed after the Dhuhr prayer, considered sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
يندب (yundab): It is recommended (mandub); a level below sunnah muakkadah, indicating a desirable act without strong emphasis.
تسليمة واحدة (taslimah wāhidah): One greeting of peace at the end of the prayer; performing four rak'ahs with one taslim means praying them as one unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the preferred way to perform the four rak'ahs after Dhuhr?
A) With two separate taslims
B) With one taslim
C) Only two rak'ahs without adding more
D) It is disliked to add more

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school establishes two rak'ahs after Dhuhr as sunnah muakkadah, and recommends adding two more, preferably with one taslim.
